801 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Clephane v. State


No. 55A01-9905-CR-145


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


719 N.E.2d 840; 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 2008



November 19, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MORGAN SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Christopher L. Burnham, Judge. Cause No. 55D02-9802-CF-31.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his convictions of Sexual Misconduct with a Minor and Contributing to the Delinquency of a Minor received in the Morgan Superior Court (Indiana).


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his convictions of Sexual Misconduct with a Minor and Contributing to the Delinquency of a Minor. Appellant claimed that his statements to a social worker should have been suppressed at trial because they amounted to an involuntary confession in violation of U.S. Const. amend. V; Ind. Const. art. I, § 14; and his Miranda rights. The court held that the admission of appellant's statements into evidence was constitutional. The social worker was an agent of the government in the course of securing a conviction, but appellant's statements to her were voluntary. Similarly, there was no problem with the lack of Miranda warnings before appellant made his statements because appellant was not in custody (though he was subject to interrogation). Appellant testified that he knew he was "free to leave" the interview with the social worker. The court affirmed appellant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction because statements made to a social worker were not an unconstitutional confession and were admissible as evidence. The statements were voluntary and appellant was not in custody when he made them (he was free to leave).

 

802 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. State


No. 49A02-9901-JV-15


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


719 N.E.2d 445; 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 1998



November 17, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable James W. Payne, Judge. Cause No. 49D09-9809-JD-4702 & 49D09-9709-JD-3614.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the decision of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which adjudicated defendant as a delinquent child based upon disorderly conduct, a Class B misdemeanor when committed by an adult.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's mother called the police during an argument between defendant and his mother. Defendant argued with the police officer and his mother, speaking in a voice louder than everyone else did. Defendant was arrested and was adjudicated as a delinquent child based upon disorderly conduct. Defendant appealed. The court affirmed the adjudication. The evidence was sufficient to support a finding of disorderly conduct, because defendant's loud manner of speaking disrupted a police investigation. Defendant's adjudication did not contravene Ind. Const. art. 1, § 9, because defendant did not establish that his comments were political and the State could have rationally concluded that defendant's conduct constituted an abuse of the right to speak, and thus, fell within the State's police power.


OUTCOME: Decision adjudicating defendant as a delinquent child was affirmed, because the evidence was sufficient to support a finding of disorderly conduct and defendant's adjudication was not unconstitutional.

 

803 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Mahowald v. State


No. 49A02-9808-CV-693


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


719 N.E.2d 421; 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 1996; 23 Employee Benefits Cas. (BNA) 2260



November 16, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. ROOM NO. 11. The Honorable John L. Price, Judge. Cause No. 49D11-9712-CP-1772.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed the Marion Superior Court's (Indiana) grant of summary judgment in favor of defendant in an action challenging the constitutionality of the Legislators' Retirement System, Ind. Code §§ 2-3.5-4-1 - 2-3.5-4-10, under Ind. Const. art. I, § 23.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, a retired state legislator, brought an action challenging the constitutionality of the Indiana Legislators' Retirement System, Ind. Code §§ 2-3.5-4-1 - 2-3.5-4-10, under Ind. Const. art. I, § 23. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of defendant State. On appeal, the issue was whether the trial court erred in determining that the retirement system was constitutional. The statute granted unequal privileges to different members of the legislature, but the date of service classification legitimately distinguished between retired legislators and current and future legislators. This distinction represented a reasonable exercise of legislative line drawing. Plaintiff failed to overcome the presumption of constitutionality and failed to negate every conceivable basis that might have supported the classification. Consequently, the trial court properly granted defendant's motion for summary judgment.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment affirmed because plaintiff failed to overcome the presumption of constitutionality and failed to negate every conceivable basis that might have supported the classification.

 

804 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Town of Avon v. Harville


No. 32A01-9902-CV-39


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


718 N.E.2d 1194; 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 1970



November 9, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 21, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 2395.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE HENDRICKS CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Jeffrey V. Boles, Judge. Cause No. 32C01-9802-CP-62.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant municipality appealed the judgment of the Hendricks Circuit Court (Indiana), which found that appellant's enforcement of Avon, Ind., Zoning Ordinances ch. 4, § 4-6(1) against appellee's real estate violated appellee's rights under U.S. Const. amend. V and granted an injunction against enforcement of the ordinance against him.


OVERVIEW: Appellee, a landowner who operated a salvage recycling business on his property, received a judgment in his favor which enjoined appellant municipality from enforcing its new ordinance, Avon, Ind., Zoning Ordinances ch. 4, § 4-6(1), against him because it would violated his rights under U.S. Const. amend. V. The court found that appellee had never met his burden of proving that, at the time the ordinance was adopted, he had used his property in a manner amounting to a lawful nonconforming use. In the event that the case required further proceedings, the court noted that appellant was not precluded from adopting an amortization provision in its zoning ordinance should it choose to do so. The judgment was therefore reversed.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed on the grounds that appellee failed to meet his burden of proving that he used his property in the manner of a lawful nonconforming use when the ordinance was adopted.

 

805 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. State


No. 44A03-9901-CR-19


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


717 N.E.2d 1277; 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 1922



October 29, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAGRANGE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable George E. Brown, Judge. Cause No. 44D01-9711-CV-58.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the LaGrange Superior Court (Indiana), which convicted him of armed robbery under Ind. Code § 35-42-5-1 and two counts of criminal confinement under Ind. Code § 35-42-3-3, and sentenced him as a habitual offender under Ind. Code § 35-50-2-8.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted in trial court of armed robbery under Ind. Code § 35-42-5-1, two counts of criminal confinement under Ind. Code § 35-42-3-3, and sentenced as a habitual offender under Ind. Code § 35-50-2-8. Defendant appealed, claiming that the convictions violated his right against double jeopardy; that the state failed to present sufficient evidence that he was an habitual offender; and that his sentence violated Ind. Const. art. 1, § 16. The court affirmed, holding that defendant's convictions did not violate his right against double jeopardy, because both the robbery charge and the confinement charges contained at least one separate and distinct element; past offense evidence presented by the state was sufficient to establish that he was a habitual offender; and his sentence was proportionate to the nature of his offenses.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed. They were not violative of defendant's double-jeopardy rights because each offense contained distinct elements. Past offense evidence presented by the state was sufficient to establish that defendant was a habitual offender. Defendant's sentence was proportionate to the nature of his offenses.

M.S. v. Eagle-Union Community Sch. Corp.


No. 06A04-9806-CV-291


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


717 N.E.2d 1255; 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 1887



October 28, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 3, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 2402.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE BOONE SUPERIOR COURT II. The Honorable James R. Detamore, Judge. Cause No. 06D02-9706-CP-31.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner student appealed the judgment of the Boone Superior Court II (Indiana), granting respondent schools' motion for summary judgment in an action for review of a student disciplinary decision taken against petitioner by respondent school.


OVERVIEW: After petitioner student was tardy six times, respondent school withdrew petitioner from geometry and deleted the class from petitioner's record. The local school board affirmed. Petitioner appealed the school board's decision to the trial court. The trial court denied petitioner's summary judgment motion and granted summary judgment in favor of respondent. On appeal, petitioner argued the trial court erred by upholding respondent's disciplinary policies against petitioner's challenge to the validity of those policies and against petitioner's challenge that the action violated his procedural due process rights; denying petitioner's motion for a change of venue; and granting respondent summary judgment. Petitioner also argued that the judicial review section of the Indiana Student Discipline Act (Act) was unconstitutional. The court found that respondent's disciplinary action did not violate the Act and found no ground for reversal of the trial court's judgment. The judicial review section of the Act was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment affirmed because the school's disciplinary policy did not conflict with the Indiana Student Discipline Act, and there was no ground for reversal of the trial court's summary judgment upholding the policy.

 

807 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Mendenhall v. City of Indianapolis


No. 49A04-9901-CV-1


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


717 N.E.2d 1218; 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 1827



October 12, 1999, Decided  
October 12, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Kenneth H. Johnson, Judge. Cause No. 49D02-9801-CP-134.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners appealed the Marion Superior Court's (Indiana) entry of summary judgment in favor of defendants city and county and its denial of plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment on plaintiffs' complaint for damages for inverse condemnation.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff landowners brought inverse condemnation action against defendants city and county to recover damages suffered after the prosecutor obtained a seizure order against the plaintiffs' property based on its use as an adult bookstore, which displayed obscene material. All parties moved for summary judgment. The denial of plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment and the granting of defendants' motion for summary judgment were affirmed because collateral estoppel barred the subsequent litigation of the issue that the prosecutor was an agent of the state and acted on behalf of the state and not on behalf of defendants. Also, judicial immunity extended to the local police because they were enforcing the court-ordered seizure. Thus, judicial immunity barred liability against the police and all other actors involved in the seizure.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed because defendant's actions were so integral with the judicial process that it was considered an arm of the judicial officer and judicial immunity applied, and because the actions of which plaintiffs' complained were undertaken by the state and not by defendants.

 

808 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Washington


No. 49A04-9808-CV-398


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


716 N.E.2d 607; 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 1696



September 28, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition to Transfer Granted September 1, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Ind. LEXIS 711.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. CIVIL DIVISION. The Honorable Kenneth Johnson, Judge. Cause No. 49D02-9503-CT-459.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part, affirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed the court's reduction of the damages award by 50 percent and defendant cross-appealed the judgment entered for plaintiff from the Marion Superior Court, Civil Division (Indiana).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff sued defendant ophthalmologist for failure to advise of the type and risk and benefits of surgery, which prevented plaintiff from pursuing surgery and led to further deterioration of his eye from glaucoma and eventual removal. The trial court found that absent defendant's negligence, plaintiff had a 50 percent chance of retaining vision in his eye and awarded damages reduced by 50 percent. Plaintiff appealed the reduction of the award and defendant cross-appealed. The court reversed in part, finding that the trial court erred in reducing the award because under the increased risk of harm rule, applicable to causation, a plaintiff recovers for the harm suffered, not for the loss of the chance of recovery; and the court affirmed in part, in finding that the trial court did not err in concluding that the case was timely filed, in denying defendant's belated request for a jury trial, and in finding that plaintiff was not contributorily negligent.


OUTCOME: The reduction of the award was reversed and remanded because the increased risk of harm rule, applicable to causation, did not limit recovery. Judgment otherwise was affirmed because the trial court did not err in concluding that it was timely filed, in denying the late request for a jury trial, and in finding plaintiff was not contributorily negligent.

Hoehn v. Hoehn


No. 10A01-9812-CV-473


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


716 N.E.2d 479; 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 1492



September 17, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE CLARK SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Jerome F. Jacobi, Judge. Cause No. 10D01-8711-DR-503.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, vacated in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a Clark Superior Court (Indiana) judgment declaring that Indiana law applied to the parties' dispute, modifying his child support obligation and awarding back child support, awarding attorney's fees to appellee and ordering appellant stop his Georgia litigation.


OVERVIEW: Appellant husband challenged a judgment applying Indiana law to the dispute, modifying appellant's child support obligation, awarding attorney's fees to appellee wife and ordering appellant stop his Georgia litigation. The court affirmed in part, vacated in part and remanded for recalculation of the support obligation. Under Ind. Code § 31-18-6-12(d), part of the Uniform Interstate Family Support Act (UIFSA), Ind. Code §§ 31-18-1-1 to 31-18-9-3, the court had continuing, exclusive jurisdiction because appellant previously sought relief in Indiana court at least three times. Consequently, Indiana law also applied to extend the child support duration.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part, vacated in part and remanded for recalculation of the support obligation; Indiana had jurisdiction because appellant previously submitted to jurisdiction the calculation of appellant's income and extending appellant's support obligation beyond 18 was not erroneous.

Boggs v. Tri-State Radiology, Inc.


No. 82A04-9809-CV-450


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


716 N.E.2d 45; 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 1473



September 7, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE VANDERBURGH SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Terry D. Dietsch, Judge. Cause No. 82D03-9710-CP-3553.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant-plaintiff, individually and on behalf of his wife, appealed the judgment of the Vanderburgh Superior Court (Indiana), which dismissed his medical malpractice claim against appellee-defendant.


OVERVIEW: The trial court dismissed appellant-plaintiff's medical malpractice claim against appellee-defendant. Appellant-plaintiff, individually and on behalf of his wife, appealed. The issue before the court, was whether plaintiffs who discovered the malpractice during the occurrence-based statute of limitations, Ind. Code § 34-18-7-1(b) (1998), but filed their claim after the same expired could bring their action within two years of discovering the malpractice. The occurrence-based statute of limitations was unconstitutional as applied to plaintiff pursuant to Ind. Const. art. I, § 23. Plaintiff filed his complaint less than two years from either date, and therefore, he filed his complaint in accordance with the medical malpractice statute of limitations as construed by the court.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and remanded; the medical malpractice occurrence-based statute of limitations was unconstitutional as applied to plaintiff. Plaintiff filed his complaint in accordance with the medical malpractice statute of limitations as construed by the court.

United States Outdoor Adver. Co. v. Indiana DOT


No. 49A02-9803-CV-276


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


714 N.E.2d 1244; 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 1419



August 20, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by U. S. Outdoor Adver. Co. v. Indiana DOT, 735 N.E.2d 221, 2000 Ind. LEXIS 83 (Ind., 2000)
Later proceeding at Ind. Dep't of Transp. v. United States Outdoor Adver. Co., 882 N.E.2d 295, 2008 Ind. App. LEXIS 505 (Ind. Ct. App., 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable John L. Price, Judge. Cause No. 49D11-9612-CP-1716.



DISPOSITION: Cause remanded to the department for additional factual findings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant billboard company sought review of a Marion County Superior Court (Indiana) decision that affirmed appellee Department of Transportation's denial of appellant's billboard sign applications.


OVERVIEW: Appellant billboard company submitted applications to appellee Department of Transportation for two sign permits for legal, nonconforming billboards. Appellee denied the applications, the trial court affirmed the denial, and appellant sought review. It argued that appellee erroneously denied the permits, that appellee was estopped from denying the application, that the denial violated due process and appellant's rights to free speech and equal protection, and that the denial was an unconstitutional taking. The court remanded for a determination of whether the signs were in residential or business zones, because if the signs were in residential zones, they would be ineligible for permits. The court further found that appellee was equitably estopped from denying the application and that the appellant failed to show that it was denied due process. The court also found that the Indiana Billboard Act, Ind. Code §§ 8-23-20-1 to -26, was constitutional because it did not distinguish between signs based on content. The court found that the taking issue was not properly before it because the billboards were still standing and a takings claim could only be made after the signs were removed.


OUTCOME: The court remanded appellant's billboard permit request for further fact-finding to determine whether the signs were located in either residential or zoned or unzoned commercial areas. The court noted that if the signs were in residential zones, the signs would be ineligible for permits.

State v. Bailey


No. 56A03-9807-CR-311


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


714 N.E.2d 1144; 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 1206



July 22, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE NEWTON SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Daniel J. Molter, Judge. Cause No. 56D01-9703-CF-11.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the Newton Superior Court (Indiana), denying appellant's motion to correct errors after it denied appellant's motion to quash appellee's deposition subpoenas under Ind. Code § 33-19-1-5. Appellee cross-appealed for attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: Appellant's employees were witnesses for the prosecution in appellee's prosecution for child molestation. Appellee served deposition subpoenas on employees. Appellant insisted that employees be compensated by a minimum amount and additional hourly fees. Appellee claimed employees were only entitled to general compensation under Ind. Code § 33-19-1-5.Appellant moved to quash the deposition subpoenas. The trial court denied appellant's motion and ordered that employees be deposed at standard witness fees. After the depositions took place, appellant moved to correct errors. The trial court denied the motion. Appellant sought review, claiming employees were entitled to additional fees, and appellee's counsel exceeded the intended scope of the depositions. Appellee cross-appealed for attorney fees. The court affirmed because the trial court did not abuse its discretion, and appellee's counsel did not exceed the intended scope of the depositions. The court also denied appellee's request for attorney fees because the appeal had sufficient merit.


OUTCOME: Denial of appellant's motion to correct errors was affirmed because the trial court did not abuse its discretion, and appellee's counsel did not exceed the intended scope of the depositions. Appellee's request for attorney fees was denied because the appeal was not meritless.

Myers v. State


No. 64A03-9808-CR-349


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


714 N.E.2d 276; 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 1209



July 22, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Counsel Amended August 18, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE PORTER SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Nancy H. Vaidik, Judge. Cause No. 64D04-9610-CM-1387.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Under Ind. Code § 20-12-3.5-1 and the Establishment Clause, U.S. Const. amend. I, appellant driver sought review of the decision of the Porter Superior Court (Indiana), convicting appellant of driving while intoxicated as a Class A misdemeanor after denying appellant's motion to suppress the evidence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant driver was stopped by a campus police officer for a church-related university after officer observed appellant's truck driving over the center line. Appellant's eyes were glassy and bloodshot, his breath smelled of alcohol, and he admitted to consuming alcohol. Appellant's chemical breath test was .16 percent. At trial, appellant moved to suppress the evidence. The trial court denied the motion. Appellant was convicted of driving while intoxicated as a Class A misdemeanor. Appellant sought review, claiming Ind. Code § 20-12-3.5-1 violated the Establishment Clause, U.S. Const. amend. I, that university police officers were required to complete training by the Indiana Law Enforcement Academy, and officer lacked reasonable suspicion. The court affirmed because § 20-12-3.5-1 did not violate the Establishment Clause, university police officers were not required to complete training conducted by the Indiana Law Enforcement Academy, and officer had reasonable suspicion to initiate a traffic stop.


OUTCOME: Appellant driver's conviction of driving while intoxicated was affirmed because officer had reasonable suspicion to initiate a traffic stop, the statute allowing creation of university police forces did not violate the applicable clause of constitutional amendment, and university police officers were not required to complete training conducted by the Indiana Law Enforcement Academy.

 

814 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Borgman v. State Farm Ins. Co.


No. 30A04-9810-CV-515


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


713 N.E.2d 851; 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 924



June 9, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE HANCOCK SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Richard T. Payne, Judge. Cause No. 30D01-9807-CT-230.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an injured employee and her husband, appealed the judgment of the Hancock Superior Court (Indiana) that dismissed their complaint against defendant insurer and defendant employer for wrongful denial of plaintiff employee's request for worker's compensation benefits. The trial court determined that it lacked subject matter jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff employee worked for defendant employer, an animal hospital. Plaintiff employee fell in a kennel and injured her arm and neck. Defendant insurer, which was defendant employer's worker's compensation carrier, paid for plaintiff employee's medical care on the day of her fall. Subsequently, plaintiff employee sought further medical treatment for shoulder and neck pain. Defendant employer contended that plaintiff employee's condition was no longer caused by her work-related injury and denied worker's compensation coverage. Ultimately, defendant insurer provided worker's compensation benefits to plaintiff employee. On appeal, plaintiffs contended that the exclusivity provisions of the Worker's Compensation Act, Ind. Code § 22-3-2-6, did not bar their complaint, which was based on defendants' actions subsequent to the original injury. The court determined that plaintiffs' cause of action fell squarely within the bad faith statute, Ind. Code § 22-3-4-12.1(a), and rested within the exclusive jurisdiction of the Worker's Compensation Board. The court rejected plaintiffs' argument that the bad faith statute violated the open courts provision of the Ind. Const. art. I, § 12.


OUTCOME: Judgment that dismissed plaintiffs' complaint against defendants for wrongful denial of plaintiff employee's request for worker's compensation benefits was affirmed. The court determined that plaintiffs' complaint was within the exclusive jurisdiction of the Worker's Compensation Board because it alleged that defendants' conduct violated the bad faith statute.

 

815 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Walker v. Campbell


No. 17A03-9806-CV-279


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


711 N.E.2d 42; 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 827



May 24, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 5, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 2341.
As Corrected June 22, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DEKALB CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Paul R. Cherry, Judge. Cause No. 17C01-9710-AD16.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a father and paternal grandparents, challenged the granting of a petition for adoption of the father's natural son, filed by appellees, a child's mother and her husband, and granted by the Dekalb Circuit Court (Indiana).


OVERVIEW: Appellant father and his parents objected to the proposed adoption of the father's natural son by appellees, a natural mother and her husband, on the basis that the state adoption statute, which operated to establish the father's irrevocable, implied consent to the adoption without notice or hearing, was violative of the father's constitutional due process rights. The trial court overruled appellant father's objection to the adoption, finding that he was not entitled to notice of the adoption proceedings nor was his consent required. Accordingly, the trial court granted the adoption over appellant father's objection. Although a settlement was reached between the parties regarding visitation, the court determined that the case was one that involved a matter of great public interest and that the issues raised should be addressed. On appeal, the court held that Indiana's adoption statutes, which operated to automatically extinguish a father's rights without notice or a hearing, violated the father's rights to due process and/or due course of law as guaranteed under the United States and Indiana constitutions. The order granting the adoption was reversed.


OUTCOME: The court granted in favor of appellants, a father and paternal grandparents, and reversed the lower court's order granting a petition for adoption of the father's natural son, by appellees, the child's mother and her husband. The court reversed on the basis that the statute in question, which did not allow for notice and opportunity to be heard, violated appellant father's due process rights.

Minks v. Pina


No. 45A03-9708-CV-273


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


709 N.E.2d 379; 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 640



April 30, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied June 15, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 2354.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Jeffrey J. Dywan, Judge. Cause No. 45D01-9602-CT-163.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed the order from the Lake Superior Court (Indiana) dismissing his complaint, pursuant to Ind. Trial R. 12(B)(6), in an action for negligence and relief under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, the father of the decedent, brought suit against defendants, the city, its police department, its police chief, and certain police officers, for negligence and for relief pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 after defendant police officers instructed a drunk motorist to drive home and the motorist caused an accident in which plaintiff's son died. The trial court granted defendants' motion to dismiss, and the court affirmed. Defendants had governmental immunity from suit under the Indiana Tort Claims Act, Ind. Code § 34-13-3-3. Plaintiff's § 1983 claim also failed because the due process clause did not confer on plaintiff an affirmative right to government aid. Defendants did not deprive plaintiff's decedent of life in violation of the due process clause but merely failed to protect him from private violence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order because defendants had governmental immunity under the Indiana Tort Claims Act from plaintiff's negligence claim and because plaintiff did not have an affirmative right to government aid under the due process clause to protect him from private violence.

 

817 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Miller v. State


No. 46A03-9805-CR-236


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


709 N.E.2d 48; 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 619



April 27, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAPORTE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Robert W. Gilmore, Jr., Judge. Cause No. 46C01-9701-CF-1.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant appealed a judgment from the Laporte Circuit Court (Indiana) sentencing him to 30 years in prison with five years suspended following his guilty plea to possession of cocaine, a Class A felony, under Ind. Code § 35-4-6- (Supp. 1996).


OVERVIEW: Criminal defendant was arrested after he was found with drugs within 1,000 feet of a school. He was charged with numerous offenses and, while out on bond, committed two more drug-related offenses. Under a plea agreement, he pled guilty to possession of cocaine in exchange for plaintiff state's dismissal of all other charges. Defendant appealed his 30-year sentence. The court found that the presumptive sentence under Ind. Code § 35-50-2-4 (1993) was 30 years. The lower court did not have to explain its reasons for imposing the presumptive sentence, but did list aggravating and mitigating factors in the order. The lower court did not err in considering the subsequent arrests as aggravating factors, but did err by using the facts surrounding the subsequent arrests. That was an improper consideration, as the subsequent charges were dropped in defendant's plea agreement. The court remanded to allow the lower court to reweigh all valid factors. The court found that Ind. Code § 35-48-4-6, regarding drug offenses in a school zone, imposed strict liability. The imposition of a 30-year sentence for defendant's crime was not so disproportionate as to shock the conscience.


OUTCOME: Criminal defendant's 30-year sentence for cocaine possession was affirmed in part because the sentence for such a grave crime was not so disproportionate as to shock the conscience. The judgment was reversed in part because the lower court considered improper aggravating factors in imposing sentence, and remanded for a proper determination of sentence using valid aggravating and mitigating factors.

Furrer v. State


No. 79A02-9811-CR-874


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


709 N.E.2d 744; 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 620



April 23, 1999, Decided  
April 23, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE TIPPECANOE COUNTY COURT. The Honorable Laura Zeman, Judge. Cause No. 79E02-9712-DF-862.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought an interlocutory review from the Tippecanoe County Court (Indiana), which ordered that appellant testify as a victim-witness in a battery case in exchange for a grant of use immunity offered by the state.


OVERVIEW: Appellant victim-witness filed an interlocutory appeal from an order that she testify in a battery case in exchange for a grant of use immunity offered by the state. Appellant argued that the order violated her privilege against self-incrimination, as guaranteed by U.S. Const. amend. V and Ind. Const. art. I, § 14, where her compelled testimony would reveal self-incriminating evidence of untruthfulness. Appellant claimed that to force her to testify necessarily would show that either that she gave false information in her first statement to police or that she perjured herself in a later sworn statement to the prosecutor's office recanting her prior statement. The court determined that the perjury exception in Ind. Code § 35-37-3-3 applied only to present perjury, that is, perjury committed as part of compelled testimony. The court construed § 35-37-3-3(b) to be constitutionally valid; the grant of use immunity required that appellant testify truthfully under a grant of use immunity but protected appellant from prosecution for past perjurious statements thereby revealed. Thus, the court affirmed the order that appellant be compelled to testify.


OUTCOME: The order that appellant victim-witness testify in a battery case in exchange for a grant of use immunity offered by the state was affirmed. The grant of use immunity required that appellant testify truthfully under a grant of use immunity but protected appellant from prosecution for past perjurious statements thereby revealed. Therefore, appellant could be compelled to testify.

 

819 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Benedetto v. Indiana Univ.


No. 49A02-9805-CV-440


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


707 N.E.2d 1062; 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 508



April 5, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Steven A. Frank, Judge. Cause No. 49D13-9707-CT-985.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action against appellees, a state university, its trustees and officials, brought under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 to recover the difference between resident and non-resident fees, appellant graduate challenged a judgment of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) that granted appellees' motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant law school graduate of appellee university brought an action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 against appellees, the university and its officials in their official capacity, to recover the difference between the fees charged resident students and the non-resident fees he had paid. Appellant claimed the university's rules governing resident and non-resident tuition rates violated constitutional due process and equal protection rights. Appellant later amended the complaint to allege the same violations, but deleted all reference to § 1983. Appellees moved for summary judgment, which the trial court granted. Appellant sought review. The court affirmed, finding appellant's case was readily distinguishable from prior actions, alleging constitutional violations allowed to be brought directly under the Fourteenth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. XIV. Appellant's election to pay the tuition fees in order to attend the university was not compelled but rather chosen. Moreover, appellant's payment of the fees did not constitute a taking, and appellant had merely stated a claim for damages, excluded against both the state university and its officials acting within their official capacity.


OUTCOME: Judgment granting appellees' motion for summary judgment was affirmed because appellant's claim was excluded against both the university and its officials acting within their official capacity.

 

820 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Spencer v. O'Connor


No. 49A02-9805-CV-466


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


707 N.E.2d 1039; 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 458



March 30, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable John L. Price, Judge. Cause No. 49D11-9801-CP-139.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, convicted sex offenders, appealed the grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee government official by the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) in their suit alleging that their inclusion in the Indiana Sex Offender Registry violated the prohibition against ex post facto laws contained in both the state and federal constitutions.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, convicted sex offenders, brought suit against appellee, the director of the Indiana Criminal Justice Institute, and alleged their inclusion in the Indiana Sex Offender Registry violated the prohibitions against ex post facto laws contained in U.S. Const. art. I, § 10 and Ind. Const. art. I, § 24. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellee. On appeal, the court agreed that the Indiana Sex Offender Registration statute, Ind. Code § 5-2-12-1 et seq., applied retroactively to appellants and therefore the specific issue was whether the registration and notification provisions imposed additional punishment for appellants' crimes. The court applied a two-step process for determining whether inclusion in the registry was punishment. First, the court determined that the legislature had not intended inclusion in the registry to be a criminal sanction because the statute was not part of the criminal code and its design signified a regulatory intent. Next, the court held appellants had not met their burden of providing proof that the statute had a punitive purpose or effect. The court therefore affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee after determining that the civil sanction of inclusion in a sex offender registry was not punishment that violated constitutional prohibitions against ex post facto laws.

Fleming v. International Pizza Supply Corp.


No. 49A02-9802-CV-193


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


707 N.E.2d 1033; 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 427



March 29, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT NO. 5. The Honorable Steven R. Eichholtz, Judge. Cause No. 49D05-9104-MI-506-001.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought interlocutory review of a decision of the Marion Superior Court, (Indiana) that denied appellant's motion for leave to file a second amended counterclaim in his shareholder's dissent and appraisal rights action.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was a minority shareholder. Appellee, the majority shareholder, approved the sale of assets of another corporation to their corporation. Appellant disapproved of the asset sale and exercised his dissenters' rights under Ind. Code § 23-1-44-8, which proscribed challenges to a corporate action by dissenters. Appellee filed a petition to determine share value. The state supreme court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to appellee on appellant's counterclaims. The trial court denied appellant's motion for leave to file a second amended counterclaim. The court affirmed in part holding that Ind. Code § 23-1-44-8(c) did not violate the Indiana Constitution. The court reversed in part and remanded to the trial court for clarification as to why it denied appellant's motion to amend because appellant's fraudulent conveyance and contract claims were not governed by the Business Corporation Law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the denial of appellant's motion to amend because appellant's fraudulent conveyance and contract claims were not governed by the Business Corporation Law. The court held that the Indiana Constitution was not violated by the governing statute.

 

822 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Wurster v. State


CONSOLIDATED NO. 49A02-9802-CR-126


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


708 N.E.2d 587; 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 426



March 29, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] On Petition for Transfer July 28, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Ind. LEXIS 546.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Cale Bradford, Presiding Judge. Cause Nos. 49G03-9704-CF-60445; 49G03-9704-CF-60442; and 49G03-9704-CF-60430.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants filed an interlocutory appeal of a decision of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), denying their motions to dismiss the grand jury indictment charging each of the three appellants with bribery, two with unlawful lobbying, and one with five counts of filing a fraudulent report and one count of perjury.


OVERVIEW: Appellants challenged, through an interlocutory appeal, the trial court's denial of their motions to dismiss a grand jury indictment. One appellant was a member of the Indiana House of Representatives, who had part time employment as a marketing representative. The essential charges were that the other appellants bribed him. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court affirmed as to grand jury impropriety, and held that the government had no duty to disclose to the grand jury substantial exculpatory evidence in its possession. The court reversed as to bribery because the charge was insufficient. Indiana's bribery statute prohibited public servants from accepting property for a forbidden purpose; however, it specifically exempted property the public servant was authorized by law to accept. Ind. Code § 35-44-1-1(a)(1). Appellant legislator was authorized by statute to accept compensation for part-time employment. The indictment also failed to sufficiently apprise appellants of the offense; and the indictment failed to disclose sufficient facts so as to protect appellants from future prosecutions arising from the same facts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the trial court's denial of appellant's motion to dismiss an indictment. As to the claim of grand jury impropriety, the court reversed because the government had no duty to present exculpatory evidence to the grand jury. The court reversed the bribery count because the charge failed for sufficiency. Appellant legislator was authorized to accept compensation for part-time employment.

 

823 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Oman v. State


No. 46A03-9808-CR-365


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


707 N.E.2d 325; 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 419; 14 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1662



March 23, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAPORTE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable William J. Boklund, Judge. Cause No. 46D04-9805-CM-679.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the denial by the LaPorte Superior Court (Indiana) of his motion to suppress his employment-related drug test results obtained pursuant to a prosecutor-issued subpoena duces tecum. The drug test had been obtained pursuant to a government-employer's workplace drug testing policy.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was the driver a fire truck involved in a collision with another fire truck. Both drivers were driven to a drug testing lab for drug testing. Later, a police officer heard from an unidentified source that defendant's drug tests were positive. The prosecutor then issued a subpoena duces tecum directing the testing lab to produce defendant's results. The lab complied, and the results revealed defendant tested positive for marijuana. Defendant was charged with operating a vehicle with a controlled substance in his blood. Defendant moved to suppress his test results. The lower court denied his motion and certified the issue for interlocutory appeal. The court reversed the denial of defendant's suppression motion. The prosecutor exceeded his statutory authority for issuing a subpoena because there was no reliable information to warrant probable cause. Also, the subpoena represented an unreasonable demand on the test lab because it did not have the legal authority to comply. The court found that the use of the mandatory drug testing policy to pursue criminal prosecutions against defendant was a violation of defendant's constitutional rights under the U.S. Const. amend. IV.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the lower court denying defendant's motion to suppress his employment-related drug test results, finding that the subpoena was improperly issued and the use of compulsory drug testing results to pursue criminal prosecution against defendant was a violation of defendant's constitutional rights.

Town Council of New Harmony v. Parker


No. 87A01-9808-CV-305


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


707 N.E.2d 1002; 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 418



March 23, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied May 18, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 2363.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE WARRICK CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Donald G. Hendrickson, Judge. Cause No. 87C01-9608-CP-305.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a ruling of the Warrick Circuit Court (Indiana) ordering appellant to provide services and utilities to appellee's real estate lots but rejecting appellant's proposal for service provision and assessing damages for the taking of appellee's property without just compensation.


OVERVIEW: Appellee owner purchased several subdivision lots. The lots were assessed on the basis of being on a paved street with water, sewer, gas and electric, but none of these improvements were provided. Appellee made demands on the appellant town to provide services but appellant refused. Appellant declared a moratorium on improvement permits for appellee's lots and restricted access by placing a chain across unimproved portion of the street. The trial court held appellant was required to provide services to appellee's lots in a comparable manner as those similarly situated. Appellant's service proposal was rejected so damages were assessed for the taking of appellee's property without just compensation. The appellate court affirmed since appellant was obligated to provide municipal services to appellee's annexed lots and appellant's actions constituted a taking without just compensation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision ordering appellant to provide services to appellee and assessing damage for a taking without just compensation since annexation cases and statute implicitly required appellant to provide municipal services to appellee's lots based on the demand by town's growth.

 

825 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Sears Roebuck & Co. v. Noppert


No. 84A04-9802-CV-47


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


705 N.E.2d 1065; 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 161



February 17, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE VIGO SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Dexter L. Bolin, Jr., Judge. Cause No. 84D03-9604-CT-652.



DISPOSITION: Decision of trial court granting motion to correct errors reversed, and this case remanded to trial court with instructions to reinstate summary judgment in favor of Sears.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant store challenged a decision of the Vigo Superior Court (Indiana), granting appellees' motion to correct errors and vacating its summary judgment order in appellant's favor in a products liability action. Appellant argued that the motion to correct errors was erroneously granted because the motion was untimely filed and because appellees did not have a meritorious defense to the summary judgment motion.


OVERVIEW: Appellees brought a product liability action against appellant department store. The trial court granted appellant's motion for summary judgment, ruling that the action was barred by the statute of limitations in Ind. Code § 33-1-1.5-5. The trial court later granted appellees' motion to correct errors and vacated its summary judgment order in appellant's favor. On appeal, appellant argued that the motion to correct errors was erroneously granted because the motion was untimely filed and because appellees did not have a meritorious defense to the summary judgment motion. The appeals court reversed the decision and remanded the matter for reinstatement of the summary judgment for appellant. The court ruled that the motion to correct errors was improperly granted because appellees were aware of the trial court's summary judgment ruling well before the 30 days for filing an appeal had elapsed, but appellees neglected to file an appeal. The court noted that relief under Ind. Trial R. 60(B) was only proper after a failure to perfect an appeal when some additional fact was present justifying extraordinary relief such that a trial court could invoke its equitable powers to do justice.


OUTCOME: The appeals court reversed the decision granting appellees' motion to correct errors and remanded the matter for reinstatement of the summary judgment in favor of appellant. The court ruled that a motion to correct errors was not an appropriate substitute for the timely filing of an appeal.

 

826 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


McCullough v. McCullough


No. 53A04-9702-CV-43


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


705 N.E.2d 190; 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 76



January 26, 1999, Decided  
January 26, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MONROE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Frank M. Nardi, Special Judge. Cause No. 53C03-9401-DR-70.



DISPOSITION: Petition denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed from a ruling of the Monroe Circuit Court (Indiana) seeking to disqualify a senior judge from serving as a judge in his case.


OVERVIEW: The court denied appellant's petition to disqualify a senior judge appointed by the supreme court to perform temporary judicial duties on behalf of the court of appeals from serving as a judge in his case. The court held that the Indiana Constitution did not prohibit the appointment of senior judges to perform temporary judicial duties on behalf of the Indiana Court of Appeals. The court determined that the Indiana Supreme Court had statutory authority to appoint the judge as a senior judge of the Indiana Court of Appeals under Ind. Code § 33-2.1-5-1 (1993). The court rejected appellant's argument that the judge lacked authority to decide his case because he had not been appointed senior judge at the time the court of appeals obtained jurisdiction over his case. The court of appeals' jurisdiction lies in the court as a whole, not individual judges or districts. The judge did not hold an office as that term was meant by Ind. Const. art. II, § 9, and his service as a senior judge did not violate that provision. Finally, the court disagreed that the judge's impartially might reasonably be questioned under the facts of the case. Therefore, his disqualification was not required.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's request to disqualify a senior judge because the Indiana Supreme Court had authority to appoint the judge, the judge had authority to decide the case, and his disqualification was not required as his impartiality was not reasonably questioned.

 

827 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. Sullivan


No. 71A03-9801-CV-11


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


703 N.E.2d 1102; 1998 Ind. App. LEXIS 2270



December 31, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ST. JOSEPH SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable William C. Whitman, Judge. Cause No. 71D06-9508-CP-765.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part and Affirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant grandmother challenged an order of the St. Joseph Superior Court (Indiana), which granted summary judgment to appellee secretary of the family and social services administration in appellant's suit pursuant to the Aid to Families with Dependent Children Act, 42 U.S.C.S. § 602, that challenged the amount she was paid for childcare services and appellee's methodologies and standards for determining such amount.


OVERVIEW: Appellant grandmother filed suit against appellee secretary of family and social services administration and claimed that she was underpaid for childcare services she provided for her grandchildren so that her daughter could obtain independence from the Aid to Families with Dependent Children Act (act), 42 U.S.C.S. § 602. The trial court entered summary judgment for appellee based on appellant's lack of standing. Appellant sought review of the amounts reimbursed and appellee's methodologies, procedures, and standards related thereto. The court held that where appellant, as a caretaker relative under the act, was intended to have been benefitted under the act, she had a demonstrable interest in a correct determination of her reimbursement from appellee; therefore, she had standing to seek judicial review of whether she was paid the correct amount. Appellant did not have standing to challenge appellee's methodologies where her interest was indirect and contingent upon her daughter's discretion in choosing her as the childcare provider. The court reversed and remanded for a determination of whether appellant was paid the proper amount and otherwise affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment as to the methodologies because appellant grandmother's interest was contingent upon being chosen to provide childcare; therefore, she lacked standing. The court reversed and remanded for further determination as to the amount paid because appellant had standing as a caretaker relative intended to benefit from Aid to Families with Dependent Children.

City of Indianapolis v. Woods


No. 49A02-9801-CV-74


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


703 N.E.2d 1087; 1998 Ind. App. LEXIS 2252



December 23, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. CIVIL DIVISION, ROOM NO. 12. The Honorable Susan M. Thompson, Judge. Cause No. 49D12-9702-CP-0246.



DISPOSITION: Matter remanded to trial court with instructions to affirm Merit Board's termination decision in all respects.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a judgment of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which reversed the decision by the Indianapolis Civilian Police Merit Board to terminate the employment of appellee employee and ordered his reinstatement as an officer with the police department.


OVERVIEW: Appellant city challenged the reversal of the decision by the Police Merit Board (Board) that terminated appellee employee as an officer with the police department. Appellant questioned whether the trial court erred in permitting additional evidence to supplement the record and whether the trial court improperly reweighed the evidence. The court concluded that the trial court abused its discretion in admitting the disciplinary record of appellee because he failed to show that he exercised due diligence in obtaining the newly discovered evidence. Further, the evidence of record was adequate to support the conclusion that appellee violated each departmental rule cited by the Board in its decision terminating employment as an officer. The Board's decision was logically supported by the evidence and was, therefore, not arbitrary or capricious. The court ordered the matter remanded to the trial court with instructions to affirm the Board's termination decision in all respects.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the trial court's decision that reversed the decision of the Police Merit Board (Board) terminating appellee employee. The court instructed the trial court to affirm the Board's decision and held that the trial court abused its discretion in admitting the newly discovered evidence without finding that appellee exercised due diligence in obtaining the evidence and that the Board's decision was not arbitrary or capricious.

Scott County v. Vaughn


No. 72A05-9805-CV-271


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


704 N.E.2d 1029; 1998 Ind. App. LEXIS 2253



December 23, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied February 19, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 2380.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE SCOTT CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable James D. Kleopfer, Judge. Cause No. 72C01-9403-CT-19.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of the judgment of the Scott Circuit Court (Indiana) in favor of appellees, injured person, her spouse, and state.


OVERVIEW: Appellee injured person was hurt when her vehicle was struck by a northbound vehicle travelling on a state road. Appellee injured person and her spouse commenced suit against appellee state and appellant county and alleged negligent design, construction, and maintenance of the intersection. Following negotiations, appellee state entered into loan receipt agreements with appellees, injured person and her spouse. Appellant sought to set aside the loan receipt agreement and the lower court dismissed appellant's motion. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that a loan receipt agreement was permitted under Ind. Const. art. XI, § 12 under the liberal approach to constitutional construction and giving effect to the intent of those who framed the provision. The court held that the use of loan receipt agreements had been approved by the courts in the past and were not contrary to public policy, as a whole or in this particular case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court in favor of appellees, injured person, her spouse, and state, because the use of a loan receipt agreement as a settlement tool was not violative of the Indiana Constitution and was not contrary to public policy.

 

830 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Dvorak v. City of Bloomington


No. 53A05-9712-CV-503


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


702 N.E.2d 1121; 1998 Ind. App. LEXIS 2191



December 15, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MONROE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Elizabeth N. Mann, Judge. Cause No. 53C04-9604-OV-360.



DISPOSITION: Vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, owner and unrelated residents, disputed a decision of the Monroe County Circuit Court (Indiana), which denied their motion for summary judgment. Appellants argued that Bloomington, Ind., Municipal Code § 20.02.01.00, a zoning ordinance, which prohibited property being occupied by more than four adults who were unrelated by blood, marriage, or adoption, was an ultra vires act and it violated Ind. Const. art. I, § 23.


OVERVIEW: Whether the ordinance was an ultra vires act depended upon the interpretation of the enabling statutes, Ind. Code §§ 36-7-4-601 and 36-7-4-201, which granted local governments the power to zone. The court agreed with the city that the statutes mandated that the city would provide healthful surroundings for family life and promote the general welfare and safety of its citizens. The dispositive issue was, therefore, whether the city constitutionally defined "family" in the ordinance. The court considered art. I, § 23, the Equal Privileges Clause of the Indiana Constitution. The court held that appellants had the burden of disproving the city's bases for the classification that were readily apparent, including but not limited to those set forth in the ordinance, and those reasonably relied upon by the city during the course of the litigation. However, by objecting to appellants' interrogatory and receiving an order from the trial court relieving it of the duty to answer the interrogatory, the city thwarted appellants' attempt to discover what bases the city advanced in support of the ordinance. Therefore, the court expressed no opinion on the merits of appellants' argument.


OUTCOME: The court vacated and remanded for further proceedings. In particular, the court directed that appellants should be given a reasonable opportunity for discovery in order to determine what goals the ordinance was designed to promote.

 

831 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Boss v. State


No. 79A05-9803-CR-173


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


702 N.E.2d 782; 1998 Ind. App. LEXIS 2187



December 11, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE TIPPECANOE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Donald C. Johnson, Judge. Cause No. 79D01-9611-CF-92.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The prosecutor charged defendant with three counts of nonsupport, under Ind. Code § 35-46-1-5, for failure to support his three minor children. Defendant failed to appear at trial or sentencing, and the Tippecanoe Superior Court (Indiana) convicted defendant on all three counts, and was sentenced to three consecutive three-year sentences for a total of nine years. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had previous been convicted of nonsupport, and argued the following: (1) the statute was unconstitutionally vague, ambiguous, and improperly delegated legislative powers to the prosecutor; (2) his convictions violated double jeopardy because he had previously been convicted for nonsupport of the same children; (3) the prosecutor arbitrarily divided the offenses into separate time periods in order to charge three separate offenses; and (4) he was denied effective assistance of trial counsel. The court determined that the statute clearly informed defendant of the criminal penalties attached to his failure to support his children, the statute was not unconstitutionally vague, and he could be prosecuted again under the same statute because the previous prosecution was for a specified period of time in the past which did not overlap the periods of time presently at issue. The court ruled that the consecutive sentences which resulted from three separate charges and convictions constituted multiple punishments for the same offense, and therefore defendant could be convicted and sentenced for only one crime. Defendant failed to show ineffective assistance of trial counsel.


OUTCOME: The matter was remanded with instructions to vacate two of the convictions and resentence accordingly.

LeBrun v. Conner


No. 84A05-9708-CV-359


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


702 N.E.2d 754; 1998 Ind. App. LEXIS 2092



December 8, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE VIGO SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Michael Eldred, Judge. Cause No. 84D01-9611-CT-2019.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, patient and spouse, sought review of the decision of the Vigo Superior Court (Indiana), which granted the motion for summary judgment by appellee optometrist doctor, in the patient's action for medical malpractice and fraud.


OVERVIEW: The doctor examined the patient and failed to diagnose her with glaucoma. The patient consulted an ophthalmologist that informed the patient she had glaucoma and had her intraocular pressure been monitored previously and treated with drops it could have been controlled. The patient filed a complaint pursuant to the Indiana Medical Malpractice Act, Ind. Code § 27-12-1 et seq., which alleged the doctor negligently monitored her elevated intraocular pressure. The trial court granted the doctor's motion for summary judgment because the patient's action was bared by the statute of limitations. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that under Ind. Code § 27-12-7-1 a medical malpractice claim had to be filed within two years after the date of the alleged act. The court held that even if the doctor was estopped from asserting the statute of limitations as a defense due to fraudulent concealment, the patient was required to institute an action within a reasonable time after the alleged malpractice was deemed to have been discovered. The court found that the patient waited over two years after discovering the alleged malpractice, which was deemed unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that granted the doctor's motion for summary judgment in the patient's medical malpractice action.

 

833 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Monschein v. Lalonde


No. 49A05-9803-CV-171


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


701 N.E.2d 1275; 1998 Ind. App. LEXIS 2081



November 30, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Kenneth H. Johnson, Judge. Cause No. 49D02-9604-DR-490.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of an order from the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which granted visitation of his daughters to appellee grandmother pursuant to former Ind. Code § 31-1-11.7-2.


OVERVIEW: The father adopted his late wife's daughter from a previous relationship after he was granted permanent custody by a Colorado court. The trial court then granted the grandmother visitation rights to that daughter and the father's natural daughter. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the father waived any argument regarding the constitutionality of § 31-1-11.7-2 because he did not raise the argument at trial. Although the court held that the father waived any argument regarding his status as a stepparent on the same basis, the court noted that the father still would be a stepparent for statutory purposes even though his late wife's daughter was not born during a previous marriage. The court held that the grandmother's visitation rights survived the adoption by the father, a stepparent, even where the adoption occurred after the death of the child's natural mother. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in granting the grandmother visitation rights based on its factual findings because, although the grandmother did exhibit misconduct in the custody proceedings, the grandmother finally agreed to forego any custody claim to her granddaughter.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of visitation rights to the grandmother.

State Bd. of Registration for Prof'l Eng'rs v. Eberenz


No. 10A04-9805-CV-237


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


701 N.E.2d 892; 1998 Ind. App. LEXIS 1989



November 17, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied January 22, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 2391.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE CLARK SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Cecile A. Blau, Judge. Cause No. 10D02-9706-CP-156.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an administrative action, appellants, the State Board of Registration for Professional Engineers and the Indiana Professional Licensing Agency, sought review of the order of the Clark Superior Court (Indiana), granting summary judgment in favor of respondent, a professional engineer.


OVERVIEW: A professional engineer in Kentucky filed an application for comity registration as an Indiana professional engineer in 1996. An administrative law judge denied his request. He filed a civil action, whereby the trial court determined that the denial was not in accordance with the law. The appellate court agreed. The requirements of the governing statute, Ind. Code § 25-31-1-21 were satisfied. The Kentucky engineer applied for registration as an Indiana professional engineer, paid the fee established by the Board, and showed that he held a valid out-of-state certificate of registration as a professional engineer.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

835 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Warren v. State


No. 53A01-9704-CR-130


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


701 N.E.2d 902; 1998 Ind. App. LEXIS 1990



November 17, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MONROE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Kenneth G. Todd, Judge. Cause No. 53C03-9603-CF-150.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Monroe Circuit Court (Indiana) of sexual misconduct with a minor, a Class C felony under Ind. Code § 35-42-4-9. He appealed and claimed that the trial court improperly instructed the jury, the State presented insufficient evidence to convict him, and his trial counsel was constitutionally ineffective.


OVERVIEW: Neither defendant nor the State objected to the jury instructions or tendered an instruction of their own regarding the elements of sexual misconduct with a minor. Therefore, defendant waived review of that issue. The instructions on sexual misconduct with a minor tracked the language of the statute and did not preclude consideration of the intent element of the crime. The instructions given to the jury contained words that in their plain meaning could be understood by the jury as including criminal intent and did not mislead the jury as to the law of the case. To sustain the conviction, the State needed to prove that defendant did: (1) perform sexual intercourse; (2) with the victim; (3) when defendant was at least eighteen years of age, and (4) when the victim was at least fourteen years of age, but less than sixteen. The testimony from the victim regarding the defendant's acts was sufficient to sustain the conviction. The defendant failed to show that his counsel's substandard performance was so prejudicial as to deny him a fair trial and, but for his trial counsel's actions, that the outcome of the trial would have been different.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed.

Area Plan Comm'n v. Wilson


No. 82A01-9712-CV-429


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


701 N.E.2d 856; 1998 Ind. App. LEXIS 1962



November 12, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied November 29, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 7786.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE VANDERBURGH SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable William J. Brune, Judge. Cause No. 82D03-9606-CP-1626.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner brought a declaratory judgment action against defendants, city and planning commission, to determine whether the city's zoning code was unconstitutional when it required him to obtain a special use permit in order to operate a church on his property. The Vanderburgh Superior Court (Indiana) found in favor of the landowner. The city and planning commission appealed.


OVERVIEW: The landowner obtained a special use permit to operate a church for one year. At the expiration of that year, the landowner filed suit against the city and planning commission, alleging that its zoning code violated the First Amendment by requiring him to obtain a special use permit to operate a church on his property. The trial court found for the landowner. On appeal, however, the court reversed. The city's zoning code and the special use ordinance did not violate the Free Exercise Clause of the First Amendment because they did not constitute an unreasonable burden on the landowner. The special use ordinance was not a prior restraint on religious speech because it did not impermissibly imbue the city's board of zoning appeals with unfettered discretion. The trial court clearly erred when it found that the zoning code discriminated against Christians.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment that had found that the zoning code was unconstitutional. The court remanded for entry of a declaratory judgment in favor of the city and planning commission.

State v. Harris


No. 33A05-9712-CR-508


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


702 N.E.2d 722; 1998 Ind. App. LEXIS 1855



November 4, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE HENRY CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable John L. Kellam, Judge. Cause No. 33C01-9702-CF-8.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of the judgment from the Henry Circuit Court (Indiana), which granted defendant's motion to suppress. Defendant was charged with operating a vehicle after his license was forfeited for life and without proof of financial responsibility.


OVERVIEW: An officer saw the ramp of the trailer defendant was towing drop and begin to emit sparks as it was dragged. The officer stopped defendant, requested his driver's license, and upon defendant's failure to produce it, discovered that his license was suspended. Defendant was tried for operating a vehicle after his license was forfeited for life and without proof of financial responsibility. Defendant filed a motion to suppress. The trial court granted the motion. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's decision. The court held that: (1) the officer had statutory authority to stop defendant under Ind. Code Ann. § 34-4-32-2 (1983) pertaining to the unsafe condition of the trailer; (2) in order to pull defendant over and issue a warning, it was necessary for the officer to know defendant's name; (3) the officer's request for identifying information was a small but necessary intrusion reasonably related in scope to the justification for the intrusion; and (4) when defendant repeatedly gave the officer false information, defendant's actions gave rise to a reasonable suspicion that defendant may have committed, was committing, or was about to commit a crime.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision, which had granted defendant's motion to suppress.

Indiana Dep't of Envtl. Mgmt. v. Medical Disposal Servs.


No. 56A05-9805-CV-243


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


700 N.E.2d 500; 1998 Ind. App. LEXIS 1771



October 16, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied December 29, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Ind. App. LEXIS 2391.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE NEWTON CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Robert Smart, Judge. Cause No. 56C01-9708-MI-6.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The plaintiff medical waste disposal company moved for summary judgment requesting that the Newton Circuit Court (Indiana) prohibit the defendant Indiana Department of Environmental Management (IDEM) from imposing penalties during the term of a preliminary injunction IDEM had previously obtained. The trial court granted summary judgment for the company. IDEM appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court stated that dispositive issue was whether, in the exercise of its judicial authority to control the administrative process and temper an agency's power to assess penalties, it should have prohibited IDEM from imposing a penalty against the company for the operation of its transfer station that: (1) never posed a threat to the environment; and (2) had become expressly permitted by law since the issuance of the preliminary injunction . The 1997 promulgation of Ind. Code § 13-11-2-235 legalized the very operation in which the company had been engaged. This distinctive statute was enacted specifically to remedy the plight of the company. The premise upon which the doctrine of amelioration rested compelled the court to exercise its judicial authority over the administrative process and prohibit IDEM from imposing penalties against the company under those circumstances. IDEM should also have been prohibited from imposing any type of penalty against the company for its past operation of the transfer facility.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Schweitzer v. State


No. 32A05-9805-CR-251


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


700 N.E.2d 488; 1998 Ind. App. LEXIS 1763



October 14, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE HENDRICKS SUPERIOR COURT. ROOM ONE. The Honorable Mary Lee Comer, Judge. Cause No. 32D01-8605-CF-34.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the decision of the Hendricks Superior Court (Indiana), which denied defendant's motion to modify the 50-year sentence imposed upon her conviction for criminal deviate conduct as a class A felony.


OVERVIEW: The trial court sentenced defendant to 50 years imprisonment for her criminal deviate conduct conviction. The trial court granted defendant's motion to reduce her sentence to 20 years and later vacated the order because defendant had failed to file her petition within 180 days after she began serving her sentence in accordance with Ind. Code § 35-38-1-17. Defendant filed another petition to modify her sentence, which the trial court denied. Defendant sought review, contending that § 35-38-1-17 conflicted with Ind. Const. art. I, §§ 16, 18, and that the trial court erred in ruling that it had no jurisdiction on defendant's motion for sentence modification. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held defendant's claim of unconstitutionality was without merit. The legislature was free to give the trial court authority to render a modification of the sentence with whatever conditions and within whatever time it deemed appropriate. The court found that Ind. Code § 35-38-1-17 did not take judicial power away from the trial court and give it to the prosecuting attorney. The court concluded that under § 35-38-1-17, the trial court was without jurisdiction to modify defendant's sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision to deny defendant's motion to modify her 50-year sentence for criminal deviate conduct as a class A felony.
