Reynolds v. State


No. 65A05-9712-CR-547


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


698 N.E.2d 390; 1998 Ind. App. LEXIS 1344



August 27, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE POSEY SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Donald E. Baier, Judge. Cause No. 65D01-9707-DF-382.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver challenged a decision of the Posey Superior Court (Indiana), which denied his petition for judicial review of the suspension of his driver's license by appellee state.


OVERVIEW: An officer stopped the driver for suspected drunk driving. The driver submitted to a portable breath test, which resulted in him being arrested and informed that if he refused to submit to a chemical breath test, his driving privileges were subject to suspension for one year. The driver failed to give an adequate breath sample on four different occasions. Thus, pursuant to Ind. Code § 9-30-6-8, his license was suspended. The trial court denied the driver's petition for judicial review. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that Ind. Code § 9-309-6-10(f), which required one to show that the license suspension was erroneous, was constitutional and did not violate the Fourteenth Amendment or Ind. Const. art. I, § 12. The court was unable to say that placing the burden of going forward with the evidence at the hearing on the driver created a substantial risk of erroneously depriving him of his license. He was not entitled to a jury trial under Ind. Const. art. I, § 20 on the issue of whether he refused to submit to a chemical test. The trial court properly denied his petition because he did not comply with the statute in providing breath samples.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the driver's petition for judicial review of the suspension of his driver's license.

Michigan Mut. Ins. Co. v. Sports, Inc.


No. 84A04-9707-CV-314


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


698 N.E.2d 834; 1998 Ind. App. LEXIS 1345



August 27, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE VIGO SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Michael H. Eldred, Judge. Cause No. 84D01-9201-CP-133.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurance company sought review from a judgment of the Vigo Superior Court (Indiana), which rendered a jury verdict in favor of appellee insured, awarding compensatory damages and punitive damages claiming breach of good faith and fair dealing.


OVERVIEW: The issues for the court were whether the trial court erred in instructing the jury and whether the punitive damage award violated due process. The insurance company declined coverage because it claimed that no policy was ever written to cover the insured's interest in the bowling alley. On appeal, the court held that the jury might have been better instructed had it been given the definition of a general agent. However, when the challenged instruction was read together with the other instructions, the court did not find the instruction to be a misstatement of the law constituting an abuse of discretion. The trial did not abuse its discretion in instructing the jury on any issue. Further, given the nature of the insurance company's conduct, the court did not find that punitive damages in an amount nearly 14 times the compensatory damages awarded so lacked a reasonable relationship between those two figures as to render the punitive damage award constitutionally unacceptable. Therefore, although the ratio of punitive to actual damages was high, the court did not conclude that the punitive damages were so grossly excessive as to violate the constitutional limits of due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Vaillancourt v. State


No. 44A03-9712-CR-406


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


695 N.E.2d 606; 1998 Ind. App. LEXIS 788



May 22, 1998, Decided  
May 22, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAGRANGE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable George E. Brown, Judge. Cause No. 44D01-9505-CF-053.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the LaGrange Superior Court (Indiana), which convicted him of burglary that resulted in serious bodily injury, a Class A felony.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and another knocked on the victim's door, sprayed the victim's face with mace, and defendant hit the victim over the head with a jar of nuts and bolts. On appeal, defendant argued that the term "extreme pain," found in Ind. Code § 35-41-1-25, was unconstitutionally vague. The court affirmed the conviction and held that defendant's constitutional argument failed for two reasons: (1) it was waived because it was not properly raised in the trial court, and (2) the term "extreme pain" was not unconstitutionally vague because it was not a term that persons of average intelligence could not understand. The court also held that the trial court did not err when it denied defendant's Motion for Discharge because defendant failed to cite any factual basis or evidence for his contention that the delay in bringing him to trial was not due to the congestion of the trial court's calendar. The court further found sufficient evidence to support defendant's conviction because a reasonable jury could have found that the offense resulted in serious bodily injury to the victim in that the victim sustained multiple bruises, a damaged wrist, a concussion, and a three-inch head wound.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of burglary that resulted in serious bodily injury.

Ad Craft v. Board of Zoning Appeals


No. 82A01-9705-CV-146


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


693 N.E.2d 110; 1998 Ind. App. LEXIS 398



March 27, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Rehearing Denied May 29, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE VANDERBURGH SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Terry D. Dietsch, Judge. Cause No. 82D03-9602-CP-366.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant business sought review of a decision of the Venderburgh Superior Court (Indiana), which affirmed the decision of appellee board of zoning appeals that a business needed a permit in order to place a new face on an existing sign.


OVERVIEW: The business merged with another business, and placed a new face on its existing business sign, for which a permit had been obtained, to reflect the new name. The area planning commission advised the business that it needed a permit to change the sign, and the board upheld the decision of the planning commission. The trial court subsequently upheld the board's decision, and on appeal the court affirmed, holding that under the wording of Evansville, Ind. Code § 15.153.06.106(A), (B), a change to the face of the sign required a permit. The court noted that the board's failure to timely file its conclusions was harmless error. The court then rejected the business' argument that requiring a permit to change the wording on the sign violated its constitutional right to free speech, as the ordinance was content neutral, and the ordinance advanced the legitimate governmental interest of aesthetics and traffic safety. The permit requirement enabled the commission to verify the alteration of the design did not affect the characteristics that were allowed under the previous permit. Further, as there was no deprivation of a constitutional right, there was no claim under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision upholding the determination of the board that a permit was needed to change the face on an existing sign.

Deasy-Leas v. Leas


No. 02A03-9708-CV-277


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


693 N.E.2d 90; 1998 Ind. App. LEXIS 396



March 25, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellee's Rehearing Denied May 27, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE ALLEN CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Thomas L. Ryan, Judge. The Honorable Thomas J. Felts, Magistrate. Cause Nos. 02C01-9209-DR-1096, 02C01-9510-DR-1299.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, parents and a guardian ad litem, challenged an order by the Allen Circuit Court (Indiana), which denied the guardian ad litem's motion to quash discovery requests by appellee spouses for production of the guardian ad litem's file in separate custody proceedings.


OVERVIEW: Appellant guardian ad litem filed a motion to quash discovery requests by appellee spouses for production of the guardian ad litem's file in separate custody proceedings. The trial judge denied the motion and the guardian ad litem and appellant parents appealed. The court held that although Indiana had not enacted a statutory privilege for communications between guardians ad litem and their charges and the court could not create a privilege where none had been created by statute, the general confidentiality provision in Ind. Code § 31-17-2-20 (1997) allowed a court to make a determination that the particular circumstances require confidentiality as to a "public record." The court also held that a court could rely upon the protective powers of Ind. R. Trial P. 26(C) when a guardian ad litem or any other party requested confidentiality. The court reversed the trial court's judgment denying the motion to quash because the judgment erroneously stated that no statutes or trial rules existed that protected from discovery a guardian ad litem's file. The court remanded for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's denial of appellant guardian ad litem's motion to quash discovery requests for production of the guardian ad litem's file and remanded for further proceedings.

 

845 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Common Cause v. State


No. 49A02-9612-CV-842


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


691 N.E.2d 1358; 1998 Ind. App. LEXIS 140



March 10, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. CIVIL DIVISION 1. The Honorable Anthony J. Metz, III, Judge. Cause No. 49D01-9406-CP-491.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff lobbyists brought an action in the Marion Superior Court, Civil Division (Indiana) against defendant State of Indiana (state) challenging the delegation of authority to the Indiana Lobby Registration Commission (commission) by Ind. Code § 2-7-1-1 et seq. as unconstitutionally assuming the duties of another branch of government, Ind. Const. art. 3, § 1. The trial court granted the state summary judgment. The lobbyists appealed.


OVERVIEW: The statute required lobbyists to register and file reports. The commission was an agency of the legislative branch. The commission collected the reports, made them available to the public, and conducted audits. The speaker of the house, the president pro tempore of the senate, and the minority leaders of both the house and senate, each appointed one member of the commission. The court held that each branch of government was allowed to perform incidental activities, that appeared the duties of another branch, where necessary to carry out its proper powers. Thus, even thought the power of appointment was generally a legislative function, the legislature had the authority to appoint the commission's members as an incidental power. The regulation of lobbyists was incidental to the functions of the legislature. The legislature had a legitimate interest in regulating those who sought to influence its members. While the commission was given authority to investigate violation of the statute, hold hearings, and impose civil remedies, criminal investigations and prosecutions were performed by the executive and judicial branch.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment.

Deible v. Poole


No. 45A03-9706-CV-211


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


691 N.E.2d 1313; 1998 Ind. App. LEXIS 130



March 4, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] On Petition to Transfer Granted December 10, 1998, Reported at; 1998 Ind. LEXIS 631. Rehearing Denied June 19, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Ind. App. LEXIS 2437.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Jeffery J. Dywan, Judge. Cause No. 45D01-8904-CT-383.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for new trial on issue of damages.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sought review of a judgment of the Lake Superior Court (Indiana) denying her motion to correct error after a jury returned a verdict for defendant in plaintiff's personal injury case, denying plaintiff damages, even though defendant admitted causation and some damages.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was simply stopped at a red light when defendant struck her from behind. Defendant admitted fault and conceded that some damages were due, but argued that plaintiff failed to mitigate her damages by continuing to seek unwarranted medical treatments. The jury, however, returned a verdict for defendant, and the superior court refused to grant plaintiff's motion to correct error. The court reversed, remanding for a new trial on the issue of damages. The mitigation defense concerned only plaintiff's act of continuing to seek allegedly unwarranted medical treatments, not any act contributing to the accident itself. Thus, a verdict for defendant was inappropriate because the defense only operated as to the amount of damages, not to the ultimate issue of liability.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision, remanding for a new trial on the issue of damages.

Mayfield v. Continental Rehabilitation Hosp.

COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient and wife sought review of the decision from the Vigo Superior Court No. 3 (Indiana), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee hospital. The hospital had brought suit against the patient and wife requesting the preliminary determination of law that the proposed complaint was time-barred. The patient and wife's complaint had previously been dismissed by the trial court.


OVERVIEW: The patient and wife argued that the Journey Account Statute, Ind. Code § 34-1-2-8, operated to permit them to reinstate their complaint after having filed their untimely proposed complaint with the Department of Insurance. The court held that there was no reason, other than negligence, why the patient and wife could not have filed their complaint with the Department of Insurance within the applicable time period. The patient and wife also argued that the cause of action was not time-barred because the statute of limitations prescribed for medical malpractice actions, Ind. The court held that a determination that the "occurrence" statute of limitations was unconstitutional was not necessary because the claim was time-barred even under the discovery rule.

Peterson v. State


No. 64A05-9703-PC-102


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


689 N.E.2d 1290; 1998 Ind. App. LEXIS 2



January 13, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellee's Transfer Granted February 18, 1998. On Petition to Transfer Granted May 6, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Ind. LEXIS 54.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE PORTER SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Roger V. Bradford, Judge. Cause No. 64D01-9311-CF-161.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Porter Superior Court (Indiana) denying his petition for post-conviction relief in which he sought reversal of his conviction for deliver of cocaine, a Class B felony. He claimed in part that double jeopardy principles barred his prosecution for the drug offense because he had previously received an Indiana Controlled Substance Excise Tax assessment for the same offense.


OVERVIEW: The revenue department assessed a CSET tax against defendant for the sale of cocaine. He also pleaded guilty to delivery of cocaine as a Class B felony. In a petition for post-conviction relief, he claimed that double jeopardy barred his conviction on the drug charge. The trial court denied relief, but the court reversed the judgment, ruling first that although defendant's time for appeals had expired, he was allowed to bring the petition. A new case had held that double jeopardy principles barred a prosecution for a particular drug offense after imposition of the CSET tax. Retroactive application of new criminal procedure rules was permitted when they prohibited a certain category of punishment for a class of defendants because of their status or offense. Because the prosecution of defendants assessed a CSET for the same drug offense had been prohibited for that reason, the rules applied retroactively. Further, because the assessment constituted a punishment for double jeopardy purposes, it was error to independently analyze whether the tax was a punishment. The trial court also failed to consider all four relevant factors in determining whether the tax constituted a punishment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment denying defendant's petition for post-conviction relief, and it remanded the case with instructions to grant the petition and vacate the conviction.

Hoovler v. State

December 17, 1997, Filed

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers appealed a judgment from the Tippecanoe Circuit Court (Indiana), which, on remand, rejected their constitutional challenge to an income tax statute, 1994 Ind. Acts 44.


OVERVIEW: The challenged statute authorized an increase in the economic development income tax in Indiana counties and cities falling within certain narrowly defined population ranges. Only one county fell within this range, and the taxpayers contended that the imposition of the tax violated several of their state and federal constitutional rights. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that the tax was constitutional. The court found that the legislation was confined to one subject as required by Ind. Const. art. IV, § 19. The court held that the creation of local entities for the purpose of public improvements did not violate the prohibition against the creation of corporations by special act in Ind. Const. art. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment finding the challenged statute valid.

Baxter v. State


No. 57A03-9701-PC-17


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


689 N.E.2d 1254; 1997 Ind. App. LEXIS 1762



December 15, 1997, Decided  
December 15, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE NOBLE COUNTY SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Kevin P. Wallace, Special Judge. Cause No. 57D01-8910-CF-8.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the Noble County Superior Court (Indiana), which partially denied his petition for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of two counts of child molesting and two counts of incest. He was also found to be an habitual offender and was sentenced for an aggregate term of 30 years. His convictions were upheld on direct appeal. Defendant then filed a petition for post-conviction relief. The post-conviction court vacated one of defendant's habitual offender enhancements and his two incest convictions, but denied relief in all other respects. On appeal, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court held that: (1) a caselaw decision which prohibited the exclusion of alibi testimony by defendants was not retroactively available to defendant; and, (2) defendant waived his complaint that the trial judge erred by failing to instruct the jury on the definition of prior unrelated felony, since he did not tender a proposed instruction or raise the issue on direct appeal. However, the court also held that it was fundamental error not to instruct the jury on "prior unrelated felony;" therefore, counsel's failure to raise this issue on appeal constituted ineffective assistance of appellate counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision concerning defendant's alibi testimony and the trial court's failure to instruct the jury on the definition of prior unrelated felony, but reversed on the issue of ineffective assistance of appellate counsel. The court remanded the action for a retrial of the habitual offender allegation.

 

852 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Land


Consolidated No. 79A02-9705-CR-282


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


688 N.E.2d 1307; 1997 Ind. App. LEXIS 1750



December 11, 1997, Decided  
December 11, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellee's Transfer Denied February 18, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: CONSOLIDATED APPEALS FROM THE TIPPECANOE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Ronald E. Melichar, Judge. Cause Nos. 79C01-9610-CF-17 and 79C01-9702-CF-3.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed the decision of the Tippecanoe Circuit Court (Indiana), which dismissed informations charging defendants with Nonsupport of a Dependent Child as a Class C felony. The trial court determined that Ind. Code § 35-46-1-5(a) (Supp. 1997) was an unconstitutional ex post facto law as applied to defendants.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with Nonsupport of a Dependent Child as a Class C felony under § 35-46-1-5(a), which provided that intentional nonsupport of a dependent child was a Class D felony, and was a Class C felony if the amount due and owing was at least $ 10,000. Defendants challenged the charges as violating ex post facto principles, arguing that their accrual of at least $ 10,000 in arrearages occurred before the law was enacted. The trial court dismissed the charges. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that § 35-46-1-5(a) was not an ex post facto law as applied to defendants because it did not punish them for past acts. Rather, the court explained, the law criminalized nonsupport, and the state had properly charged defendants with nonsupport that occurred after the law was enacted. The court further explained that defendants were not being punished for their past accrual of $ 10,000 in arrearages as a separate offense; the felony status of the underlying offense of nonsupport was merely being enhanced by reason of the amount of arrearages.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision, which dismissed the charges against defendants for nonsupport of a dependent child, and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

853 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Faver v. Bayh


No. 67A01-9607-CV-220


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


689 N.E.2d 727; 1997 Ind. App. LEXIS 1747



December 10, 1997, Decided  
December 10, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE PUTNAM CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Diana LaViolette, Judge. Cause No. 67C01-9407-CP-353.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoners sued appellee government officials in their individual and representative capacities, alleging that inmates in the protective custody unit (PCU) of a certain prison were treated differently from inmates in the general population, in violation of the United States and Indiana Constitutions and several Indiana statutes. The prisoners appealed the decision of the Putnam Circuit Court (Indiana), which ruled in appellees' favor.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the issues were whether the trial court erred when it concluded that: (1) the denial of "idle pay" to PCU inmates did not violate the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment; and (2) the State complied with Ind. Code § 11-10-5-1, which required the State to provide educational programs to inmates. The appellate court held that voluntary PCU inmates were entitled to receive "idle pay" to the same extent that it was provided to the general population and to those inmates involuntarily committed to PCU. Although the State had a legitimate government interest in withholding "state pay" from inmates who did not work or participate in education or vocational programs, the State failed to demonstrate a legitimate penological interest in providing such pay to some but not all inmates. In addition, the State violated the Indiana Code by denying education programs to PCU inmates. While Ind. Code § 11-10-5-1 did not impose an obligation to provide each program to each inmate or a right on the part of an inmate to gain access to each program, the statute mandated that access to some form of education program be provided to all inmates.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court was reversed.

 

854 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Board of Zoning Appeals v. Leisz


No. 53A01-9703-CV-82


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


686 N.E.2d 935; 1997 Ind. App. LEXIS 1567



November 12, 1997, Decided  
November 12, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition to Transfer Granted December 2, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Ind. LEXIS 597. Rehearing Denied January 6, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MONROE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Marc R. Kellams, Judge. Cause No. 53C02-9506-CP-789.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee landlords owned two student rental properties which were in nonconformance with local ordinances because they were rented to more than three adults. Appellant Bloomington, Indiana, Board of Zoning Appeals (BZA), appealed the judgment of the Monroe Circuit Court (Indiana), which granted a writ of certiorari relief from a decision of the BZA upon the application of the landlords.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the BZA raised several issues relating to housing code violations, grandfather registration, and continuous use. The appellate court concluded that the trial court correctly determined that the landlords' predecessor's failure to register the rental units under the housing code did not render the uses unlawful so as to work a forfeiture of the vested rights to the nonconforming uses. In addition, the trial court correctly determined that a vested property interest in a nonconforming use could not be forfeited by the mere failure to register it under a grandfathering provision. The trial court reversed the BZA's finding on the basis that the only evidence submitted showed the continuous occupancy of the rental units in nonconformity with the ordinance. The appellate court agreed that there was no evidence in the record that occupancy of the rentals dropped below four unrelated adults. Moreover, there had never been any contention that the landlords had ever intended to abandon the nonconforming uses. Therefore, the trial court correctly determined that the BZA's decision could not be sustained on the basis that the landlords failed to prove continuous nonconformity.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

855 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. Schrader


No. 49A02-9602-CV-00087


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


687 N.E.2d 370; 1997 Ind. App. LEXIS 1546



October 30, 1997, Decided  
October 30, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable David Rimstidt, Judge. Cause No. 49D05-9411-CP-1212.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Indiana Department of Family and Social Services, represented by its secretary and assistant secretary, sought review of a decision of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which granted summary judgment to appellee Medicaid recipients and invalidated a state Medicaid regulation.


OVERVIEW: The Medicaid recipients had medical problems that caused foot pain so severe they could not walk without orthopedic shoes. An amendment to state Medicaid regulations excluded coverage for these shoes. The recipients brought an action to enjoin the state from eliminating the shoe coverage and sought a declaratory judgment to invalidate the regulatory amendment. They then filed a summary judgment motion, based in part on affidavits in which their physicians attested that the shoes were medically necessary. The trial court concluded that the state Medicaid program was required to pay for medically necessary items and granted summary judgment. The trial court also stated that the decision of whether or not certain devices were medically necessary rested with the recipient's physician. The state appealed. The court affirmed and held that (1) the state had to cover medically necessary treatments in service areas in which the state opted to provide coverage; (2) the state, not the physician, defined medical necessity, so long as the definition comported with the federal Medicaid laws; and (3) the amendment eliminating coverage for medically necessary orthopedic shoes was invalid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision that Medicaid had to provide the medically necessary orthopedic shoes to the recipients.

 

856 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Burnett v. Villaneuve


No. 34A02-9610-CV-686


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


685 N.E.2d 1103; 1997 Ind. App. LEXIS 1403



September 30, 1997, Decided  
September 30, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE HOWARD CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Lynn Murray, Judge. Cause No. 34C01-9607-CP-00116.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant personal representative of estate sought review of a judgment from the Howard Circuit Court (Indiana) which denied appellant's motion to dismiss the claims of appellee creditors against the estate. Appellant contended that the claims were filed beyond the limitation period of one year from date of death contained in Ind. Code § 29-1-14-1 and were not subject to equitable tolling or waiver.


OVERVIEW: Appellant personal representative of the estate had opened the estate on the last day of the year following decedent's death with notice to all known creditors and by publication pursuant to Ind. Code § 12-1-7-7. Appellee creditors filed claims against the estate and appellant denied all the claims upon the ground that they were filed more than one year after decedent's death and barred pursuant to Ind. Code § 29-1-14-1. The trial court denied appellant's motion to dismiss appellees' claims because the limitation period was tolled to provide appellees time to file claims. The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, finding that the one-year limitation period was an absolute bar because all claims were subject to the one-year nonclaim provision found in Ind. Code § 29-1-14-1(d) and Ind. Code § 29-1-7-7(e). The court determined that, if commencement of the action was not within the specified time, the action and the right of action no longer existed. The court concluded that neither equitable tolling nor waiver were available, for Ind. Code § 29-1-14-1 was a nonclaim statute, as opposed to a general statute of limitation, and that the statute did not violate due process.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's denial of the motion of appellant personal representative to dismiss the claims of appellee creditors because the claims were filed beyond the one-year limitation period. The court determined that, even though the estate was opened on the last day of the year following decedent's death, the limitation period was not equitably tolled or waived, and the time period did not violate the due process clause.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with operating a vehicle while intoxicated (OWI). Defendant filed a pre-trial motion for a change in venue. Defendant's motion was denied. The Howard Superior Court (Indiana) convicted defendant and assessed defendant with $ 1,060 for jury fees. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had previously been convicted of reckless homicide following a motor vehicle accident. The local newspaper published an article intimating that the accident was alcohol-related. This coverage led defendant to request a change of venue. On appeal, defendant claimed that he was deprived of his right to a fair trial because the trial court denied his request to move the trial to another county. The court of appeals held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in refusing to move the trial to another county. The court of appeals found no abuse of discretion based on the jurors' assurances that they could be fair and impartial. Finally, defendant argued that the trial court's assessment of jury fees was unconstitutional. In reversing the assessment, the court of appeals noted that there was no statutory authority in Indiana for such an assessment.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for OWI was affirmed. The assessment against defendant for jury fees was reversed.

August 15, 1997, Filed

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The LaPorte Circuit Court (Indiana) denied appellant parents' motions to dismiss appellee grandparent's petition for visitation relating to their son. The parents challenged the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The parents of the child were not married, but the mother of the child's biological father was awarded visitation under the Grandparent Visitation Act (Act), Ind. Code § 31-1-11.7-1 et seq. After the mother married, her husband adopted the child. The parents argued that the trial court erred in denying their motions to dismiss the grandparent visitation petition for lack of jurisdiction. The parents also argued that the Act was unconstitutional. The court held that a grandparent's visitation rights survived adoption of the child by a stepparent. The court found that there was no evidence that the Act restricted the definition of stepparent to circumstances when the parent was previously married at the time of the child's birth. The court held that the Act was not unconstitutional under a rational basis test because the visitation rights did not impinge upon the integrity of the adoptive family.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Johnson v. Gupta

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sought review of a decision of the Porter Superior Court (Indiana), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee doctors in the patient's medical malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: After a doctor performed a hemorrhoidectomy and mucopexy on the patient in September 1990, the patient began experiencing fecal incontinence. Moore v. Liggins


No. 49A05-9512-CV-477


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


685 N.E.2d 57; 1997 Ind. App. LEXIS 1126



July 2, 1997, Decided  
July 2, 1997, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Barbara A. Collins, Master Commissioner. Cause No. S4-87-1622.

Reported in Table Case Format at: 1997 Ind. App. LEXIS 916.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ex-husband sought review of the judgment of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) that, in a Title IV-D enforcement action brought by appellee ex-wife, held the ex-husband in contempt of court for failing to pay child support.


OVERVIEW: In an action initiated by the ex-wife under the Title IV-D program, a master commissioner found the ex-husband in contempt for failing to pay child support. On appeal, the ex-husband raised several issues having to do with the validity of the order, whether the commissioner abused her discretion by failing to recuse herself, whether the procedure used was constitutional, and whether sufficient evidence supported the trial court's finding of contempt. The court held that, pursuant to state statute, the commissioner was specifically granted the authority to punish contempt under Ind. Code § 33-5.1-2-11(e). Also, the state had authority under Ind. Further, the court ruled that the ex-husband failed to establish an actual bias that would require the recusal of the commissioner. Finally, the court found that the constitutional proscription against imprisonment for debt was inapplicable because child support obligations did not constitute a debt. The evidence was sufficient to find that the ex-husband willfully neglected his duty although he had the financial ability to pay.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court, which held the ex-husband in contempt of court for failing to pay child support.

Maloney v. Cline


No. 49A02-9610-CV-679


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


682 N.E.2d 554; 1997 Ind. App. LEXIS 781



June 30, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Richard Huston, Judge. Cause No. 49D10-9602-CF-290.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Small claims plaintiff challenged a decision of the Marion Superior Court(Indiana), which, on defendants' appeal from the small claims court's denial of their motion to vacate default judgment, ordered plaintiff to replead her complaint within 20 days and dismissed her complaint on her failure to replead. Plaintiff claimed it was error to dismiss her cause of action without determining whether the defendants were required to file an appeal bond.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff obtained a default judgment in small claims court. Defendants' motion to set aside the default judgment was denied and they filed a notice of appeal. The appellate court ordered plaintiff to replead or risk dismissal; however, it did not require defendants to provide an appeal bond. Plaintiff did not replead, but filed a motion to dismiss the appeal based on defendants' failure to file a bond. Defendants moved to dismiss for failure to replead the complaint. The appellate court granted defendants' motion to dismiss and denied plaintiff's motion to correct errors. The court affirmed the dismissal. It found that appeals from the small claims action were to be tried de novo and that the phrase "de novo" contemplated repleading the case, even after an otherwise final judgment had been rendered. Further, plaintiff did not dispute that she was aware of the instruction. As such, the appellate court had the authority to require plaintiff to replead her cause or risk dismissal and properly dismissed her cause of action upon her failure to replead.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of plaintiff's small claims action by the appellate court when she failed to replead her cause as ordered by that court.

Indiana State Teachers Ass'n v. Board of Sch. Comm'rs


No. 49A02-9604-CV-194


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


679 N.E.2d 933; 1997 Ind. App. LEXIS 505



May 6, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable John L. Price, Judge. Cause No. 49D11-9509-CP-1494.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, teacher and teachers' associations, appealed a judgment from the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which upheld the constitutionality of Ind. Code § 20-3.1 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The Indiana legislature passed a law which provided for the reformation of the Indianapolis Public Schools (IPS). The bill contained limitations on the subject matter of collective bargaining and other provisions that affected IPS teachers. An IPS teacher and two teachers associations filed a complaint, claiming that the law, because it was not confined to one subject, violated Ind. Const. art. IV, § 19, and that Ind. On appeal, the court affirmed, concluding that although the legal connection between the budget of the state and a restriction on the right of IPS teachers to collectively bargain was tenuous, the statute contained only a single subject. Further, even though the law currently applied only to Marion County and IPS, it was not a special law in violation of Ind. Const. art. IV, § 23.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the constitutional of a statute that applied only to the school district in Indianapolis.

Winski Bros. v. Bayh


No. 49A04-9607-CV-271


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT

867 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mohler


No. 87A01-9605-PC-163


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


679 N.E.2d 170; 1997 Ind. App. LEXIS 495



April 30, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Transfer Granted September 12, 1997. On Petition to Transfer May 6, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Ind. LEXIS 52.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE WARRICK SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Edward A. Campbell, Judge. Cause Nos. 87D01-9311-CF-116. 87D01-9311-CF-117.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of the decision of the Warrick Superior Court (Indiana), which granted petitioner inmate's post-conviction relief petition and which vacated his convictions for possession and dealing in a controlled substance, as Class D felonies, because he had already been assessed a controlled substance excise tax for the same drugs.


OVERVIEW: The issue before the court was whether the rule announced in recent caselaw applied retroactively to cases on collateral review. The State supreme court had found that the Indiana Controlled Substance Excise Tax (CSET) was a punishment and, thus, a jeopardy for double jeopardy purposes, which attached at the moment of assessment. In defendant's case, the marijuana, which supported the CSET was the same marijuana which supported defendant's convictions for possession and dealing. The rule constituted a new constitutional rule of criminal procedure, and it was necessary to determine if any exceptions applied. The court noted that the rule prohibited the prosecution of a specific class of defendants because of their status or offense, for example those persons who had previously been assessed a CSET for the same drug. Therefore, the rule fell squarely within an exception and was accorded full retroactive effect. The rule applied retroactively to cases on collateral review and the post-conviction court correctly vacated defendant's convictions for possession and dealing in a controlled substance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

869 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Crowl v. Berryhill


No. 17A03-9603-CV-81


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


678 N.E.2d 828; 1997 Ind. App. LEXIS 382



April 10, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE DEKALB SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Kevin P. Wallace, Judge. Cause No. 17D01-8705-DR-61.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother appealed the order of the Superior Court of DeKalb County (Indiana), which held her in contempt for not complying with the trial court's visitation order in an action brought by appellee grandparents pursuant to the Grandparent Visitation Statute, Ind. Code § 31-1-11.7-1 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Appellant mother was found in contempt for violating a stipulated visitation order in an action brought by appellee grandparents under the Grandparent Visitation Statute (GVS), Ind. Code § 31-1-11.7-1 et seq. She argued that GVS was unconstitutional and therefore any order pursuant to it was not enforceable by contempt. The court refused to address the issue because only judgments void due to lack of jurisdiction were subject to collateral attack; the constitutionality of GVS had to be addressed on direct appeal. The mother's second argument was that GVS did not provide for temporary visitation orders. This was dismissed because the parties had agreed to the order; therefore, the error, if any, was invited error and would not be reviewed. The mother's final argument was that the grandparents should not have been awarded attorney fees because GVS did not expressly provide for them. The court held that although normally the courts did not award attorney fees in the absence of statutory authority, the trial court had inherent authority to do so for civil contempt actions. The court found no abuse of discretion by the trial court in holding the mother in contempt and affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that held appellant mother in contempt for violating a visitation order in appellee grandparents' action pursuant to the Grandparent Visitation Statute. The court held that the constitutionality of the statute was not subject to collateral review and was not a defense to contempt. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in finding contempt, and the other allegations of error were without merit.

Board of Sch. Trustees v. Barnell by Duncan


No. 18A02-9602-CV-101


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


678 N.E.2d 799; 1997 Ind. App. LEXIS 302



April 7, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE DELAWARE SUPERIOR COURT NO. 3. The Honorable Betty Shelton Cole, Special Judge. Cause No. 18D03-9511-CP-88.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, school board, school, and superintendent, sought review of a judgment of the Delaware (Indiana) Superior Court, which lifted appellants' expulsion of appellee student for bringing a Swiss army knife to school and ordered the student's reinstatement to school.


OVERVIEW: The student was expelled for bringing a Swiss army knife to school. The review court ordered the student reinstated to school on the basis that appellants unreasonably and arbitrarily expelled the student. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment and ordered the judgment vacated. The court held that the action was moot because the time during which the student was to have been expelled had passed. However, the court reviewed the issue because it was a question of significant public importance, which was likely to recur. Thus, the court held that the review court did not exceed its statutorily prescribed scope of judicial review under Ind. Code Ann. § 20-8.1-5.1-15 when it reversed the decision to expel the student. Ind. Const. art. 1, § 12 provided a right to judicial review of administrative decisions. Also, the scope of judicial review was properly limited by the standards set forth in the Administrative Orders and Procedures Act. However, the court concluded that appellants did not act in an unreasonable and arbitrary manner. In bringing the knife to school, the student violated a validly enacted rule under which students faced automatic expulsion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the review court's judgment lifting the student's expulsion and ordering his reinstatement to school. The court instructed the review court to vacate the judgment as a matter of record.

State v. Farber


No. 82A05-9509-CR-372


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


677 N.E.2d 1111; 1997 Ind. App. LEXIS 290



March 26, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellee's Transfer Denied June 30, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE VANDERBURGH SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable William J. Brune, Judge. Cause No. 82D02-9504-CF-139.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with murder and robbery. He filed a motion to suppress certain evidence, which was granted by the Vanderburgh Superior Court (Indiana). The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: The police suspected defendant of murdering a man. They questioned defendant's wife, who agreed to wear a body wire and talk to defendant about the crime. During the conversation, defendant made incriminating statements. He was then taken to the police station where he waived his rights, confessed to the crime, admitted where the murder weapon was and where items he stole from the victim were, and consented to the police obtaining his bags that contained blood-stained clothes. The police found the weapon and personal items of the victim and they searched the bag without a warrant. Defendant was charged with murder and robbery. He filed a motion to suppress the recorded conversation as well as all the other evidence he gave to the police. The trial court granted the motion. On appeal, the court affirmed the suppression of the recorded conversation on privilege grounds. However, because there was no Fourth Amendment violation in recording the conversation, the trial court improperly excluded all the other evidence under the fruit of the poisonous tree doctrine. The confession was not improperly coerced and the search was not the product of improper police conduct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the exclusion of a recorded conversation defendant had with his wife, but because there was no constitutional violation in recording the conversation, all other evidence was improperly excluded under the fruit of the poisonous tree doctrine. Thus, the court reversed as to the exclusion of such evidence.

Montgomery v. Estate of Montgomery


No. 75A03-9604-CV-133


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


677 N.E.2d 571; 1997 Ind. App. LEXIS 88



March 5, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE STARKE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable David P. Matsey, Judge. Cause No. 75C01-9306-EU-006.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed the trial court's denial of the petition for partial distribution and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant widower sought review of an order of the Starke Circuit Court (Indiana), which denied his petition for a partial distribution of his share of the real estate of his deceased wife's estate.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the trial court did not err in denying the widower's petition because a partial distribution under Ind. Code § 29-1-17-1 was at the discretion of the trial court and the estate had a legitimate legal dispute regarding the widower's share of the estate. The court held that the legislature intended that a surviving spouse taking against the will pursuant to Ind. Code § 29-1-3-1 should take his or her share of the net estate of both the personalty and the real estate. The court determined that the legislative intent of Ind. Code § 29-1-2-2 was to protect a portion of the widow's share of the decedent's real estate from creditors, except mortgage or lien creditors, but that § 29-1-2-2 did not exempt the widow's share from the expenses of administration and funeral expenses. The court found that there was no support for the differing treatment of widows and widowers as having a fair and substantial relation to the object of Ind. Code § 29-1-2-2. Although the court found that applying the protection of § 29-1-2-2 only to widows violated equal protection, the court held that the provisions of § 29-1-2-2 could be made applicable to all surviving spouses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the petition for partial distribution and remanded to the trial court.

Yater v. Hancock County Bd. of Health


CAUSE NO. 30A01-9605-CV-152


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property lots owners sought review of a decision by the Hancock Circuit Court (Indiana), which denied their petition for mandate in which they requested the trial court to compel appellees, Hancock County Board of Health and the Indiana State Board of Health, to issue permits for the construction of residential sewage disposal systems in their subdivision and/or award compensation for the regulatory taking of the lots.

Wallace v. Estate of Davies by Davies


No. 79A04-9603-CV-116


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


676 N.E.2d 422; 1997 Ind. App. LEXIS 78



February 27, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Transfer Denied September 5, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TIPPECANOE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable George J. Heid, Judge. Cause No. 79D02-9403-CP-30.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, city and police officer, challenged a jury verdict in favor of plaintiff widow rendered in the Tippecanoe Superior Court (Indiana). She was awarded damages in her action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 for the excessive force used against her husband that resulted in his death.


OVERVIEW: The decedent threatened suicide and the police were dispatched to his apartment. Once there, the decedent came out of the apartment with a shotgun in the "port arms" position. Fearing for his safety, the officer shot the decedent. The widow brought this action and alleged the use of excessive force. The jury awarded her damages and the city and officer argued on appeal that there was insufficient evidence to support the jury's verdict. The court affirmed the judgment. The jury could have found that, under the circumstances, the force that the officer used was unreasonable and that he violated the decedent's Fourth Amendment rights. The officer was not entitled to qualified immunity because the decedent's constitutional rights were sufficiently clear enough so that any reasonable officer would have understood that his actions in this instance violated those rights. The jury also could have concluded that the city's failure to have a policy on suicide intervention would likely have resulted in the deprivation of citizens' constitutional rights. Thus, the verdict against the city was also proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the widow.

Green v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT

January 30, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellants Motion for Transfer Denied April 16, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE NEWTON SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Daniel J. Molter, Judge. Cause No. 56D01-9509-CM-242 and 56D01-9509-DF-47.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant brought an interlocutory appeal from the decision of the Newton Superior Court (Indiana), which denied his motion to suppress evidence in his trial on charges of marijuana possession.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with possession of marijuana. Defendant filed a motion to quash the search warrant for a safe found in his studio and sought to have the items seized excluded. The trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress. Defendant filed a timely petition for interlocutory appeal, contending that the search of a safe removed from his studio constituted an invalid search and that the search warrant was constitutionally invalid because the issuing judge was not neutral and detached. The court found that a search warrant authorizing the search of defined premises also authorized the search of containers found on the premises which reasonably might have concealed items listed in the warrant. Accordingly, the court held that the initial warrant to search defendant's studio authorized the search of the safe. The court concluded that contact or knowledge by a judge obtained outside the setting of a formal hearing did not per se invalidate a search warrant, and defendant failed to offer any evidence of bias or prejudice on the part of the issuing judge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion to suppress.

Ford v. Madison-Grant Teachers Ass'n


No. 27A02-9602-CV-102


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


675 N.E.2d 734; 1997 Ind. App. LEXIS 7



January 15, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Transfer Denied May 29, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE GRANT SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Thomas G. Wright, Judge. Cause No. 27D02-9311-CP-281.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant non-members sought review of the summary judgment entered by the Grant Superior Court (Indiana) in favor of appellee union in the non-members' action challenging the fair share fee provision contained in a collective bargaining agreement (CBA). The trial court also denied the non-members' cross-motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The union was the exclusive bargaining representative for a school corporation's teachers. Their CBA imposed a fair share fee on teachers that did not belong to the union. The union also adopted an internal remedy providing for a pro rata refund of the fair share fee. The non-members challenged the validity of the fair share fee provision. The trial court entered summary judgment in favor of the union. The non-members appealed from that judgment, which was reversed. The trial court was instructed to grant the non-members summary judgment on remand. The court noted that requiring nonunion employees to support a union impacted their First Amendment rights. Therefore, only those activities that were germane to the collective-bargaining process were chargeable to nonunion employees. Furthermore, a union bore the burden of establishing that its procedures dealing with fair share fees were tailored to minimize the infringement on First Amendment rights. Therefore, the court found that the rebate provided by the union was insufficient because it did not ensure that the non-members' funds would not be used temporarily for ideological purposes unrelated to collective bargaining.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's entry of summary judgment in favor of the union. The trial court was instructed to enter summary judgment in favor of the non-members on remand.

Martin v. Richey


No. 53A04-9603-CV-104


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


674 N.E.2d 1015; 1997 Ind. App. LEXIS 1



January 13, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellee's Motion for Rehearing Denied June 10, 1997. Appellee's Transfer Granted May 8, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MONROE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Douglas R. Bridges, Judge. Cause No. 53C05-9505-CP-585.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sought review of a grant of summary judgment from the Monroe Circuit Court (Indiana) in favor of appellee physician. The trial court determined that the patient's malpractice claim against the physician was barred by the two-year medical malpractice statute of limitations, Ind. Code § 27-12-7-1(b), because she had not proven that the statute was tolled by the physician's active fraudulent concealment.


OVERVIEW: The patient's malpractice claim against the physician alleged that he was negligent in his care and treatment due to his failure to diagnose and treat her breast cancer in a timely manner. The physician had treated a lump in the patient's breast, after which he did not treat her again. Over three years later, the patient discovered that she had breast cancer and had to undergo a mastectomy. The patient argued that the malpractice statute of limitations applied against her was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court agreed and declared that Ind. Code § 27-12-7-1(b) was unconstitutional because, unlike the general tort statute of limitations, it began to run at the occurrence of the alleged negligence rather than at the discovery of the alleged negligence. The court held that such disparate treatment of medical malpractice victims from other tort victims was against Ind. Const. art. I, § 23. The court also held that Ind. Code § 27-12-7-1(b) violated Ind. Const. art. I, § 12, the "open courts" provision, because it effectively abrogated the right to a complete tort remedy. The court also found a genuine issue of material fact regarding the physician's alleged fraudulent concealment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's grant of summary judgment to the physician and held that the medical malpractice statute applied to the patient's claim violated the state constitution.

Fields v. State


No. 49A02-9503-CR-151


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


674 N.E.2d 613; 1996 Ind. App. LEXIS 1737



December 31, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellee's Petition to transfer Granted May 13, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Ind. LEXIS 72.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MARION MUNICIPAL COURT. CRIMINAL DIVISION, ROOM NO. 9. The Honorable Charles A. Wiles, Judge. Cause No. 49F09-9409-CF-116396.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Marion County Municipal Court, Criminal Division (Indiana), which convicted him of operating a motor vehicle while his driving privileges were suspended as an habitual violator of traffic laws as a class A misdemeanor, a violation of Ind. Code § 9-30-10-16 (1991).


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the evidence was insufficient to prove that he knew his driving privileges had been suspended as an habitual traffic offender because the notice of suspension was inadequate. The court agreed and reversed. The court stated that the State must present evidence that demonstrated that a letter of suspension was mailed to defendant's last known address in order to prove such notice. Moreover, the address must have been defendant's last known address as of the date upon which the letter of suspension was mailed. The court held that in order to convict an individual of the offense of driving while an habitual offender of traffic laws the State had the burden of proving that the individual knew of his suspension. When the bureau of motor vehicles had notice that an individual resided at a more current address than one listed in its records, the more current address was in fact an individual's last known address, and it could not ignore this information and rely upon outdated records. To predicate an inference of knowledge of suspension upon a letter mailed to an address other than an individual's last known address defeated the purpose of the notice requirement.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

Hammond v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who was charged with two counts of dealing in a schedule I controlled substance, as a class B felony and one count of possession of paraphernalia, as a class A misdemeanor, sought review of the judgment from the Perry Circuit Court (Indiana) that denied defendant's motion to suppress the State's evidence against her on the grounds that it was the result of an unlawful arrest, search and seizure.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with two counts of dealing in a schedule I controlled substance, as a class B felony and one count of possession of paraphernalia, as a class A misdemeanor. Defendant filed a motion to suppress certain evidence. The trial court denied the motion to suppress and defendant filed an interlocutory appeal. Defendant contended that Ind. Code § 9-25-8-2 had been amended or that the arrest was a pretense for searching defendant's purse. The court concluded that defendant was not arrested for a chargeable offense and that the evidence seized following her unlawful arrest is inadmissible.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that denied defendant's motion to suppress the State's evidence against defendant. Further, the court remanded the matter.

 

881 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State v. D.M.Z.


No. 73A01-9603-CR-87


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


674 N.E.2d 585; 1996 Ind. App. LEXIS 1713



December 16, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Case Name Amended by the Court January 7, 1997. Appellants Motion for Transfer Denied February 19, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SHELBY SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable James K. Coachys, Special Judge. Cause No. 73D01-9502-CF-7.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed the judgment of the Shelby County Superior Court (Indiana), which granted defendant's motion to dismiss the information charging him with three counts of seducing a 16-year-old male. The state asserted that the trial court erred in holding that the county youth shelter was not a foster care facility and that defendant was not a custodian of the victim.


OVERVIEW: The child seduction statute defined "custodian" as a person responsible for a child's welfare. The state claimed that as a child-care worker, defendant was a "custodian" as defined by the statute. Defendant countered that the trial court correctly held that a custodian was a person in a position of authority similar to that of an adoptive parent, adoptive grandparent, guardian, or stepparent. The court turned to the rules of statutory construction to resolve the question. The court found the term custodian was used together with guardian, adoptive parent, adoptive grandparent, and stepparent. The grouping of "custodian" with these terms and the definition of responsible indicated a legislative intent that as used in the statute "custodian" meant an individual who occupied a position of trust, authority and responsibility in loco parentis. Here, the state's evidence showed that defendant was a staff employee. The court held that to be a "custodian" within the meaning of the child seduction statute, an individual had to exercise more than limited or occasional supervision over a child. Because defendant was not responsible for the child's welfare, the charges were properly dismissed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's determination that the three charges of child seduction be dismissed.

Anderson v. State


No. 20A03-9605-CR-178


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


674 N.E.2d 184; 1996 Ind. App. LEXIS 1608



December 3, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ELKHART SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Donald W. Jones, Judge. Cause No. 20D01-9006-CF-64.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed from a decision of the Elkhart Superior Court (Indiana) denying his request for post-conviction relief. He contended that his conviction of aggravated battery as a Class B felony pursuant to Ind. Code § 35-42-2-1.5 violated the proscriptions contained in Ind. Const. art. I, § 24 and U.S. Const. art. 1, § 10, cl. 1 against ex post facto laws.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of attempted murder for shooting his girlfriend's father. After petitioner's conviction was set aside he was retried and found guilty of aggravated battery as a Class B felony, a violation of Ind. Code § 35-42-1-1.5. The trial court denied petitioner's request for post-conviction relief and, on appeal, the court reversed. The court vacated petitioner's conviction on the ground that § 35-42-1-1.5 was an unconstitutional ex post facto law because it was not in effect at the time of the shooting and it made the crime of aggravated battery greater than when it was committed and imposed additional punishment, in that § 35-42-1-1.5 provided for elevation of battery to a Class B felony, whereas the earlier battery statute, Ind. Code § 35-42-1-1, had not. The court further held that retrial for attempted murder was precluded by the prohibition on double jeopardy contained in the Fifth Amendment and in Ind. Code § 35-41-4-3(a)(1). The court held, however, that petitioner could be tried for the different offense of battery with a deadly weapon and that the evidence justified convicting him of that offense without retrial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment denying petitioner's request for post-conviction relief, vacated petitioner's conviction of aggravated assault as a Class B felony and his sentence, and remanded the case with instructions to enter judgment and sentence on the offense of battery with a deadly weapon, a Class C felony, a lesser included offense of attempted murder.

Baseball, Inc. v. Indiana Dep't of State Revenue

884 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Seay v. State


No. 82A01-9604-PC-139


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


673 N.E.2d 475; 1996 Ind. App. LEXIS 1511



November 8, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Transfer Granted January 15, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE VANDERBURGH CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Richard L. Young, Judge. Cause No. 82C01-9009-MI-2477.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate challenged the judgment of the Vanderburgh Circuit Court (Indiana) that denied his petition for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of dealing in a schedule II controlled substance and dealing in cocaine. His sentence was enhanced based on a finding that he was a habitual offender. The convictions and sentence were affirmed. The trial court denied the inmate's petition for post-conviction relief. Affirming, the court found that the trial court did not commit fundamental error when it instructed the jury during the habitual offender proceeding that it was restricted to determining the facts only and not the law. Although the instructions violated Ind. Const. art. I, § 19, which gave to the jury the right to determine the law and the facts in all criminal cases, they did not make it impossible for the inmate to have a fair hearing. Because the trial court gave 25 instructions addressing alleged prior convictions, the definition of "felony conviction," and the sequence of events required to support a habitual offender finding, the court was not convinced that the inmate's sentence was clearly wrong. The inmate was not denied effective assistance of counsel because it was not likely that, without the challenged instructions, the result of the proceeding would have been different.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of post-conviction relief.

 

885 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Dubois County Office of Family & Children v. Adams


No. 19A01-9603-CV-100


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


671 N.E.2d 202; 1996 Ind. App. LEXIS 1443



October 22, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE DUBOIS JUVENILE COURT. The Honorable Marvin D. Stratton, Special Judge. Cause No. 19C01-9503-JM-53.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and remanded for proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the Dubois County Office of Family and Children (DCOFC) and others, sought an interlocutory appeal of a judgment of the Dubois Juvenile Court (Indiana), which denied appellants' motion to dismiss appellee licensed foster parent's petition to expunge the juvenile court records relating to the foster parent.


OVERVIEW: The foster parent and his wife were both licensed foster parents. The foster parent was accused of molesting two children for whom his wife was babysitting. An investigation by the DCOFC and the police department substantiated the accusations. No criminal charges were filed against the foster parent but one foster child was removed from the home and no children were placed there. The foster parent filed a petition to expunge the juvenile court record pertaining to the alleged child molestations. Appellants' motion to dismiss was denied. On interlocutory appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court held that Ind. Code § 31-6-8-2(b) gave the juvenile court jurisdiction to order the expungement of records relating to a person's involvement in juvenile court proceedings. However, neither the children who accused the foster parent of molesting them nor the child removed from the home was involved in any juvenile court proceedings. Thus, the juvenile court lacked jurisdiction to order the expungement of records relating to the children. Consequently, it was error to deny appellants' motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded for proceedings consistent with the court's opinion.

 

886 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Ferguson v. State


No. 10A01-9502-CR-37


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


670 N.E.2d 371; 1996 Ind. App. LEXIS 1241



September 17, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Transfer Denied November 20, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CLARK CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Daniel F. Donahue, Judge. Cause No. 10C01-9312-CF-77.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision from the Clark Circuit Court (Indiana), which convicted him of murder and conspiracy to commit murder. Defendant asserted that the trial court violated his right to a compulsory process.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was 16 years old when the primary co-conspirator enlisted him and another of his friends to murder the primary co-conspirator's former lover, in exchange for the life insurance proceeds from the policy held on victim's life. At trial, all four of defendant's co-conspirators testified against him, and he requested discovery with respect to all agreements entered into between the State and its witnesses. The trial court granted an order compelling the State to provide that discovery and the deputy prosecutor was subpoenaed to testify for the defense with respect to any deals or understanding the State had with the primary co-conspirator to obtain her testimony. The trial court granted the State's motion to quash the subpoena and entered a protective order prohibiting the defense from calling the prosecutor as a witness. Defendant asserted that the trial court violated his right to a compulsory process. The court reversed defendant's convictions, holding that the trial court abused its discretion in quashing defendant's subpoena to obtain the deputy prosecutor's testimony which, in turn, violated his right to compulsory process, resulting in the denial of due process of law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's convictions for murder and conspiracy to commit murder.

Lake County Juvenile Court v. Swanson


No. 64A03-9512-CV-396


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


671 N.E.2d 429; 1996 Ind. App. LEXIS 1256



September 16, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellee's Rehearing Denied October 24, 1996. Appellants and Appellee's Motion for Transfer Denied April 14, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: INTERLOCUTORY APPEAL FROM THE PORTER COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Raymond D. Kickbush, Presiding Judge. Cause No. 64D05-9301-CT-165.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, county entities, state entities, and government employees, sought review, by interlocutory appeal, of an order from the Porter County Circuit Court (Indiana), which denied defendants motions for summary judgment on the 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim and state tort law claim filed by plaintiffs, juvenile and his parents, for an injury the juvenile sustained in pre-trial detention.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile and his parents filed a §1983 claim and state tort claim against various government entities and employees arising out his assault and rape by another inmate in the juvenile detention center. All defendants filed motions for summary judgment. The trial court denied the motion to all parties on both claims. On appeal, the court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded. The court held, among other things, that: (1) the juvenile court and the judge, in her official capacity, were not "persons" under § 1983; (2) plaintiffs' did not provide a formal written policy or informal custom of the county which caused the alleged constitutional violation under § 1983; and (3) the county did not establish whether its failure to provide funding to the juvenile detention center was a discretionary planning function which entitled it to immunity on the state tort claim. The court found that the § 1983 action and the state tort action could proceed against the juvenile detention officers. On the state tort claim, the court remanded for a determination of whether the county engaged in a discretionary decision-making process regarding allocation of funds for the juvenile center.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order, in part, and granted summary judgment for the juvenile court, the judge, and the county on plaintiffs' § 1983 claim. The court also reversed the denial of summary judgment to the juvenile court and judge on the state tort claim. The court affirmed the denial of summary judgment to the juvenile detention officers on the § 1983 claim and for the county and detention officers on the state tort claim.

Reinking v. Metropolitan Bd. of Zoning Appeals


No. 49A04-9512-CV-462


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


671 N.E.2d 137; 1996 Ind. App. LEXIS 1231



September 13, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Rehearing Denied November 7, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT NO. 7. The Honorable Gerald S. Zore, Judge. Cause No. 49D07-9504-MI-0569.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner landowners appealed the decision from the Marion Superior Court No. 7 (Indiana), which upheld the decision of respondent Metropolitan Board of Zoning Appeals to deny the landowners' petition for variance.


OVERVIEW: After a dwelling district ordinance was passed, the landowners purchased the lot and filed a petition for variance. The zoning board refused the landowners' petition, and the superior court affirmed the zoning board's decision. On appeal, the court affirmed. The landowners lacked standing to raise the argument that the zoning board had unconstitutionally taken their property when it enacted the dwelling district ordinance because the alleged taking had occurred before they had bought the lot. The landowners' knowledge of zoning restrictions prior to their purchase of the lot was insufficient to bar their petition for variance. The zoning board, however, acted within its discretionary powers when it denied the landowners' petition for variance. The zoning board's decision was orderly, judicious, and fundamentally fair.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's decision to uphold the zoning board's decision to deny the landowners' petition for variance.

Gorka v. Sullivan


No. 49A02-9507-CV-385


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


671 N.E.2d 122; 1996 Ind. App. LEXIS 1064



August 14, 1996, Filed

Transfer denied by Gorka v. Sullivan, 683 N.E.2d 580, 1997 Ind. LEXIS 325 (Ind., 1997)
Related proceeding at Roob v. Fisher, 2006 Ind. App. LEXIS 2318 (Ind. Ct. App., Nov. 8, 2006)

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, Medicaid recipients, a taxi company, and a certified class of common carriers (common carriers) challenged an order of the Marion Superior Court ( Indiana), which entered summary judgment in favor of appellees, social services agency and related officials (agency).


OVERVIEW: Common carriers filed a complaint against the agency, challenging new rates for transportation of Medicaid recipients. Common carriers alleged that the new rates violated state and federal law. The parties all filed for summary judgment. The trial courts, state and federal, granted summary judgment in favor of agency. Common carrier appealed both decision and the cases that were consolidated for appeal. The court determined that the federal Medicaid Act did not preempt the filed rate provisions of the Indiana Motor Carrier Act. The court also held that agency had not demanded common carrier services within the meaning of the just compensation provision in the Indiana Constitution and that the agency had not taken the common carriers' property within the meaning of the just compensation provision of the Indiana Constitution.
