Greer v. State


No. 57A03-9510-CR-333


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


669 N.E.2d 751; 1996 Ind. App. LEXIS 943



July 25, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Transfer Granted October 15, 1996. On Petition to Transfer Granted October 16, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Ind. LEXIS 161.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE NOBLE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Stephen S. Spindler, Judge. Cause No. 57D01-9101-CF-3.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Noble Superior Court (Indiana), which revoked defendant's probation for child molestation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of child molestation and sentences to eight years imprisonment. Later, defendant's sentence was modified to probation. Defendant's probation was revoked after a report that defendant had violated the terms of his probation by drinking alcohol. Defendant filed a motion for credit for the time he spent on home detention. The motion was denied, and defendant sought review of the revocation of his probation and the denial of his credit motion. Defendant argued that he received ineffective counsel, and that denial of credit time violated the state and federal constitutions' provisions of equal protection. The court found that it had jurisdiction over defendant's appeal even though his praecipe was not timely filed because the state failed to object prior to filing its appellate brief, that defendant failed to show that if his counsel had objected to a probation officer's statement, that it would have been sustained, and that home detention as part of defendant's probation was a benefit to defendant and did not violate due process or equal protection rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the revocation of defendant's probation and the denial of defendant's motion for credit time.

 

891 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Long v. State


No. 82A01-9511-CR-367


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


666 N.E.2d 1258; 1996 Ind. App. LEXIS 776



June 12, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended June 20, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE VANDERBURGH SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Maurice O'Connor, Judge. Cause No. 82D02-9506-CM-287.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant nude dancer brought a permissive interlocutory appeal from the decision of the Vanderburgh Superior Court (Indiana), which denied her motion to dismiss the public indecency charges brought against her pursuant to Ind. Code § 35-45-4-1.


OVERVIEW: The nude dancer was arrested and charged with public indecency, pursuant to Ind. Code § 35-45-4-1(a), after police officers observed her dancing completely nude on stage at a club. The nude dancer filed a motion to dismiss the charges in the trial court, which was denied. The nude dancer brought a permissive interlocutory appeal from the decision of the trial court and claimed that the club was not a public place as required by Ind. Code § 35-45-4-1(a). On appeal, the court affirmed the decision of the trial court and found that the club was a public place because it was open to the public and patrons were able to enter at will. Also, the court determined that the club's attempt to restrict access to members were insufficient to convert a public place into a private club. The court found that the club did not have any attributed of self-government, membership participation or ownership typically associated with a private club. Also, the court found that while private areas may exist within a public place, the nude dancers actions occurred before a group of people and although they desired to see her performance, the state had a valid interest in prohibiting an immoral activity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the nude dancer's motion to dismiss the public indecency charges because the events that resulted in the charges occurred within a public place.

Reeves v. State


No. 71A05-9509-CR-352


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


666 N.E.2d 933; 1996 Ind. App. LEXIS 772



June 4, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ST. JOSEPH SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Jerome Frese, Judge. Cause No. 71D01-9412-CF-1259.



DISPOSITION: Reeves's conviction is vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the St. Joseph Superior Court (Indiana), which convicted him of carrying a handgun without a license within 1000 feet of school property in violation of Ind. Code §§ 35-47-2-1, 35-47-2-23(c)(1)(b).


OVERVIEW: Defendant and another juvenile were standing on a street corner near a school. When the arresting officer drove by, defendant waved, but the other juvenile looked at the ground and glanced at the officer several times as he passed. The arresting officer became suspicious because of the inconsistent reactions to his presence and stopped the two juveniles. He discovered a gun when he frisked defendant. Defendant's motion to suppress the physical evidence was denied. On appeal, defendant argued that the stop and subsequent pat down violated his Fourth Amendment rights under the United States Constitution. Vacating the conviction, the court held that the juveniles' actions in reaction to the officer's presence were not sufficiently specific and articulable facts indicative of criminal activity. Therefore, the officer did not have a reasonable suspicion at the time of the stop and the gun discovered could not be used against defendant. The court found that without the gun, there was no crime.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's conviction for carrying a handgun without a license within 1000 feet of school property after the handgun found during an illegal stop could not be used against him.

Manns v. Skolnik


No. 53A05-9509-CV-351


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


666 N.E.2d 1236; 1996 Ind. App. LEXIS 755



May 30, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MONROE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable E. Michael Hoff, Judge. Cause No. 53C01-9410-CP-01118.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner advisor brought an action against respondents, the securities commissioner, the secretary of state, and the State, after the Indiana Securities Division found that she had violated securities registration and licensing requirements and anti-trust provisions. The Monroe Circuit Court (Indiana) affirmed the Indiana Securities Division's order. The advisor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The advisor told an acquaintance that she knew of a good investment. The acquaintance signed an agreement and delivered her money, but the advisor did not return the investment or any profit. The Indiana Securities Division found that the agreement was a security, that the advisor had violated the registration and licensing requirements of Ind. Code §§ 23-2-1-3, 23-2-2-8, and that the advisor had violated the anti-trust provisions of Ind. Code § 23-2-1-12. The advisor sought review of the order in the trial court, but the trial court affirmed. On further appeal, the court also affirmed. Enforcement of Ind. Code § 23-2-2-1(k) was not fundamental error, and the advisor had failed to raise the issue of the statute's constitutionality at the trial court level. The trial court did not err in affirming the order that found that the agreement constituted a note subject to securities regulation. The Indiana Securities Division correctly found that the advisor violated registration and licensing requirements and anti-trust provisions. The advisor had violated Ind. Code § 23-2-1-12(2) even if she had not intended to defraud the acquaintance because she omitted material information.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision to affirm the Indiana Securities Division's findings that the advisor had violated securities registration and licensing requirements and anti-trust provisions.

Burton v. State


No: 49A02-9512-CR-719


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


665 N.E.2d 924; 1996 Ind. App. LEXIS 718



May 20, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE COURT. The Honorable Ruth Reichard, Judge. Cause No. 49F16-9411-CF-167375 and 49F16-9502-DF-15485.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the District Court of Marion County (Indiana), which, following a bench trial, found defendant guilty of stalking, Ind. Code § 35-45-10-5, invasion of privacy, § 35-46-1-15.1, and harassment, § 35-45-2-2.


OVERVIEW: After an attack, defendant's girlfriend obtained a permanent protective order but, based on several phone calls and a neighbor's observation of the defendant in the girlfriend's driveway, defendant was charged with one count each of intimidation, stalking, invasion of privacy, and harassment. In a bench trial, the trial judge found defendant guilty of stalking, invasion of privacy, and harassment, Ind. Code §§ 35-45-10-5, 35-46-1-15.1, 35-45-2-2. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions for stalking and harassment, holding that the evidence was sufficient to support the trial court's conclusion that defendant had the intent to harass, annoy or alarm and had no intent of legitimate conversation. The court further held that stalking and invasion of privacy each contained an element that the other did not, and thus, were not the same for double jeopardy purposes, U.S. Const. amend. V and Ind. Const. art. 1, § 14, however, because the same actions were the sole basis for the convictions of both offenses in the manner in which they were charged, double jeopardy principles barred conviction for both offenses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions for stalking and harassment but reversed and remanded to the trial court with instructions to vacate the conviction and sentence on the invasion of privacy charge.

Sublett v. State


No: 49A02-9506-CR-325


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


665 N.E.2d 621; 1996 Ind. App. LEXIS 719



May 20, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 7, 1996. Transfer Denied October 10, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. CRIMINAL DIVISION, ROOM 6. The Honorable Howard N. Bernstein, Judge Pro Tempore. Cause No. 49G06-9305-CF-54610.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision of the Marion Superior Court, Criminal Division (Indiana), which convicted defendant of one count of attempted murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant stabbed his former girlfriend and her sister multiple times and was charged with two counts of attempted murder. Defendant had requested and obtained the withdrawal of five different public defenders assigned to represent him. Five weeks prior to trial, a sixth public defender was appointed to represent defendant. Defendant argued that he was denied a fair trial because the manner in which the county public defender's office assigned cases to its counsel resulted in ineffective representation. In affirming the decision, the court found that a violation of a Sixth Amendment right arose only after a defendant had shown that he was prejudiced by an unfair trial. There was no allegation or proof that defendant's counsel rendered deficient performance or that defendant suffered any prejudice as a result of his counsel's performance at trial. Additionally, it was not an abuse of discretion to deny defendant's motion for a continuance. The continuance was requested so that defendant's counsel could explore a possible defense characterized as one of diminished capacity based upon his diabetic condition. Indiana did not recognize the separate legal defense of diminished capacity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

Knox County Rural Elec. Mbrshp. Corp. v. PSI Energy


No. 93A02-9406-EX-370


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


663 N.E.2d 182; 1996 Ind. App. LEXIS 339



March 21, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Transfer Denied September 18, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE INDIANA UTILITY REGULATORY COMMISSION. The Honorable John F. Mortell, Chairman. Cause No. 39587.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former electric supplier sought review of an order of the Indiana Utility Regulatory Commission (commission) stratifying its service territory and granting appellee new energy supplier the right to service appellee coal company's coal mining operation. The former electric supplier had petitioned the commission to modify the service area boundaries between the service territories pursuant to Ind. Code § 8-1-2.3-6(3).


OVERVIEW: The former electric supplier contended that the commission lacked the authority to stratify the territory because § 8-1-2.3-6(3) did not specifically provide for stratification. The new electric supplier and the coal company argued that the commission erred by holding that a customer who legally purchased electricity could not construct its own private distribution facility to transport the electricity across the boundary of two suppliers' service areas without violating Ind. Code § 8-1-2.3-4(b). After determining that public convenience and necessity favored allowing the new supplier to service the mine, the commission explained why it did not want to modify the boundaries using the traditional approach. The court affirmed, finding that it was within the commission's discretion to determine whether to change the boundaries and reflect the change upon the assigned service area maps. The commission based its decision to stratify on the erroneous assumption that the coal company could not privately distribute the electricity without violating the statute. However, the ability to stratify was well within the commission's discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the commission stratifying the former electric supplier's service territory and granting the new energy supplier the right to service the coal company's coal mining operation.

Indiana Wholesale Wine & Liquor Co. v. State ex rel. Indiana Alcoholic Bev. Comm'n


CONSOLIDATED No. 49A02-9406-CV-384


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


662 N.E.2d 950; 1996 Ind. App. LEXIS 209



February 27, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's and Appellee's Transfer Granted September 18, 1996.
Petition to Transfer Granted May 28, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Ind. LEXIS 65.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT, CIVIL DIVISION 5. The Honorable James S. Kirsch, Judge, and The Honorable David L. Rimstidt, Judge. 1 Cause No. 49D05-9108-CP-0871.


1  After judgment was entered in the trial court, Judge Rimstidt succeeded Judge Kirsch as Judge of Marion Superior Court, Civil Division 5.

.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee state alcoholic beverage commission (commission) brought a declaratory judgment action against appellant wholesaler and appellee permittees, seeking a judicial determination of the application of Ind. Code § 7.1-3-21-5 (1991). The Marion Superior Court (Indiana) rendered summary judgment, determining that the resolution of the issue should be left to the commission. All parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: Ind. Code § 7.1-3-21-5 (1991) prohibited the issuance of a wholesaler liquor permit to any corporate applicant unless 60 percent of the corporation's common stock was owned by Indiana residents. The commission sought a judicial declaration of the application of the resident ownership requirement to the wholesaler and the permittees. On appeal, the court held that the trial court erred by remanding the issue of interpretation of the ambiguous statute to the commission. The court held that the commission had standing to bring the action under Ind. Code § 7.1-2-8-3 and that the permittees had standing to participate in the action because they had some stake in the outcome. The court held that the resident ownership requirement violated the commerce clause of U.S. Const. art. I, § 8 because it facially discriminated against interstate commerce and the requirement had no nexus with the putative benefits of ensuring the qualification of permit holders and the increased ease of ensuring compliance with the state law and regulations. The court held that the statute did not serve a "core concern" of the Twenty-first Amendment and was therefore not saved by application of that amendment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and declared that Indiana's resident ownership requirement for corporate applicants for wholesale liquor permits violated the commerce clause.

Hackett v. State


No. 45A04-9506-PC-201


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


661 N.E.2d 1231; 1996 Ind. App. LEXIS 156



February 21, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 15, 1996


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable James L. Clement, Judge. Cause No. 4CR-20-175-72.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged a judgment of the Lake Superior Court (Indiana), which denied his petition for post-conviction relief, in which he challenged his convictions and sentences for two counts of murder in the first degree for which he received concurrent life sentences.


OVERVIEW: The inmate filed a petition for post-conviction relief, which was denied. The court affirmed. Because the jury instructions as a whole instructed the jury as to the elements of the robbery, appellate counsel was not ineffective for failing to allege that the inmate's trial counsel was ineffective because he failed to object to one particular final instruction. Moreover, appellate counsel was not ineffective for failing to raise on direct appeal the admission of the testimony of a rebuttal witness whose identity was not disclosed before trial because, at the time of the inmate's trial, the State was under no obligation to disclose the witness's identity. Furthermore, the inmate's ineligibility for parole under § 11-13-3-2(b)(3) because of his receipt of life sentences for two counts of murder did not violate his right to equal protection. There was nothing irrational about the legislative judgment that parole should be denied to any individual who committed two felonies generating life sentences. Moreover, a comparison of the inmate's life sentence to the determinate sentences of those convicted under the "new" penal code did not raise equal protection concerns.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Walker v. State


No. 34A02-9502-CR-96


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


661 N.E.2d 869; 1996 Ind. App. LEXIS 170



February 21, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE HOWARD SUPERIOR COURT #3. The Honorable Randy G. Hainlen, Judge. Cause No. 34D03-9408-CM-01494.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Howard Superior Court, No. 3 (Indiana) that after a bench trial convicted him of possession of marijuana, a violation of Ind. Code § 34-48-4-11 (1993). Defendant was sentenced to one year in prison and the suspension of his driver's license for 180 days. Defendant's prison sentence was suspended and his entire sentence was stayed pending appeal.


OVERVIEW: Police officer were dispatched to a tavern to investigate a fight involving weapons. A witness informed one of the officers that defendant had struck a bar employee with a pool cue. The officer conducted a patdown search of defendant's clothing and sensed an article in defendant's pants pocket, which he believed was a bag of marijuana. Defendant was subsequently convicted. On appeal, the court held that defendant's motion to suppress the evidence obtained during the search was properly denied. The court held that search did not exceed the scope of Terry and the "plain feel" doctrine. The officer's determination that the item was contraband was contemporaneous with his weapons search. Regarding the suspension of defendant's driver's license, the court followed a precedential state supreme court case, which held that license suspension under Ind. Code § 35-48-4-15 violated neither procedural due process nor substantive due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Person v. State


No. 49A04-9503-CR-99


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


661 N.E.2d 587; 1996 Ind. App. LEXIS 144



February 20, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Transfer Denied April 17, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MARION MUNICIPAL COURT. The Honorable Susan Macey Thompson, Judge. Cause No. 49F19-9409-CM-119347.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Marion Municipal Court (Indiana) for dangerous possession of a handgun, a Class A misdemeanor under Ind. Code § 35-47-10-5 (1995 Supp.).


OVERVIEW: Defendant engaged in furtive gestures when police stopped the car in which he was a passenger. After defendant exited the car, police found a handgun where defendant had been sitting. Defendant was convicted of dangerous possession of a handgun and appealed. The court affirmed. The court held that the state presented sufficient evidence to support defendant's conviction because constructive possession had been established where it was shown that defendant had the capability and intent to exercise dominion and control over the handgun. The court rejected defendant's constitutional challenges to § 35-47-10-5, which made a child's possession of a handgun a misdemeanor, and to Ind. Code § 35-47-10-8, which required a five-day sentence in addition to any other penalty. There was no violation of Ind. Const. art. I, §§ 16, 18 because the statutes were the legislature's reasonable determination of the penalties to be imposed. Nor was there a violation of Ind. Const. art. I, § 23, the privileges and immunities clause, because the special classification created was reasonably related to the legislation's subject matter and the purpose of deterring children from possessing handguns.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for dangerous possession of a handgun.

 

901 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Indiana High Sch. Athletic Ass'n v. Carlberg


No. 29A02-9412-CV-724


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


661 N.E.2d 833; 1996 Ind. App. LEXIS 148



February 19, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Transfer Granted October 24, 1996. On Petition to Transfer December 17, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Ind. LEXIS 230.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE HAMILTON CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Richard T. Payne, Special Judge. Cause No. 29C01-9410-CP-737.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state high school athletic association (association) appealed an order of the Hamilton Circuit Court (Indiana) enjoining the enforcement of the association's "Transfer Rule" against plaintiff high school student, who had transferred from a private high school to a public one for reasons unrelated to athletics without an attendant move by his parents.


OVERVIEW: The high school student sought to enjoin the state high school athletic association from imposing its Transfer Rule making him ineligible to participate on the varsity swimming team for the year following his transfer. The trial court enjoined the association from enforcing the Transfer Rule against the student and ordered that he be allowed to participate on the varsity swimming team. The association appealed. The court held that under binding supreme court precedent, the association's Transfer Rule was unconstitutionally overbroad in violation of the equal protection clause of the Fourteenth Amendment when applied to deny a student eligibility to participate in varsity athletics where the student had transferred from one high school to another for reasons unrelated to athletics. The court found that the association's application of its Transfer Rule was properly enjoined because the student had transferred for academic and financial reasons rather than athletic reasons. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment enjoining the state high school athletic association from imposing its Transfer Rule against the high school student.

Lincoln Utils. v. Office of Util. Consumer Counselor


No. 93A02-9504-EX-201


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


661 N.E.2d 562; 1996 Ind. App. LEXIS 137



February 13, 1996, Decided  
February 13, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 18, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE INDIANA UTILITY REGULATORY COMMISSION. The Honorable Scott Jones, ACALJ, Presiding. Cause No. 39956.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant utility challenged the Indiana Utility Regulatory Commission order denying its petition to increase its revenues by 19 percent. The utility asserted that the commission erred in excluding Contributions in Aid of Construction (CIAC) in determining its rate base, and that the 3.5 percent rate established was confiscatory. Appellee Office of Utility Consumer Counselor (consumer) asserted misinterpretation of Ind. Code § 8-1-2-6.


OVERVIEW: The utility petitioned the commission for approval of a 19 percent increase in its total revenues. At an evidentiary hearing, the consumer presented evidence of the CIAC to arrive at a negative rate base, and proposed a 2.95 percent increase. The commission authorized an across-the-board increase of 3.51 percent. The utility appealed, asserting that the commission erred in excluding the CIAC to determine the rate base, and that the approved rate was confiscatory. The court affirmed the commission's order. Relying on controlling precedent, it rejected the utility's proposition that Ind. Code § 8-1-2-6 did not differentiate between property that was purchased or contributed. The court concluded that the utility was seeking the ability to earn a profit on property for which it had paid nothing and held that this was an incorrect interpretation of § 8-1-2-6. The court further held that as the commission had not yet made a final determination respecting the rate of return on the base rate, the issue of confiscatory taking was not ripe for adjudication.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the commission setting the utility's rate increase at 3.5 percent in a proceeding seeking approval of a rate increase of 19 percent.

Hooks v. State


No. 49A04-9502-CR-57


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


660 N.E.2d 1076; 1996 Ind. App. LEXIS 38



January 31, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Transfer Denied March 21, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MARION MUNICIPAL COURT CRIMINAL DIVISION, ROOM NUMBER 5. The Honorable Clarence D. Bolden, Judge. Cause No. 49F05-9308-CM-102578.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Marion County Municipal Court (Indiana), which convicted him of disorderly conduct.


OVERVIEW: As defendant was entering his mother's house, a police officer asked to speak to him. Defendant refused the request. The officer ran a check on defendant's vehicle and discovered that it was not registered. When the officer prepared to have the vehicle towed, defendant and his brother came out of the house and began screaming obscenities at the officer. Defendant was asked to quiet down, but he persisted in shouting obscenities. The court affirmed the municipal court's judgment that convicted defendant of disorderly conduct. Speech was protected under the United States Constitution when it was aimed at protesting the actions of police rather than hindering or obstructing police duties or investigations. The disorderly conduct statute, Ind. Code § 35-45-1-3, was aimed at the intrusiveness and loudness of expression, not whether the content of the language was obscene or provocative. There was sufficient evidence to show that defendant's screaming infringed upon the peace and tranquility of others.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the municipal court's judgment.

Malone v. State


No. 20A05-9410-CR-398


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


660 N.E.2d 619; 1996 Ind. App. LEXIS 33



January 29, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Transfer Denied May 23, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE ELKHART SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Donald W. Jones, Judge. Cause No. 20D01-9309-CF-090.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Elkhart Superior Court (Indiana) that convicted him of burglary, a class B felony.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with burglary. To prove defendant guilty of burglary, the state had to demonstrate that he broke and entered the dwelling of the victim with the specific intent to commit a felony in the dwelling pursuant to Ind. Code § 35-43-2-1. Defendant was convicted of burglary by the trial court and he appealed. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. Defendant's trial counsel failed to object to certain testimony by the victim regarding the wallet on the basis of hearsay. The court held that the jury reasonably could have concluded that the wallet was in the bathroom with defendant because he had carried it in there from the owner's room after entering the apartment through her window. That would constitute the exercise of unauthorized control over the property and would suffice to establish the requisite intent. The court determined that defendant failed to demonstrate a reasonable probability that, had the statement not been admitted, there would have been insufficient evidence for the jury to find beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant broke into the apartment with the intent to commit theft.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that convicted defendant of burglary.

D.A.X., Inc. v. Employers Ins.


No. 49A04-9410-CV-397


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


659 N.E.2d 1150; 1996 Ind. App. LEXIS 9



January 12, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 15, 1996. Transfer Denied August 20, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT CIVIL DIVISION, ROOM 1. The Honorable Anthony J. Metz, III, Judge. Cause No. 49D01-9111-CP-1298.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insured challenged the order of the Marion Superior Court Civil Division (Indiana), which awarded judgment to appellee insurer in the insurer's action to recover additional premiums under a worker's compensation policy after an audit revealed that the premium had been incorrectly based on the wrong state's rates.


OVERVIEW: After the insured applied for worker's compensation through the Indiana Compensation Rating Bureau, the insurer was assigned to provide insurance to the insured. The premium rate was based on the insured's representations regarding its operations in Indiana. During an audit in which the insured failed to completely cooperate, the insurer discovered that Illinois was the proper state for the premium rate base, and it sought the additional premium. When the insured refused to pay, the insurer filed an action and obtained a judgment for the additional premium. The insured appealed, and the court affirmed, holding that the insured's contractual rights were not impaired by the retroactive rate because the insured never had a contractual right to the lower premium rate. The court disregarded the argument that the trial court improperly reformed the contract because it had enforced the provision regarding the final premium, not reformed it. Moreover, the insured failed to pursue the mandatory administrative remedy of Ind. Code § 27-7-2-20.3(c)(2) and was barred from contesting the non-Indiana rates.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the insurer in its action to recover additional premiums under a worker's compensation policy after an audit revealed that the premiums had been incorrectly based on the wrong state's rates.

 

906 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Starzenski v. City of Elkhart


No. 20A05-9502-CV-56


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


659 N.E.2d 1132; 1996 Ind. App. LEXIS 7



January 10, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Transfer Denied May 31, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE ELKHART SUPERIOR COURT ROOM NUMBER 2. The Honorable Stephen E. Platt, Judge. Cause No. 20D02-9302-CP-107.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners appealed the decision from the Elkhart Superior Court (Indiana), which refused to enter a preliminary injunction in favor of the property owners in their suit against defendants, city and related officials (city), to enjoin the cleanup of property. The property owners largely argued that they could collaterally attack the cleanup instituted under state procedures and that the cleanup was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The landowners' property was covered with debris, and the city took steps to clean up the property by holding a hearing under Ind. Code § 36-7-9-7. The landowners were ordered to clean up the property, they did not, a second hearing was held, the landowners were again ordered to remove the debris, and finally the city entered the property. The landowners could not collaterally attack the orders through injunctive relief but were required to appeal the cleanup orders pursuant to Ind. Code § 36-7-9-8. The landowners did not timely file an appeal under that statute. Written notice of the orders by the hearing authority was not required. The Fourth Amendment applied in a civil context. However, due process was afforded since there were several hearings, the hearing officer heard all the evidence, and the landowners failed to follow their appellate rights. The city acted within its police powers and was not required to provide just compensation. The city also acted reasonably in removing the debris. The rules related to the execution of a search warrant did not apply since the city was abating a nuisance, not executing a warrant.


OUTCOME: The denial of a premininary injunction to the landowners to block the cleanup of their property and the removal of debris was affirmed.

Nobles v. Cartwright


No. 49A02-9406-CV-331


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


659 N.E.2d 1064; 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 1634



December 21, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended January 22, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT CIVIL DIVISION, ROOM 3. The Honorable Frank M. Nardi, Special Judge. Cause No. 49D03-9009-CP-1375.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is reversed and the cause is remanded with instructions to enter judgment consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee employee filed an action for wrongful discharge, invasion of privacy, and breach of contract against appellant, the State Lottery Commission of Indiana (SLCI) and its agents, in the Marion Superior Court, Civil Division, Indiana. The trial court denied a motion for summary judgment by the SLCI and agents. The agents and SLCI appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee filed claims of sexual harassment against her boss who was a public official. Her statement, which the agents promised would be kept confidential and which detailed her extramarital affair with the official, was published. She was later terminated from her employment. The employee's complaint alleged wrongful discharge, invasion of privacy, and breach of contract. The SLCI and the agents contended that the trial court erred when it denied their motion for summary judgment. The court concluded that the trial court did err when it denied summary judgment. It would have been unreasonable as a matter of law for a trier of fact to have inferred that the employee was fired in retaliation for reporting the official's actions and not for the reasons outlined in her termination letter. The employee did not present a genuine issue of material fact with regard to the "legitimate public interest" element to prevail on a claim of public disclosure of private information. There were no genuine issues of material fact with respect to the breach of contract issue because the employee did not set forth specific facts to demonstrate a genuine issue for trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court that denied the motion for summary judgment of the SLCI and the agents was reversed and the cause was remanded with instructions to enter judgment against the employee.

Indiana High Sch. Ath. Ass'n v. Reyes


No. 79A02-9504-CV-175


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


659 N.E.2d 158; 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 1605



December 11, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Transfer Granted May 15, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TIPPECANOE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Donald C. Johnson, Judge. Cause No. 79D01-9502-CP-46.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, high school athletic association (association) and its commissioner, sought review of a decision of the Tippeecanoe Superior Court (Indiana), which enjoined the association from enforcing its "Eight-Semester Rule" against appellee high school baseball player and preventing him from participating in association-sponsored sports during his senior year in high school.


OVERVIEW: The student first enrolled in the ninth grade during the 1990-91 school year in Puerto Rico. Due to psychological problems, he did poorly academically and was forced to repeat the grade. He came to Indiana and competed for the high school team as a sophomore and as a junior. He requested that the association grant him an extra year of eligibility pursuant to its hardship rule. The association's executive committee denied the student's request. The student filed a complaint for injunctive relief. The trial court ruled in the student's favor, and the association appealed. The court reversed and held that: (1) the scope of review applied by the trial court was overly broad; (2) the association's refusal to grant the student an exception under the hardship rule was supported by the record; (2) the goals and purposes underlying the Eight-Semester Rule were legitimate, and the association's determination that at least some of those purposes and goals would be served by denying the student's application for an additional year of eligibility was not arbitrary and capricious; and (3) the hardship rule was constitutional and did not violate Ind. Const. art. I, § 23.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision allowing the high school athlete an extra year of eligibility.

 

909 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Virtue


No. 12A02-9503-CR-156


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


658 N.E.2d 605; 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 1420



November 17, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 26, 1996. Transfer Denied July 17, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CLINTON CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Jack R. O'Neill, Judge. Cause No. 12C01-9309-CM-42.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and remanded for proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed the decision from the Clinton Circuit Court (Indiana), which dismissed the indictment of defendant for violating Ind. Code § 35-49-3-1 for the distribution of obscene matter. The trial court held that the indictment violated the First Amendment and the Indiana Constitution's ban on the regulation of freedom of expression.


OVERVIEW: Defendant owned a movie video store that rented adult movies. Following the rental of one such movie, defendant was indicted. On appeal, the court ruled in favor of the state. First, in accordance with § 35-34-1-8 and related rules, defendant failed to file a proper motion to dismiss with supporting affidavits. However, since the state did not challenge the facts, the error was harmless. The right to possess obscene matter did not apply to the right to distribute obscene materials. The consenting adult standard did not apply to the distribution of obscenity. Thus, the First Amendment was not violated. Ind. Const. art. I, § 9 was not violated as well. Ind. Code § 35-49-2-1 defined obscenity in terms of contemporary community standards, not the standards of the persons who wished to view the materials. Thus, the fact that consenting adults rented obscene tapes was of no import. The nature of a videotape did not render the tape in question less obscene. The distribution of obscenity was determined by its content, not by its packaging. Thus, the fact that the obscenity was not viewed until a VCR was used did not render the tape non-obscene.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing the indictment was reversed and remanded. The distribution of obscenity was governed by a different standard than the right to the private possession of obscenity. The indictment of defendant for violating a distribution statute was not an unconstitutional violation of the right to freedom of expression.

 

910 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Y.A. v. BAYH


No. 49A05-9311-CV-00421


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


657 N.E.2d 410; 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 1403



November 8, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable James S. Kirsch, Judge. Cause No. 49D05-9010-CP-1571.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a class and sub-class that consisted of emotionally disturbed youths in need of residential services and those similar youths in the custody of the state, challenged a decision from the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which granted summary judgment to defendants, the Indiana Division of Mental Health and state officials, in the youths' complaint that sought long-term psychiatric residential care and therapeutic placements.


OVERVIEW: The youths alleged that Ind. Const. art. 9, § 1, and laws passed pursuant to that provision, imposed an obligation upon the state to provide residential services for members of a class of emotionally disturbed children, and that the state violated the due process rights of youths in state custody, by failing to provide them with adequate treatment in a residential placement. On appeal, the court affirmed summary judgment to the state, and held that the legislative intent of the applicable statutes was to limit services for the mentally or emotionally ill to those that were available under existing appropriations, and that whether or not an individual could receive treatment depended on the resources of the state. Limitations were imposed upon Const. art. 9, § 1 by a necessity to distribute and apportion available state funds for the welfare of all citizens. The Due Process Clause did not impose any affirmative right to governmental aid. States, state entities and state officials who were sued in their official capacities were not "persons" for purposes of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, and an exception for injunctive relief was not applicable as there were no constitutional violations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment in favor of the state.

American Legion Post # 113 v. State


No. 06A01-9501-CR-24


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


656 N.E.2d 1190; 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 1364



October 31, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Transfer Denied January 9, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE BOONE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Allen F. Wharry, Judge. Cause No. 06C01-9311-CF-42.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed its convictions from the Boone Circuit Court (Indiana) for unlawful gambling, promoting professional gambling, and professional gambling after it refused to remove gambling devices from its post.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was repeatedly warned that its gambling devices in its post were illegal. When defendant refused to remove the devices, the state police raided the post. Defendant was convicted of unlawful gambling, promoting professional gambling, and professional gambling. Defendant appealed, challenging the constitutionality of the prohibitions against gambling activities in Ind. Code §§ 35-45-5-2 to 35-45-5-4. The court affirmed defendant's convictions. The court held that the statutes did not violate Ind. Const. art. I, § 23 because the riverboat and pari-mutuel exceptions to the general prohibitions against gambling created particular forms of permissible gambling, not unlawful classifications of individuals who were allowed to participate in those forms of gambling. All individuals were allowed to engage in the permissible forms of gambling. Further, there were inherent distinctions between the state and other individuals to justify the state-run lottery. The court also concluded that defendant was not denied equal protection of the law under the Fourteenth Amendment and that regulation through the gambling statutes constituted a valid exercise of the state's police power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for unlawful gambling, promoting professional gambling, and professional gambling.

Robison v. Dana Corp.


No. 27A05-9502-CV-54


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT

October 24, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE GRANT CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Thomas R. Hunt, Judge. Cause No. 27C01-9304-CP-234.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff applicant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Grant County (Indiana), which affirmed defendant commission's ruling that reversed the recommendation of an Administrative Law Judge and held that defendant employer did not discriminate against the applicant on the basis of his disability when it rejected his application for employment.


OVERVIEW: The applicant, afflicted with cerebral palsy, applied for a machine operator's position with the employer, a job for which he had previous experience. The employer interviewed 20 persons for the position and selected three others. The applicant filed a complaint with the commission. The commission found that the applicant was not discriminated against. The applicant brought an action against the commission and the employer to contest the decision. Code § 4-21.5-5-14, judicial review of administrative agency decisions was limited to a determination of whether it was without jurisdiction, arbitrary, capricious, unconstitutional, unsupported by substantial evidence, or was in violation of statute; (2) the applicant had the burden of proof that he was denied employment because of his disability under Ind. Code § 22-9-1-2; and (3) the employer had discretion to choose among prospective employees as long as it did not apply unlawful criteria.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, in the applicant's action against the commission and employer, which affirmed the commission's decision that the applicant was not denied employment because of his disability.

Cundiff by Cundiff v. Daviess County Hosp.


No. 14A04-9501-CV-11


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


656 N.E.2d 298; 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 1313; 71 A.L.R.5th 759



October 12, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Transfer Denied March 15, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DAVIESS CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Robert L. Arthur, Judge. Cause No. 14C01-9407-MI-196.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, parents and child, sought review of a decision of the Daviess Circuit Court (Indiana), which granted defendant hospital's motion for summary judgment. The parents had filed a proposed complaint for damages on their child's behalf with the Indiana Department of Insurance.


OVERVIEW: The child's parents learned that the child's hearing loss was possibly caused by an overdose of antibiotics administered by the hospital. The hospital alleged that the parents' complaint was time-barred by Ind. Code § 27-12-7-1(b), and the trial court agreed. The court affirmed the trial court as to the federal and state due process and the federal equal protection arguments, and held that § 27-12-7-1(b) did not violate the due process rights of minors. The court reversed the order as to the state equal protection argument. The court held that Ind. Const. art. 1, § 23 should have been given independent interpretation and application, which revolved around the following analysis: § 27-12-7-1(b) had to be analyzed by first, the disparate treatment accorded by the legislation had to have been reasonably related to inherent characteristics which distinguished the unequally treated classes. Second, the preferential treatment had to have been uniformly applicable and equally available to all persons similarly situated. Finally, in determining whether a statute complied with or violated Ind. Const. art. 1, § 23, courts had to exercise substantial deference to legislative discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of the hospital's motion for summary judgment as to the federal and state due process and the federal equal protection arguments. The court reversed the grant of the hospital's motion for summary judgment as to the state equal protection argument.

DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought interlocutory review of the decision of the Howard Superior Court (Indiana) that denied her motion to dismiss the criminal prosecution against her for several counts of drug dealing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was being prosecuted for several counts of drug dealing and moved to dismiss because of the jeopardy assessment and collection of the Indiana Controlled Substance Excise Tax. The lower court denied her motion, but the court reversed and remanded with instructions that the prosecution be dismissed. PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged a judgment from the Lake County Superior Court (Indiana), which denied his request for post-conviction relief. He had been convicted of carrying a handgun without a license and was sentenced to an enhanced prison term due to his status as an habitual offender.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Tippecanoe County Circuit Court (Indiana), which convicted him of unlawful dealing in a controlled substance and of being a habitual criminal. The trial court denied his motion to correct an erroneous sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of unlawful dealing in a controlled substance and of being a habitual criminal. The trial court denied his motion to correct an erroneous sentence. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in sentencing him to life imprisonment under Ind. Code § 35-8-8-1, rather than 30 years under Ind. Code § 35-50-2-8. According to defendant, when the trial court sentenced him under the old statute, it violated Ind. Const. art. I, § 18. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that because the rule was that sentencing was governed by the date that the crime was committed, the trial court had not erred in sentencing him under the old statute.

Calumet Nat'l Bank v. AT&T


No. 64A03-9411-CV-409


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


654 N.E.2d 816; 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 1006



August 15, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 4, 1996. Appellant's Motion for Transfer Granted June 19, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Ind. LEXIS 85.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PORTER COUNTY. The Honorable Roger V. Bradford, Judge. Cause No. 64D01-9003-CP-593.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff trust appealed from a summary judgment of the Superior Court of Porter County (Indiana), which ruled in favor of defendant utilities. The trial court held that one utility's license with a railroad company to install a fiber optic cable over its right-of-way was enforceable against the trust, thus precluding a trespass action. The trial court found the other utility to be a third party beneficiary of the license.


OVERVIEW: The trust contended that despite the plain language of Ind. Code § 8-4-35-8(a), consideration of Ind. Code § 8-4-35-5 rendered the utility's license with the railroad invalid. The court disagreed and affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to the utilities. The court construed the language of the relevant statutory sections together and concluded that the trust, in whom the railroad's interest vested under Ind. Code § 8-4-35-5, did not obtain an enforceable interest in the right-of-way until it obtained and filed a quitclaim deed pursuant to Ind. Code § 8-4-35-6. Under Ind. Code § 8-4-35-8(a), the trust took title to the right-of-way subject to the utility's license. Because the utility entered the land by authority of a license agreement predating the trust's acquisition of record title in the right-of-way, no trespass occurred. The court also concluded that the unambiguous language of the license agreement sufficiently indicated that the contracting parties intended to benefit one of the utilities, thereby rendering that utility a third-party beneficiary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to the utilities in the trust's action for trespass.

 

918 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Dillon v. Chicago S. S. & N. B. Ry. (In re Train Collision)


No. 45A03-9402-CV-69


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


654 N.E.2d 1137; 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 1010



August 15, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 5, 1996. Transfer Denied December 18, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF LAKE COUNTY. CIVIL DIVISION, ROOM FIVE. The Honorable James J. Richards, Judge. Cause No. 45D05-9301-CT-110.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant passengers challenged an order of the Superior Court of Lake County (Indiana), which granted partial summary judgment in favor of appellee railroad on the passengers' claim for punitive damages in a class action.


OVERVIEW: After the crash of a train, a class of passengers brought an action against the railroad. The trial court granted partial summary judgment in favor of the railroad, and the passengers sought review. The court affirmed, holding that the Indiana Transportation Act, Ind. Code § 8-5-15-2, had been constitutional when it was enacted, and the railroad was a public commuter railroad created under that statute. Because the statute had been constitutional when enacted, it was not rendered unconstitutional by any subsequent act. The railroad, being a public railroad, was a political subdivision that was subject to governmental immunity. Finally, as a governmental entity, the railroad was not to be considered liable for punitive damages.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of partial summary judgment in favor of the railroad.

 

919 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. State


No. 82A04-9410-PC-427


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


654 N.E.2d 788; 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 964



August 9, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Transfer Denied October 11, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE VANDERBURGH CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Richard L. Young, Judge. Cause No. 82C01-9004-MI-2259.



DISPOSITION: We affirm.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Vanderburgh County (Indiana), which denied his petition for post-conviction relief. Defendant argued that his two life sentences for rape and kidnapping were cruel and unusual punishment and disproportionate under current standards and in light of subsequent changes made in the criminal statutes.


OVERVIEW: Defendant took a 10-year-old girl off to a corner of a public park and raped her. Fifteen years after his convictions he filed this motion. Recent changes in the criminal law would now classify the conduct for which petitioner was convicted of rape as a Class B felony, punishable by from 6 to 20 years. The conduct for which petitioner was convicted of kidnapping would now be classified as criminal confinement, a Class C felony. Petitioner argued that proportionality required that the sentences he received be compared with what he would now receive for the same conduct. The court held that it did not. A disproportionate sentence was one that no reasonable person could find appropriate. The court did not think that a life sentence for kidnapping or for the rape of a 10-year-old girl was cruel and unusual punishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

920 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Dunn v. Marion County Office of Family & Children (In re E.P.)


No. 49A05-9306-JV-235


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


653 N.E.2d 1026; 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 815



July 20, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT JUVENILE DIVISION. The Honorable James W. Payne, Judge. Cause No. 49D09-9208-JC-412, 413.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged the decision of the Marion Superior Court Juvenile Division (Indiana), which denied motions for court-appointed counsel and for a jury trial in an action filed by appellee welfare department alleging that the mother's children were in need of services.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court affirmed but remanded for a proceeding concerning the mother's financial resources. The court found that Ind. Code § 31-6-7-10(c) made clear that, except in those instances where an adult was charged with a crime, all matters within the jurisdiction of the juvenile court were to be tried by the court rather than a jury. In addition, the court found that the state constitution did not give a party a right to a jury in juvenile court proceedings nor was the Seventh Amendment applicable to state trials. As to the request for counsel, the court determined that the risk of an erroneous child in need of services adjudication did not outweigh the presumption against court-appointed counsel. The court found that the allegation of sexual abuse by the mother's boyfriend did not assure that her parental rights would be ultimately terminated. The mother was not entitled to appointment of counsel as a matter of right under the provisions of Ind. Code § 31-6-7-2(b), and the trial court did not abuse its discretion in refusing to appoint counsel to represent her.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying the mother's motions for counsel and a jury trial were affirmed and the cause was remanded.

Ledbetter v. Hunter


No. 49A02-9412-CV-722


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


652 N.E.2d 543; 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 740



June 30, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT CIVIL DIVISION, ROOM 2. The Honorable Kenneth H. Johnson, Judge. Cause No. 49D02-9404-CT-384.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff claimant filed a medical malpractice claim against defendants, two physicians and a hospital, within two years of her 18th birthday. The Marion County Superior Court, Civil Division (Indiana), pursuant to a motion by the physician's and the hospital dismissed the claimant's complaint because it was statute-barred under the Indiana Medical Malpractice Act (the Act), Ind. Code § 27-12-1-1 to -18-2 (1993). The claimant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The physicians and the hospital argued that the claimant did not file her action by her 8th birthday or within two years of the malpractice as required by the Act. The claimant argued that (1) the Act's provision, which tolled its statute of limitations for a minor until the minor's 6th birthday, violated due process rights as guaranteed by the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution and Ind. Const. art. I, § 12; (2) the application of the Act's legal disability tolling provision, which required her to file her malpractice claim by her 8th birthday, rather than the general legal disability tolling provision, which would allow her to file her claim by her 20th birthday, denied her equal protection as guaranteed by the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution and by Ind. Const. art. I §, 23. The court the court held that it was doubtful that the Act met the constitutional requirements of Ind. Const. art. I, § 23, because the federal equal protection clause and the state privileges and immunities clause were no longer treated as coextensive.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision that dismissed the claimant's complaint. The court remanded to the trial court for reconsideration in light of the new applicable methods of analysis.

General Motors Corp. v. Indianapolis Power & Light Co.


No., 93A02-9309-EX-489


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


654 N.E.2d 752; 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 741



June 30, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion and Order on Motion to Dismiss June 30, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 779.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE INDIANA REGULATORY COMMISSION. The Honorable James R. Monk, Chairman, The Honorable Frederick L. Corban, Commissioner, The Honorable G. Richard Klein, Commissioner, The Honorable David Ziegner, Commissioner. Cause No. 39437.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant industrial companies, utility counselor on behalf of ratepayers, and coalition sought review of the Indiana Utility Regulatory Commission's order approving appellee power company's environmental compliance plan submitted in fulfillment of the requirements of the Environmental Compliance Plans Act (Act), Ind. Code § 8-1-27-1 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The power company filed its verified petition with the commission seeking approval of its environmental compliance plan. The power company also sought approval to treat costs expended for the development and implementation of its plan as qualified pollution control property. The commission approved the plan and granted related regulatory relief. Appellants sought review and argued that the commission erred in interpreting the statutory prerequisites for pre-approval of environmental compliance plans found in Ind. Code § 8-1-27-8. The court agreed and reversed the order of the commission and remanded for reconsideration. The court declared that the portions of Ind. Code § 8-1-2-6.6 relating to Indiana coal were unconstitutional and needed to be severed. The court held that the challenged portions of the Act failed to pass constitutional muster because they failed to promote any "legitimate" local interest. Preservation of local industry by protecting it from the rigors of interstate competition was the hallmark of economic protectionism that the Commerce Clause prohibited.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the commission that approved the power company's environmental compliance plan and remanded for reconsideration.

 

923 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Haimbaugh Landscaping v. Jegen


No. 49A02-9407-CV-452


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


653 N.E.2d 95; 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 734



June 28, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 18, 1995. Transfer Denied February 29, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MARION COUNTY SUPERIOR COURT No. 5. The Honorable David L. Rimstidt, Judge Pro Tempore. Cause No. 49D05-9207-CP-0717.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant contractor brought an action seeking payment for services rendered to defendant homeowners. The Marion County Superior Court granted the homeowners' summary judgment motion that contended that Ind. Code § 32-8-3-1 did not permit a mechanic's lien for landscaping services and denied the homeowners' summary judgment motion that challenged the constitutionality of the procedures for acquiring mechanic's liens. Both parties sought review.


OVERVIEW: The homeowners maintained that Indiana law precluded the contractor from obtaining a mechanic's lien for the landscaping services performed because § 32-8-3-1 required that the services performed involve the erection of a structure. The court found that the Indiana Supreme Court had defined the erecting requirement of § 32-8-3-1 to require some physical act of labor in connection with the creation of a structure or improvement on land. The court concluded that the contractor should have been entitled to prove that its services resulted in an improvement on the homeowners' land, and that as a result, summary judgment was inappropriate. The homeowners also argued that the procedures for obtaining a mechanic's lien contained in Ind. Code § 32-8-3-1 et seq. violated the Due Process Clause of the United States Constitution as well as the Due Course of Law Clause of the Indiana Constitution. The court found that while the homeowners had a property interest in their residence and while the filing of a mechanic's lien was an interference with that property interest, the mechanic's lien did not deprive the homeowners of a significant property interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part.

 

924 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Bemis v. State


No. 82A04-9407-CR-276


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


652 N.E.2d 89; 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 719



June 22, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE VANDERBURGH CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Richard L. Young, Judge. Cause No. 82C01-9303-CF-146.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Vanderburgh Circuit Court (Indiana) of dealing in a schedule I controlled substance, a Class B felony, in violation of Ind. Code § 35-48-4-2 (1994) and possession of a schedule I controlled substance, a class D felony, in violation of Ind. Code § 35-48-4-7 (1988). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant consented to a search of his apartment where the police found a Psilocybin and Psilocyn mushroom growing operation. Analysis of the mushrooms showed that they contained Psilocybin and Psilocyn. Defendant had earlier been informed by a university extension educator that growing Psilocybin and Psilocyn mushrooms was illegal. On appeal, the court affirmed in part and remanded. The court held that Ind. Code § 35-48-4-2 (1994) and Ind. Code § 35-48-2-7 were not void for vagueness as alleged by defendant where Ind. Code §§ 35-48-4-2 and 35-48-2-4 unambiguously prohibited possession of materials containing Psilocybin and Psilocyn and both offenses required the State to prove that defendant knew the mushrooms in his possession contained Psilocybin and Psilocyn. The court held that the Indiana statutory scheme was sufficiently explicit to inform defendant that growing and distributing Psilocybin and Psilocyn mushrooms was proscribed. The court held that defendant's conviction of the lesser-included possession offense could not stand because it was based upon the same facts as the dealing conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of dealing in a schedule I controlled substance. The court remanded with instructions that the trial court vacate defendant's conviction of possession and the sentence imposed for that conviction.

Hines v. Caston Sch. Corp.


No. 25A05-9401-CV-22


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


651 N.E.2d 330; 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 641



June 8, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Counsel Amended June 21, 1995. Transfer Denied February 21, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE FULTON CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Douglas B. Morton, Judge. Cause No. 25C01-9212-CP-404.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parents, on behalf of their son, brought an action against defendant school district for a declaratory judgment and injunctive relief regarding a dispute over the school district's earring policy. The Circuit Court of Fulton County (Indiana) granted a judgment in favor of the school district, and the parents appealed.


OVERVIEW: A fourth grade male student was suspended for wearing an earring to school. His parents initiated an action on his behalf against the school district, challenging a policy that forbade the wearing of earrings by male students. The trial court entered a judgment in favor of the school district and the parents appealed. The court considered the issue of whether the wearing of earrings by boys violated the student's constitutional rights under the due process and equal protection clauses of the Fourteenth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. XVI. The court held that: 1) the parents failed to show that the earring ban served no purpose rationally related to the educational function of the school; 2) the enforcement of community standards of dress to instill discipline was a legitimate educational function; and 3) the parents failed to show that the earring ban violated equal protection because it did not substantially relate to a legitimate government objective.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of the school district.

Indiana High Sch. Athletic Ass'n v. Avant


No. 45A03-9402-CV-82


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


650 N.E.2d 1164; 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 579



May 22, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable James Danikolas, Judge. Cause No. 45D03-9312-CP-04066.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant athletic association sought review of an order of the Lake Superior Court (Indiana) granting a preliminary injunction enjoining the athletic association from rendering appellee student ineligible for any varsity team during the basketball season under the athletic association's transfer rule.


OVERVIEW: The student moved from a private school to a public school in the same district. The athletic association's transfer rule provided that a transfer without a move by the parents resulted in ineligibility for the first year following the transfer. The student was found to be ineligible for varsity athletics. The trial court enjoined the association from preventing the student from participating on a varsity team, and the association appealed. The court found that the trial court erred in enjoining the association. The court found that the association's decisions were reviewable under the arbitrary and capricious standard. Substantial evidence of probative value supported the association's determination that the student was ineligible. The treatment of transfer students without a corresponding change in residence separately from students transferring with a change of residence was reasonably related to the association's purpose in deterring school jumping and applied equally to all persons similarly situated so there was no violation of the Indiana Constitution. The court concluded that the trial court did not err by prohibiting the enforcement of the association's restitution rule.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that the trial court erred by enjoining the athletic association from rendering the student ineligible to participate in varsity athletics. The court concluded that the trial court did not err by prohibiting the enforcement of the association's restitution rule against the student and member schools.

Schnitz v. State


No. 34A02-9403-CR-146


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


650 N.E.2d 717; 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 569



May 19, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Transfer Granted July 24, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE HOWARD CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable R. Alan Brubaker, Judge. Cause No. 34C01-9005-CF-56



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Howard Circuit Court (Indiana), which convicted him of Dealing in Cocaine, a Class A felony.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of Dealing in Cocaine. The court affirmed and held that (1) there was sufficient evidence to sustain the conviction; (2) the trial court properly admitted into evidence an aerial photomap; (3) the prosecutor did not committed misconduct in his closing argument; and (4) the enhancement provision of Ind. Code § 35-48-4-1 was not unconstitutional. The court held that defendant took several affirmative steps that showed he knowingly or intentionally aided in the commission of the offense. Indiana law did not require that defendant had knowledge that the delivery of cocaine occurred within 1,000 feet of a school; the enhancement was applicable anyway. The prosecutor did not urge the jury to convict defendant for improper or irrelevant reasons; while the prosecutor did make references to the war on drugs, each reference was accompanied by an exhortation to prosecute and convict those who were in fact breaking the law. Defendant was not denied substantive due process of law or equal protection of law; statutory provision that enhanced the grade of felony if the crime was committed within 1000 feet of school was valid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of Dealing in Cocaine, a Class A felony.

Turner v. State


No. 32A04-9404-CR-146


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


650 N.E.2d 705; 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 519



May 9, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 14, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE HENDRICKS SUPERIOR COURT NO. 2. The Honorable David H. Coleman, Judge. Cause No. 32D02-9211-CM-001301.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Hendricks Superior Court (Indiana), which convicted defendant of aiding, inducing, or causing public indecency in violation of Ind. Code §§ 35-41-2-4, 35-45-4-1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant owned a lounge that featured female dancers. Officers observed females dancing in the lounge. Each of the females wore a G-string. Because the officers believed that the dancers had violated Indiana's Public Indecency Statute by unlawfully exposing their buttocks, defendant was arrested for aiding, inducing, or causing public indecency, pursuant to §§ 35-45-4-1, 35-41-2-4. Defendant was convicted twice of aiding, inducing, or causing public indecency. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that, in view of the undisputed facts, the Indiana State Supreme Court's case law, and the plain meaning of Indiana's constitutional Public Indecency Statute, there was sufficient evidence to support a finding that the dancers violated § 35-45-4-1. Further, sufficient evidence existed to indicate that defendant exercised the control necessary to be convicted under § 35-41-2-4. Moreover, because defendant opened the door to a civil zoning proceeding, he waived his objection to the state's further presentation of evidence on the subject. Finally, the prosecutor's improper voir dire statements did not place defendant in grave peril because the statements were cured by instructions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision convicting defendant of aiding, inducing, or causing public indecency.

Guidry v. State


No. 49A04-9409-CR-359


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


650 N.E.2d 63; 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 474



April 28, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION MUNICIPAL COURT. The Honorable David A. Jester, Judge. Cause No. 49F14-9304-CF-049081.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Marion Municipal Court (Indiana), which convicted defendant of operating a motor vehicle while under suspension of driving privileges, a Class D felony, which was a violation of Ind. Code § 9-30-10-16.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was suspended from operating a motor vehicle for 10 years after he was adjudged a habitual traffic violator due to his two convictions for operating a vehicle while intoxicated and one conviction for driving while suspended. After a dispute with his estranged wife, defendant was seen driving a vehicle. Defendant parked his car in front of his estranged wife's apartment. When a deputy sheriff ran the plates of the vehicle, it was discovered that the car was registered to defendant and that his license was suspended. The trial court entered a judgment that convicted defendant of operating a motor vehicle while his license was suspended, which the court affirmed. The court held that the evidence sufficiently established that defendant was the driver of the car. The deputy sheriff identified defendant as the man he saw driving defendant's vehicle. The deputy saw defendant in the vehicle, and again when defendant exited the vehicle and looked back over his shoulder toward the deputy sheriff. There was no requirement in § 9-30-10-16 that the State had to show proof that defendant operated the vehicle on a public highway. The language of § 9-30-10-16 was not vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that convicted defendant of operating a motor vehicle while under suspension of driving privileges.

Montano v. State


No. 45A04-9408-PC-335


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


649 N.E.2d 1053; 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 471



April 27, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Transfer Denied July 3, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Richard W. Maroc, Judge. Cause No. 1CR-144-682-573.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner sought review of a judgment of the Lake Superior Court (Indiana), which denied his application for post-conviction relief. He had been found guilty but mentally ill for voluntary manslaughter and murder. He was sentenced to 20 years for the voluntary manslaughter conviction and 45 years for the murder conviction.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner killed his mother and six-year-old niece by striking them with a heavy metal wrench. On review, he contended that the trial court erred in denying him relief based on fundamental error and ineffective assistance of counsel, and that the trial court erred in sentencing him. The court affirmed. The court held (1) that the giving of an allegedly flawed instruction did not rise to an error that was fundamental in nature, as an instruction on voluntary manslaughter was not required absent evidence of sudden heat and there was no evidence that the niece had provoked the prisoner in any manner; (2) that the prosecutor did not commit misconduct by questioning witnesses concerning the prisoner's mental state, as the prisoner had invoked the defense of insanity; and (3) that the prisoner's sentence was properly enhanced, as the trial court found that a reduced sentence would have depreciated the seriousness of the crime and that one of the victims was only six years old.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.
