Anderson v. State


No. 02A03-9408-CR-312


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


649 N.E.2d 1060; 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 469



April 27, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ALLEN SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Kenneth R. Scheibenberger, Judge. Cause No. 02D04-9307-CF-561.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from Allen Superior Court (Indiana), which, after a jury trial, convicted him for possession of cocaine within 1000 feet of school property, a class B felony, Ind. Code § 35-48-4-6(b)(2) (1993), failure to pay the Controlled Substance Excise Tax, a class D felony, Ind. Code § 6-7-3-11, and resisting a law enforcement officer, a class A misdemeanor, Ind. Code § 35-44-3-3.


OVERVIEW: Police officers, suspecting drug activity, approached defendant where he stood at an intersection within 700 feet of a school. Defendant fled but was caught within one block. Cocaine was found on him. Affirming, the court determined that the evidence was sufficient to support the judgment. The court reviewed the evidence of probative value in the light most favorable to support the verdict. The evidence supported the jury's inference that defendant possessed the drug while he was within 1,000 feet of the school. Defendant's conviction for failure to pay the Controlled Substance Excise Tax did not violated the double jeopardy clause of .S. Const. amend V or Ind. Const. art 1, § 14. Defendant was convicted of failure to pay the tax contemporaneously with his conviction for the drug charge, so the double jeopardy clause was not implicated. The tax was meant to work independently from the statutes governing drug offenses. The intent of the legislature in imposing the tax had to be for the tax to be in addition to punishment for the underlying drug offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Rzeszutek v. Beck


No. 71A04-9410-CV-406


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


649 N.E.2d 673; 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 438



April 26, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Transfer Denied September 28, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE ST. JOSEPH SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable William T. Means, Judge. Cause No. 71D01-9305-SC-3766.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant family sought review of the judgment from the St. Joseph Superior Court (Indiana) granting respondent homeowner a one-year extension of a protective order he obtained on behalf of the daughter of the family.


OVERVIEW: The family members' daughter moved out of her on-campus dormitory during her freshman year and into the home of the homeowner. Shortly thereafter, the daughter dropped out of school. The homeowner subsequently filed a petition for a protective order on behalf of his family and the daughter and against the family members, which was granted for one year. After a year, the homeowner filed for an extension of the protective order. The lower court extended the protective order for an additional year. In affirming, the court held that (1) the daughter was a member of the homeowner's household and the homeowner was authorized to obtain a protective order on her behalf, (2) the application of Ind. Code § 34-4-5.1 did not violate the family members' right of privacy, family integrity, or their free speech and association rights, (3) the lower court did not err in basing its decision on hearsay evidence, and (4) although the lower court applied the preponderance of the evidence burden of proof, it was not error. The case was not a termination of parental rights case, but instead a protective order case, which was governed by Ind. Code § 34-4-5.1.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment from the lower court.

 

933 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Alonso v. City of Hammond


No. 64A03-9406-CV-225


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


648 N.E.2d 1221; 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 374



April 6, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 4, 1995. Transfer Denied February 5, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE PORTER SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Thomas Weber, Judge. Cause No. 64D02-9201-CT-224V.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff homeowners appealed a decision of the Porter Superior Court (Indiana), which denied class certification to the homeowners and dismissed their claim against defendants, the City of Hammond and the Sanitary District of the City, for inverse condemnation. The homeowners filed their action under the Tort Claims Act, Ind. Code § 34-4-16.5-1 et seq. (1994) after rainwater and sewage backed up in their basements.


OVERVIEW: Homeowners in the City of Hammond filed an action under the Tort Claims Act, Ind. Code § 34-4-16.5-1 et seq. (1994) against the City and its Sanitary District after rainwater and sewage filled their basements. The attorney for the proposed class gave the city a notice, which contained names and addresses for 60 plaintiffs and stated that between 800 and 900 homes and businesses had been affected. The homeowners filed a motion for class certification. The superior court denied the motion to certify the class and granted the city's motion for judgment on the pleadings on the issue of inverse condemnation. The court examined the notice requirements of the Act and found that the names and number of claimants were essential elements for substantial compliance. Actual notice alone would not suffice. The court held that the notice requirements of the Act applied to classes as well as to individual plaintiffs. The court also examined whether the plaintiffs for whom proper notice was rendered had a claim under the Act. The court held that a single act of negligence that resulted in the homeowners' property damage was not an unconstitutional taking as a matter of law. The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the action of the superior court. The court held that the homeowners did not comply with the notice requirements of the Act, and that a single act of negligence by the city was insufficient to establish a taking as a matter of law.

Johnson v. State


No. 49A02-9408-CR-475


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


648 N.E.2d 666; 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 304



March 27, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION MUNICIPAL COURT. The Honorable Ruth D. Reichard, Judge. Cause No. 49F16-9310-CM-128863.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Marion Municipal Court (Indiana) that convicted him of stalking in violation of Ind. Code § 35-45-10 and sentenced him to 180 days of confinement, with 160 days suspended and credit for time served.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's victim was his previous girlfriend, whom he followed to four homes in Ohio and then to a shelter in Indiana. He was arrested after following her into a prosecutor's office where she had gone to file charges against him. The court affirmed his conviction and sentence. The evidence adduced at trial showed that the victim felt reasonably frightened by defendant, who had produced a gun in the past and had concealed his identity to locate her hiding place. It was sufficient to support his conviction. Ind. Code § 35-45-10 was not void for vagueness because its reasonableness standard and its requirement of proof of a continuing course of conduct provided standards indicating where the line was drawn between trivial and substantial acts. The trial court did not err in considering the facts that defendant crossed state lines and that he confronted his victim at a shelter as aggravating circumstances when he was sentenced. He was not attempting to enforce laws not yet enacted, he imposed the presumptive sentence according to Ind. Code § (19xx) 35-50-3-3, and defendant showed no harm.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment that convicted defendant of stalking and sentenced him to 180 days of confinement with 160 days suspended and credit for time served.

United Rural Elec. Membership Corp. v. Indiana Mich. Power Co.


No. 17A03-9303-CV-104


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


648 N.E.2d 1194; 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 306



March 27, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Transfer Denied September 21, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DEKALB CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Paul R. Cherry, Judge. Cause No. 54C01-9108-CP-0293.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, an electricity distribution cooperative, appealed an order of the Dekalb Circuit Court (Indiana), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant utility in the cooperative's action seeking damages caused by the utility's provision of service to a manufacturing plant.


OVERVIEW: The parties had agreed to boundaries for their service areas that allowed the cooperative to remain the exclusive service provider for a 960-acre tract. The two entities filed a joint petition with the Indiana Utility Regulatory Commission, which embodied the agreement. While the petition was pending, an auto manufacturer announced plans to build a plant in the cooperative's service area. The manufacturer asked the utility to provide service to it because the cooperative did not have the capability of providing the necessary power. The utility petitioned the Commission for permission to provide service to the manufacturer. After public hearings, the Commission assigned the area of the proposed plant to the utility. The state supreme court later reversed that order. The cooperative sought damages for the time period when service was provided under the void order. The court affirmed the ruling in favor of the utility. Once the Commission issued its order, the utility was required to comply with it. The fact that the order was later reversed did not render the utility's actions retroactively "unlawful."


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order granting summary judgment to the utility.

Rider v. Rider


No. 48A02-9312-CV-0680


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


648 N.E.2d 661; 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 307



March 27, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 11, 1995. On Petition to Transfer Granted April 30, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Ind. LEXIS 93.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MADISON SUPERIOR COURT DIVISION 3. The Honorable Thomas Newman, Jr. Judge. Cause No. 48D03-9210-DR-0727.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband sought review of a judgment from the Madison Superior Court (Indiana) that awarded maintenance and fees to appellee, his former wife.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the husband argued that: (1) the trial court's maintenance award was an unconstitutional impairment of the parties' antenuptial agreement; and (2) the trial court erred in awarding maintenance to the wife. Upon review, the appellate court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The trial court's nonenforcement of a provision of the antenuptial agreement did not result from a changed judicial interpretation of a statute. Accordingly, the nonenforcement was not an unconstitutional impairment of contract under either the state or federal constitutions. In support of its maintenance award, the trial court found that: (1) the wife suffered from a severe form of inflammatory neuropathy and was unable to work to support herself; (2) the wife had assets available for her support; (3) the wife's assets were not sufficient to provide for her support; and, (4) the antenuptial provision denying the wife maintenance should not have been enforced, because enforcing the provision would have left her unable to provide for her reasonable needs. Those findings sufficiently supported the trial court's maintenance award and were supported by the evidence introduced at trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

937 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Finding of Contempt Against Steelman v. Mills


No. 48A02-9406-CR-339


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


648 N.E.2d 366; 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 228



March 16, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MADISON SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Thomas Newman, Jr., Judge. Cause No. 48D03-9301-CF-38.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review from a judgment of the Madison Superior Court (Indiana), which found defendant in contempt of court for refusing to testify after the court had granted him a use and derivative use immunity at the request of the state.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the constitutionality of Ind. Code § 35-37-3-3 as applied to a co-conspirator awaiting his own trial, arguing that it deprived a witness of the right against self-incrimination. The court disagreed. The privilege against self-incrimination was not absolute, but was to be balanced with the government's legitimate demands to compel citizens to testify. The grant of immunity should leave the witness in substantially the same position as if the privilege to remain silent had been properly exercised. The court held that constitutional concerns were not raised by the mere fact that a witness had been compelled to testify. Rather, the constitutional violation occurred when the state used the compelled testimony against the witness. Furthermore, once the government initiated prosecution against the immunized witness, a pretrial hearing was the proper manner for challenging the state's compliance with the immunity grant. After a witness demonstrated that he or she had testified pursuant to a grant of immunity to matters related to the prosecution, the government had the burden of proving an independent, legitimate source for the disputed evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Bradley v. Eagle-Union Community Sch. Corp. Bd. of Sch. Trustees


No. 06A05-9405-CV-200


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


647 N.E.2d 672; 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 226



March 14, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 18, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE BOONE SUPERIOR COURT. ROOM NUMBER 1. The Honorable Thomas K. Milligan, Special Judge. Cause No. 06D01-9307-CP-0612.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners appealed the judgment of the Boone Superior Court (Indiana) finding that defendant school board had not initiated condemnation proceedings against them and denying their petition for fees and expenses pursuant to Ind. Code § 8-23-17-27(a)(2) in the landowners' action seeking to enjoin condemnation of their property. The landowners also appealed the entry of summary judgment for the school board on their tort claim.


OVERVIEW: The school board approved a plan to construct a new school. The school board identified the landowners' property as a site. No offer to purchase was extended to the landowners. The landowners sought to enjoin the school board from condemning their property. The school board had not initiated condemnation proceedings. The landowners amended their complaint to include a tort claim arising from the threat of condemnation. The school board filed a motion to permit access to the landowners' property for soil testing. Before the trial court ruled, the school board withdrew its motion and informed the trial court that it was abandoning any interest in the property. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment finding that the school board did not initiate condemnation proceedings and denying the landowners' petition for fees and expenses in the landowners' action seeking to enjoin condemnation. However, the court reversed the entry of summary judgment for the school board on the landowners' tort claim and remanded with instructions to dismiss the claim without prejudice.

Thompson v. State


No. 65A04-9410-CR-403


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


646 N.E.2d 687; 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 103



February 13, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Transfer Denied May 11, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE POSEY COURT. The Honorable Donald E. Baier, Judge. Cause No. 65E01-9312-CM-790.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Posey Court (Indiana), which had convicted him of operating a vehicle with a .10 percent blood alcohol content. Ind. Code § 9-30-5-1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of operating a vehicle with a .10 percent blood alcohol content (BAC). Ind. Code § 9-30-5-1. He contended that the statutory presumption concerning blood alcohol content, found in Ind. Code § 9-30-6-15 did not withstand the introduction of evidence that rebutted it. The court affirmed, and held that the presumption was permissive and not mandatory, but it remained for the jury upon the introduction of other evidence. A breath test administered within three hours after a law enforcement officer had probable cause to believe defendant was driving with a BAC of at least .10 percent indicated defendant did, in fact, have at least a .10 percent BAC, and the trier of fact may have presumed the person's BAC at the time of the offense was at least .10 percent. A rational connection existed between the fact proved, that defendant had a BAC of at least .10 percent at the time the test was administered, and the ultimate fact presumed, that defendant had a BAC of at least .10 percent at the time he was driving, if the test was administered within three hours of driving.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for operating a vehicle with a .10 percent blood alcohol content.

L.E. Servs. v. State Lottery Comm'n


No. 49A04-9406-CV-226


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


646 N.E.2d 334; 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 76



January 31, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Transfer Denied September 21, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable James S. Kirsch, Judge. Cause No. 49D05-9209-CP-932.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, foreign corporation and its officers (corporation), challenged the judgment of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which granted summary judgment on behalf of appellee State Lottery Commission of Indiana. The trial court pursuant to the Indiana Civil Remedies for Racketeering Activity Act, Ind. Code § 34-4-30.5-1 et. seq., enjoined the corporation from selling out-of-state lottery tickets within the state, finding it to be illegal.


OVERVIEW: In an action brought by the State Lottery Commission of Indiana (Commission), the corporation was assessed treble damages and enjoined under the Indiana Civil Remedies for Racketeering Activity Act (Act), Ind. Code § 34-4-30.5-1 et. seq., from selling out-of-state lottery tickets in Indiana. On review the court held that any lottery conducted in Indiana or its promotion other than by the Commission was illegal. Ind. Code § 35-45-5-6. Therefore, injunctive relief was appropriate without further showing of irreparable harm or the other elements usually required for an injunction. Second, the Commission was an aggrieved party under the Act and entitled to the injunction. Third, the state's gambling laws did not violate the Commerce Clause, both under the standard analysis for commerce clause issues and because Congress had made the corporation's plan illegal under 18 U.S.C.S. § 1301, which precluded judicial review. Furthermore, the state regulatory law was exempt from federal anti-trust laws, was an acceptable regulation of commercial free speech in protection of a substantial state interest, and did not violate the Contract Clause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court which found that the plan of the corporation and its officers to sell out-of-state lottery tickets within the state was illegal. The court affirmed the damage award and the injunction granted on behalf of the Commission under the Indiana Civil Remedies for Racketeering Activity Act.

Whitt v. State


No. 02A03-9407-CR-249


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


645 N.E.2d 677; 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 13



January 19, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Transfer Granted June 15, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE ALLEN SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Kenneth R. Scheibenberger, Judge. Cause No. 02D04-9308-CF-594.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his convictions by the Allen Superior Court for possession of cocaine within 1000 feet of school property in violation of Ind. Code § 35-48-4-6 (1993), failure to pay the Controlled Substance Excise Tax (CSET) under Ind. Code § 6-7-3-11, and resisting a law enforcement officer in violation of Ind. Code § 35-44-3-3.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had been approached by police in the vicinity of an elementary school. He fled and discarded a plastic bag containing cocaine. Although defendant stipulated that the area he was in was school property, the State did not put that stipulation before the jury. On appeal, the court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded. The court reversed the conviction for possession within 1000 feet of school property because the State failed to present the stipulation or put forth any evidence that defendant was on school property. The court noted that the police officers testified that the property was a school but did not testify as to the property limits or indicate that the property fit within the statutory definition in § 35-48-4-6. Although the CSET implicated the Double Jeopardy Clause because it could impose punishment subsequent to an underlying drug prosecution, the court held that it was constitutional based on state tax court precedent. The court noted that double jeopardy was not implicated in defendant's case as his prosecution for failure to pay the CSET was contemporaneous with his prosecution for the underlying drug offense.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded regarding defendant's conviction for possession of cocaine within 1000 feet of school property but affirmed regarding the balance of defendant's convictions.

Meier v. American Maize-Products Co.


No. 49A02-9304-CV-185


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


645 N.E.2d 662; 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 11



January 18, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Upon Rehearing Granted May 23, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 576. Transfer Denied October 10, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT CIVIL DIVISION, ROOM 2. The Honorable Kenneth E. Johnson, Judge. Cause No. 49D02-9112-CP-1376.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, board and governmental entities (board), challenged an order by the Mairon Superior Civil Court (Indiana), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee industrial companies and granted an injunction against the board.


OVERVIEW: The board claimed that it had not exceeded the statutory limits of its authority when it established a National Pollutant Discharge Elimination System, that delegating authority to establish a rule setting the amounts of permit fees was well within its discretion, and that it had not violated Ind. Code § 4-22-2-29(b) when it adopted the final rule. The court said that the legislative delegation of authority did not offend the Ind. Const. art. 1, §§ 23, 25 and that because the lower court found that the delegation was improper, it had to reverse the summary judgment in favor of the industrial companies. It also vacated the injunction that was entered against the board. The court said that the board had not acted beyond its statutorily delegated authority. Moreover, the board was established by the state in order to institute compliance with the federal Clean Water Act, and the state had the authority to grant power under Ind. Code § 13-7-2-15(a) to the board. In addition, the board had the power to establish rules, set fees, and for enforcement violations. Only if the board's actions extended beyond its delegated authority would a violation found be found, and there was none here.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment granted in favor of the industrial companies and vacated the injunction entered against the board. The cause was remanded for further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.

Remington Freight Lines v. Larkey


No. 79A02-9306-CV-294


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


644 N.E.2d 931; 1994 Ind. App. LEXIS 1810; 10 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 593



December 29, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Rehearing Denied April 4, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 357.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE TIPPECANOE SUPERIOR COURT II. The Honorable Donald C. Johnson, Judge. Cause No. 79D01-8211-CP-621.



DISPOSITION: The trial court's order for a new trial upon the issue of damages is reversed and the cause is remanded with instructions to enter judgment in the amount of the jury verdict.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a former employer and its safety director, challenged the order of the Superior Court of Tippecanoe County (Indiana) that granted a new trial of the issue of damages following a jury's finding that a former employee was wrongfully discharged by appellant former employer in retaliation for his refusal to violate the state maximum weight limit law.


OVERVIEW: Appellee, a personal representative of former employee's estate, filed a wrongful discharge action against appellants, a former employer and its safety director. It was alleged that the former employee, a truckdriver, was discharged in retaliation for his refusal to violate the state's statutory maximum weight limit. At trial, a jury awarded damages for wrongful discharge. Appellants filed a motion to correct trial errors pursuant to Ind. R. Trial P. 59(A)(2) and requested a remittitur of damages or a new trial. The superior court granted appellants' motion for a new trial. The court affirmed the jury's assessment of damages and reversed and remanded the superior court's judgment that ordered a new trial, holding that the new trial order was void because the order was entered outside the requisite period provided in Ind. R. Trial P. 53.3(D). The court found sufficient evidence from which the jury could reasonably have inferred that former employee's truck exceeded the state weight limit. The court concluded that the jury's damage award properly reflected the difference between former employee's actual earnings and the earnings he would have received from appellant former employer.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the superior court's order which granted a new trial on the issue of damages following a jury's finding that a former employee was wrongfully discharged because the new trial order was not entered within the required statutory time period, and there was no error in the jury's damage award, which reflected the difference between the former employee's actual earnings and those wages he would have earned.

Smith v. State


No. 49A02-9404-PC-240


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


643 N.E.2d 944; 1994 Ind. App. LEXIS 1712



December 7, 1994, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Transfer Denied February 9, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable John R. Barney, Jr., Special Judge. Cause No. CR84-189A.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner sought review of a decision of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which denied his petition for post-conviction relief. The prisoner had previously been convicted of burglary and attempted rape after pleading guilty.


OVERVIEW: Defendant broke into the apartment of a husband and wife intending to rape the wife. At gunpoint, defendant ordered the couple into the bedroom and ordered the wife to disrobe. As she did so, defendant laid his gun on the bed, and a scuffle ensued. The husband was able to gain control of the gun, and defendant fled. Defendant was soon apprehended. A master commissioner presided at defendant's guilty plea hearing and at defendant's sentencing hearing. On appeal, defendant contended that his convictions were invalid because the commissioner presided over both hearings. The court ruled that, although it was error for the commissioner to preside at both hearings, defendant waived the error by presenting the issue for the first time on appeal. Without objecting to the commissioner's authority, defendant submitted to the commissioner's authority, and the commissioner's authority as de facto judge could not be raised for the first time on appeal. The court rejected defendant's claim that his plea was invalid because he was misinformed about his potential sentences. The court ruled that the record was replete with evidence that defendant was properly informed of possible sentences.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Pinnacle Computer Servs. v. Ameritech Publishing


No. 82A01-9407-CV-213


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


642 N.E.2d 1011; 1994 Ind. App. LEXIS 1614



November 28, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] The Docket Number of this Case has been Corrected December 10, 1994. Rehearing Denied February 23, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE VANDERBURGH SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Terry D. Dietsch, Judge. Cause No. 82D03-9303-CT-531.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant computer company sought review of a summary judgement from the Vanderburgh Superior Court (Indiana), that was granted in favor of appellee publisher and that upheld the validity of the exculpatory clause in an advertising contract. Appellant contended that the exculpatory provision limiting appellee's liability to an amount equal to the contract price or the sum of money actually paid for the advertising was unconscionable.


OVERVIEW: Following a summary judgement that was granted in favor of appellee publisher and that upheld the validity of the exculpatory clause in an advertising contract, appellant computer company on review contending that the exculpatory damage clause in the contract was unconscionable and should have been held invalid, unenforceable, and against public policy. The court affirmed, holding that by appellant's agent's act of signing the contract, appellant assented to the contract's terms and the trial court did not err in finding that there were no genuine issues as to any material fact and that appellee was entitled to judgment as a matter of law. The exculpatory clause was deemed valid and enforceable. Further, appellant did not demonstrate that it was an uninformed consumer dealing with a coercive fraudulent company, nothing in the designated matters demonstrated that appellee's contract was one that no sensible person not under delusion, duress or in distress would make, and that no honest and fair person would accept. The court concluded that there was no basis in the designated materials to conclude that appellee's exculpatory clause in the contract affected the public interest.


OUTCOME: The summary judgement that was granted in favor of appellee publisher and upheld the validity of the exculpatory clause in an advertising contract between appellee and appellant computer company was affirmed because the exculpatory clause was valid and enforceable. The court found that appellant agreed to the contract terms and that appellant did not demonstrate that it was an uninformed consumer dealing with a coercive fraudulent company.

No. 54A04-9406-CV-2471


1 This case was transferred to this office September 21, 1994, by direction of the Chief Judge.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, an applicant to be a candidate for sheriff, appealed from a judgment of the Montgomery Circuit Court (Indiana), which denied his request for a declaratory judgment that several Indiana election laws were unconstitutional. The applicant also appealed from the affirmance of the determination of defendant, the Montgomery County Election Board, that he was disqualified to be a candidate for the position of sheriff.

Katner v. State


No. 49A05-9309-CV-325


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


640 N.E.2d 388; 1994 Ind. App. LEXIS 1209



September 12, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition to Transfer Granted September 20, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Ind. LEXIS 138.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MARION MUNICIPAL COURT. The Honorable Thomas J. Carroll, Judge. Cause No. 49F01-9202-MI-0384.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision from the Marion County Municipal Court (Indiana), which entered judgment in favor of plaintiffs, Indiana Department of Correction and the State of Indiana (State), in the State's forfeiture action to gain title of defendant's automobile.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped while driving his automobile and was searched. A glass tube and plastic container which contained cocaine were found in defendant's pocket. The State filed an action for forfeiture of the automobile defendant was driving on the night of his arrest. The State asserted that the automobile was used to transport cocaine. The trial court entered judgment in favor of the State. On appeal, the court stated that defendant's possession and transport of .0573 grams of cocaine was not sufficient to have justified the forfeiture of his automobile. The court stated that the State had made no showing that defendant had used his vehicle in any way to transport cocaine for the purpose of committing the offense of possession. The court stated that while the presence of the cocaine residue in the tube was sufficient to have supported defendant's possession conviction, his possession of the substance in his automobile did not constitute transportation of cocaine for the purpose of possessing the drug. Ind. Code § 34-4-30.1-1 did not support the divestiture of private property based on an insubstantial connection between the vehicle and the illegal activity.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment which had been entered in favor of the State in the State's forfeiture action to gain title of defendant's automobile.

Bird v. County of Allen


No. 35A02-9305-CV-211


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


639 N.E.2d 320; 1994 Ind. App. LEXIS 1101



August 25, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied December 16, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE HUNTINGTON CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Mark A. McIntosh, Judge. Cause No. 35C01-9203-CP-121.



DISPOSITION: This cause is reversed and remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant officer was part of a SWAT team that raided a drug house during which a suspect was killed by a team member, and the officer first said the shooting was justified. Later he made inflammatory statements about the shooting as part of another officer's campaign for sheriff, and appellee Allen County Sheriff's Department Merit Board dismissed him. The Huntington Circuit Court (Indiana) affirmed the board's action, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: The officer prepared a public statement about alleged police cover-ups of the shooting and the candidate for sheriff read it to the press during a news briefing. The board found that the officer violated five departmental rules of conduct, unbecoming conduct, immoral conduct, incompetence, abuse of process, and departmental reports. The circuit court found that the board's decision was based upon substantial evidence in the record. On appeal, the court noted that its review of administrative actions was limited to finding abuse of discretion or arbitrariness. While public employees did not abandon their First Amendment rights, under the Connick standard the speech was protected if it was on a matter of public concern and the employee's interest not outweighed by any injury the speech could cause to the interest of the state. The court found that the officer's speech was too disruptive of the police's authority and thus unprotected. The officer's actions deprived him of standing to challenge the department's rules on unbecoming and immoral conduct. The court found that the board's decision on incompetence and departmental reports was arbitrary and lacked reasonable basis.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court, which had affirmed the action of the board, but only because the board's decisions on two of the five rules violations were arbitrary and capricious. The court remanded only for reconsideration of the appropriate level of discipline to be given to the officer and not for a new hearing.

Mitchell v. State


No. 20A03-9312-CR-402


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


638 N.E.2d 1299; 1994 Ind. App. LEXIS 1071



August 22, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to Transfer Granted December 15, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Ind. LEXIS 188.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ELKHART SUPERIOR COURT # 2. The Honorable Stephen E. Platt, Judge. Cause No. 20D02-9209-CF-106.



DISPOSITION: Remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the portion of his sentence imposed by the Elkhart Superior Court (Indiana), which suspended defendant's operator's license and motor vehicle registration pursuant to Ind. Code 35-48-4-15(a) after defendant was convicted of possession of cocaine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to possession of cocaine. Defendant received a suspended sentence and was placed on probation for one year. Additionally, the trial court applied the suspension provisions of Ind. Code 35-48-4-15(a) to defendant. On appeal the court remanded for resentencing, holding that the compulsory suspensions of § 35-48-4-15(a) were unconstitutional as applied to defendant because the record was totally devoid of any evidence that a motor vehicle was involved in the commission of the offense, and the State stipulated that a motor vehicle was in no way connected with the offense.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case to the trial court with instructions to vacate the portion of defendant's sentence providing for suspensions of his operator's license and motor vehicle registration.

 

950 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Hornaday v. State


No. 49A02-9301-PC-2


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


639 N.E.2d 303; 1994 Ind. App. LEXIS 1074



August 22, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied October 5, 1994. Transfer Denied November 30, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. CRIMINAL DIVISION THREE. The Honorable John R. Barney, Jr., Judge. Cause No. CR87-252C.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision in the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which denied his petition for post-conviction relief from his conviction of robbery. Defendant argued that the superior court lacked jurisdiction to try the case.


OVERVIEW: Defendant made a motion for a speedy trial, and his trial was set within the speedy-trial period prescribed by Ind. R. Crim. P. 4(B). Prior to trial defendant requested a continuance. On the new trial date the state dismissed the charges. The state indicted defendant again, and defendant filed a motion to dismiss the charge as time barred, which was denied. Defendant pled guilty. The court affirmed and held that even though the time limit did not start anew when the state dismissed and refiled the charge, defendant's request for a continuance meant he was charged with the time between the vacated and rescheduled trial dates. In addition, under Rule 4(B) the speedy-trial clock was stopped during the period between dismissal and refiling and began running again when new charges were filed. The tolling was not affected by defendant's incarceration on a prior conviction because his parole would have been revoked anyway. The court held that the trial court had the authority to accept defendant's guilty plea; thus, any possible speedy-trial violation was rendered moot. In addition, by pleading guilty defendant waived any right to a trial and, thereby, any right to a speedy trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court that denied defendant his petition for post-conviction relief from his conviction for robbery.

 

951 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Department of Revenue v. There to Care


No. 71A05-9310-CV-371


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


638 N.E.2d 871; 1994 Ind. App. LEXIS 1046



August 16, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer Denied December 8, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ST. JOSEPH SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable George N. Beamer, Judge. Cause No. 71D03-9212-CP-927.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant department of revenue (department) challenged the decision of the Superior Court of St. Joseph County (Indiana), which declared appellee non-profit organizations were "qualified organizations" under the Indiana Charity Gaming Act, Ind. Code § 4-32-6-20 (the Act).


OVERVIEW: The non-profit organizations were formed for charitable purposes and sought to obtain bingo licenses. On appeal, the department argued that the Act required an organization to operate in the state for at least five years before it could become "qualified." The court found that in order for a charity to be a "qualified organization," it did not need to be in existence in the state for a period of five years before becoming eligible for a bingo license under the Act. By limiting eligibility for bingo licenses to bona fide charities that have been continuously in existence in the state for at least five years, the statute excluded all similarly situated and equally worthy charities solely because they had previously been operating outside of the state. As such, it discriminated against interstate commerce, and the department had the burden of showing the statute served a "legitimate local purpose" which could not have been adequately served with nondiscriminatory alternatives. The department did not meet its burden. Therefore, the court affirmed the trial court's decision.


OUTCOME: The trial court's decision that declared the non-profit organizations to be "qualified organizations" under the Charity Gaming Act was affirmed.

McIntosh v. State


No. 36A04-9303-CR-81


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


638 N.E.2d 1269; 1994 Ind. App. LEXIS 1042



August 15, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer Denied September 28, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE JACKSON CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Robert R. Brown, Judge. Cause No. 36C01-8908-CF-147.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions on two counts of criminal recklessness, Ind. Code §35-42-2-2, class D felonies, one count of confinement, Ind. Code § 35-42-3-3,a class C felony, and one count of theft, Ind. Code §35-43-4-2, a class D felony, entered in the Jackson Circuit Court (Indiana).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of criminal recklessness, confinement, and theft after altercations with an ex-girlfriend, her child, and her new boyfriend. Defendant appealed his convictions. The court affirmed the decision of the trial court. The court held that it was not error for the trial court not to have given definitional instructions on the specific intent terms of art "knowingly" and "intentionally." The jury instructions given by the trial court on the several charges faced by defendant were corrected and tracked the statutes under which he was charged. No prejudice resulted by the jury's use of the ordinary meanings of "knowingly" and intentionally." The jury was properly instructed about the crimes charged and the state was required to prove the elements of the exact offense charged. The confinement statute, Ind. Code 35-42-3-3, was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad. The evidence was sufficient to show that defendant was driving a vehicle that held stolen property, and this sustained his theft conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction of defendant for confinement, theft, and criminal recklessness.

Osmulski v. Becze


No. 45A03-9307-CV-224


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


638 N.E.2d 828; 1994 Ind. App. LEXIS 1031



August 10, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable James J. Richards, Judge. Cause Nos. 45D05-9107-CT1495, 45D05-9107-CT1518.



DISPOSITION: For the foregoing reasons, the judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver challenged the decision of the Lake Superior Court (Indiana), which found in favor of appellee husband in appellee's negligence action relating to the death of his wife. Appellant argued that the trial court erred in denying her motion for a change of venue.


OVERVIEW: Appellee husband filed an action on behalf of his wife who was killed by appellant driver as she attempted to cross a road. A jury found in favor of appellee and appellant sought review. The court affirmed, holding that the trial court did not err in denying appellant's motion for a change of venue because Ind. R. Trial P. 76 violated the Equal Protection Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV. African-Americans comprised 25 percent of the general population of Lake County, whereas in each of the 3 counties to which the case might have been venued, African-Americans comprised less than 1 percent. Appellant's utilization of the automatic change of venue rule effectively operated as a strike against every potential African-American juror in Lake County. Although the court disagreed with the trial court's conclusion that there could never exist a race-neutral justification for the use of the automatic change of venue, the court held that appellant's mere denial of discriminatory intent was insufficient.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the verdict in favor of appellee husband because the automatic change of venue rule violated the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment, as 25 percent of the general population of Lake County was African-American compared to less than 1 percent in each of the 3 counties where the case could have been venued.

 

954 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Coplen v. Omni Restaurants


No. 79A04-9302-CV-69


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


636 N.E.2d 1285; 1994 Ind. App. LEXIS 863



July 6, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE TIPPECANOE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Ronald E. Melichar, Judge. Cause No. 79C01-9010-CP-472.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, guardian of injured party's step-father's estate (estate), sought review of a judgment of the Tippecanoe Circuit Court (Indiana) in favor of appellee, employer of injured party's father (employer), in the employer's action against the estate to recover damages for payment of the injured party's medical bills.


OVERVIEW: The injured party was injured in an accident while a guest passenger in her step-father's car. Her medical bills were paid by her father's health insurance, which he obtained through the employer. The employer believed that it suffered a separate, compensable injury when it had to pay the injured party's medical bills, and brought suit against the step-father's estate. The court entered judgment in favor of the employer on its damage claim, but denied the employer's request for attorney fees. Both parties appealed. The court reversed, holding that by stating that the driver was not liable for those losses or damages that arose from injuries to enumerated passengers, Ind. Code § 9-3-3-1 precluded claims for "loss or damage" that originated from or had as their source "injuries to" the persons enumerated in § 9-3-3-1, absent willful or wanton misconduct on the part of the driver. Therefore, the estate was not liable for the employer's damage claim which arose from the injuries that the injured party sustained as a result of the step-father's negligent driving. The court found that because the employer was no longer the prevailing party, the issue of attorney's fees was moot.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court with instructions to enter judgment rejecting the employer's claim.

Steward v. State


No. 65A04-9207-CR-251


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


636 N.E.2d 143; 1994 Ind. App. LEXIS 747



June 14, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Transfer Granted June 23, 1995. On Petition to Transfer Granted June 23, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Ind. LEXIS 91.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE POSEY CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Donald E. Baier, Special Judge. Cause No. 65C01-9104-CF-9 & 10.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions for felony child molestation in the Posey Circuit Court (Indiana).


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court erred when it denied his motion to correct an error which alleged that jurors slept during the trial, allowed several witnesses to repetitively testify concerning the acts of molestation, admitted expert testimony on "child sexual abuse syndrome," and, pursuant to the Rape Shield Statute, Ind. Code § 35-37-4-4, precluded admission of exculpatory evidence. On appeal, the court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded. The court held that (1) defendant failed to preserve any error of juror misconduct and, even if he had, he failed to show prejudice; (2) the witnesses did not repeat the allegations of the child victims but merely explained the actions and events; (3) it was not error to admit the expert testimony and defendant failed to object or ask for a curative measure; (4) defendant was denied his Sixth Amendment right to cross-examination where the state offered corroborating evidence linking defendant to the molestation but excluded evidence of prior molestations of the children through cross-examination and prohibited defendant from proving there was another possible explanation for the victims' behavior.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction in part, reversed in part, and remanded for a new trial.

American Family Mut. Ins. Co. v. Dye


No. 22A05-9310-CV-383


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


634 N.E.2d 844; 1994 Ind. App. LEXIS 628



May 31, 1994, Filed

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, an insurer and an agent, challenged an order of the Floyd Circuit Court (Indiana), which entered partial summary judgment for appellee insured and denied their cross-motions for summary judgment in an action by the insured for declaratory relief, bad faith, and breach of fiduciary duty arising from the failure of the insurer and agent to make available and advise about underinsured motorist coverage.


OVERVIEW: After a car accident, an insured brought an action against an insurer and its agent for declaratory relief, bad faith, and breach of fiduciary duty arising from the failure of the insurer and agent to make available and advise about underinsured motorist coverage. The court reversed the grant of partial summary judgment for the insured and the denial of the insurer and agent's motions for summary judgment, holding insurance policies merely renewed after January 1, 1988, did not receive the benefit of the 1987 amendments to the underinsured motorist statute, Ind. The court entered summary judgment for the insurer and the agent.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of partial summary judgment for the insured and the denial of the insurer and agent's motions for summary judgment.

Hogan v. Review Bd. Dep't of Employment & Training Servs.


No. 93A02-9305-EX-00231


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


635 N.E.2d 172; 1994 Ind. App. LEXIS 671



May 31, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM A DECISION OF THE REVIEW BOARD OF THE INDIANA DEPARTMENT OF EMPLOYMENT AND TRAINING SERVICES. Case No. (92-IBA-130) 92-4-649.



DISPOSITION: The negative award is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee, a truck driver, sought review of the order by appellee, the Review Board of the Indiana Department of Employment and Training Services (board), which affirmed the administrative law judge's decision that the employee was not entitled to unemployment benefits because he voluntarily left his position with appellee employer and did not leave for good cause.


OVERVIEW: The employee quit his job after the employer announced that it was switching from a single driver to a team operation. The employee applied for unemployment benefits, which were denied by an administrative law judge and the board. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that it had the power to hear the employee's case even though he failed to file a timely assignment of errors. The court held that a failure to file an assignment of errors no longer deprived the appellate court jurisdiction, and did not prevent the court from exercising its inherent discretionary power to hear the merits of the case. The court reasoned that jurisdiction was conferred by the Indiana Constitution or by statute, not by a piece of paper. Although the employer did change employment conditions, the court could not say that a reasonable person would be compelled to conclude that the change rose to the level of good cause to quit or that the employer had terminated his employment. Because there was no evidence of a specific agreement that the employee was only to work as a single driver, a reasonable person would not be bound to find that the employer unilaterally changed employment conditions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the board's finding that the employee was not entitled to unemployment benefits based on his resignation from the employer.

Jackson v. State


No. 27A05-9309-CR-345


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


634 N.E.2d 532; 1994 Ind. App. LEXIS 581



May 23, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE GRANT CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Thomas R. Hunt, Judge. Cause No. 27C01-9210-CF-69.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Grant Circuit Court (Indiana), which convicted him of criminal gang activity, a class D felony, in violation of Ind. Code § 35-45-9-3.


OVERVIEW: A store was burglarized and several guns were taken by members of a group called the "G's." The defendant was charged with conspiracy to commit burglary and criminal gang activity as a result. During his trial, evidence was introduced that members of the "G's" were initiated into the group by being burned on the right side of the chest or by being "jumped." Being "jumped" meant having other "G's" beat up the new member. When a member broke a rule of the group, the member was punched by the other members. There were at least nine members of the group in the state. A jury acquitted defendant of the conspiracy charge and convicted him of criminal gang activity. The court affirmed the judgment, by holding that there was sufficient evidence to support his conviction of criminal gang activity, pursuant to Ind. Code § 35-45-9-1(B)(2), because the intra-group fighting and beatings constituted the felonious battery required as a condition of gang membership. The court also held that this statute was not unconstitutionally vague because it gave persons of ordinary intelligence fair warning of the prohibited conduct and did not encourage arbitrary or discriminatory enforcement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, which convicted defendant of criminal gang activity, a class D felony, in violation of the gang statute.

Reel Pipe & Valve Co. v. Consolidated City of Indianapolis-Marion County


No. 49A05-9211-CV-403


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


633 N.E.2d 274; 1994 Ind. App. LEXIS 470



April 26, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Sitting En Banc. Cause No. 49D05-9206-CP-0682 (Consolidated with Cause Nos. 49D05-9206-M10690 and 49D05-9206-CP-0692).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners appealed a decision from the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which affirmed a resolution of defendant Metropolitan Development Commission that amended a plan adopted under provisions of the Indiana Redevelopment Act, Ind. Code § 36-7-15.1-1-30. The amended plan added the landowners' real property, located in an area previously designated as blighted, to be included on a list of property to be acquired by the commission.


OVERVIEW: The commission approved a proposed resolution declaring a large section of the city as blighted, deteriorated, and deteriorating. The commission's resolution was published in three newspapers that also set a time, date, and location for public hearing. Subsequently, the commission adopted a proposed amendment to the resolution. The amendment sought to add additional parcels of land in the redevelopment area to the existing list of property to be acquired. Affected property owners were given notice by certified mail. The landowners opposed inclusion of their property on the list. The commission approved and adopted the urban renewal plan along with an acquisition list. The landowners appealed to the superior court, which affirmed the commission's decision. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment from the superior court. The court found that the public hearing regarding the resolution declaring a large section of the city blighted was only a preliminary step in a long process of actually acquiring property, it was not a final adjudication of landowners' rights; therefore, no actual notice was required.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment from the superior court that affirmed a resolution of the commission amending a plan that added the landowners' real property, which was located in a blighted area, to be included on a list of property to be acquired by the commission.

 

960 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Hoskins v. Sharp


No. 30A01-9308-CV-259


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


629 N.E.2d 1271; 1994 Ind. App. LEXIS 230



March 3, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied April 28, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE HANCOCK CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Judith Proffitt, Special Judge. Cause No. 30C01-9012-CP-779.



DISPOSITION: We reverse and remand for proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, widow of a patient (patient), appealed the decision from the Hancock Circuit Court (Indiana), which entered summary judgment for defendant doctor in the suit for medical malpractice. The patient argued that the doctor waived the medical review panel, that the circuit court did not have jurisdiction to order the forming of striking panels, that the malpractice statute was unconstitutional, and that summary judgment was improper.


OVERVIEW: The doctor allegedly failed to diagnose leukemia. The panel, pursuant to the Indiana Medical Malpractice Act (Act), found that the doctor met the standard of care. The appellate court reversed. The doctor did not waive the rule that a claim had to be first submitted to the panel. The only type of waiver was when all parties agreed pursuant to Ind. Code § 16-9.5-9-2(b). The circuit court did have the jurisdiction to order the panel chairman to form two striking panels. The circuit court did not violate its limited authority under the Act since it did not dictate the panel's opinions or interfere with its operations. Existing law held that the Act was constitutional. However, sufficient facts existed precluding judgment based largely on an affidavit of another doctor produced by the patient. The affidavit was valid even though it was not notarized. The affidavit also met the requirements of Ind. R. Trial P. 56(E) since it was based on personal knowledge, it set forth admissible facts, and it established the other doctor's expertise. The patient was not obligated to establish each element with expert opinion but only had to address the issues raised by the summary judgment motion.


OUTCOME: The grant of summary judgment was reversed and remanded since there were genuine issues of fact based on an affidavit that the doctor did not meet the standard of care. The other issues raised by the patient, including challenging the constitutionality of the Act, were without merit.

Keen v. Keen


No. 49A04-9207-CV-245


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


629 N.E.2d 938; 1994 Ind. App. LEXIS 187



March 2, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Cynthia J. Ayers, Judge. Cause No. 49D04-9103-DR-480.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband appealed a child custody decree of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana).


OVERVIEW: The parties had entered into a baby-sitting agreement. When a court-appointed guardian later submitted his written recommendations limiting the terms of the child care provision, the trial court, without notice or hearing, accepted the guardian's limitations and incorporated them into its final order. The husband argued that, without a hearing with 10 days notice, as required by Ind. Code § 31-1-11.5-22, the trial court improperly considered the guardian's report. The court held that the parties' baby-sitting agreement did not bind the trial court if contrary to the best interests of the child. The agreement was inherently unworkable because it was impossible to discern from its terms exactly what circumstances triggered the provision. Ind. Code § 31-1-11.5-21(b) guaranteed the custodial parent the right to determine the course of the child's upbringing. Because the parties' child care agreement was not in the best interests of their child, the trial court was not bound by it. However, because the trial court improperly considered the recommendations of the guardian, the court reversed and remanded for a hearing on custody and visitation.


OUTCOME: The case was reversed and remanded for a hearing on custody and visitation.

Saurer v. Board of Zoning Appeals


No. 03A01-9305-CV-171


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


629 N.E.2d 893; 1994 Ind. App. LEXIS 180



February 28, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE BARTHOLOMEW CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Maurice A. David, Judge. Cause No. 03C01-9207-CP-907.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant landowner challenged a ruling from an Indiana trial court, which found that the landowner maintained a junkyard on his property in violation of Bartholomew Co., Ind., Zoning Ordinance § 5(28) in plaintiff zoning board's action against the landowner for injunctive relief. The trial court issued a mandatory injunction against the landowner.


OVERVIEW: The landowner kept a large number of objects outside on his property, much of it rusted and inoperable. In response to complaints regarding the "junk," the zoning board investigated and determined that the landowner was operating a junkyard in violation of the county's zoning ordinance. When entreaties to clean up the property failed, the zoning board filed an action for injunctive relief; the zoning board prevailed at the trial level, and the landowner appealed. The court held that certain items specified in the landowner's brief were not waste, valueless refuse, or fit only for recycling and therefore were not junk according to the definition adopted by the court. Some specified items were valuable antiques. The landowner was not required to comply with the zoning board's directive to license and keep operable the semi-trailers and vehicles found on the landowner's property or risk having them condemned as junk because such a requirement was not contained in the zoning ordinance, and the zoning board could not on an ad hoc basis impose a requirement not contained in the zoning ordinance. Items that were not specified in the landowner's brief were subject to the injunction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment as to some items of personalty specified in the landowner's brief and dissolved the injunction as to those items. The remaining unchallenged portion of the injunction remained in full force and effect.

Galbraith v. Planning Dep't


No. 48A02-9210-CV-494


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


627 N.E.2d 850; 1994 Ind. App. LEXIS 18



January 27, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MADISON SUPERIOR COURT, DIVISION II. The Honorable Jack L. Brinkman, Judge. Cause No. 48D02-9010-CP-520



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners sought review of a judgment of the Madison Superior Court, Division II (Indiana), which granted judgment for appellee city planning commission (commission) in the landowners' claim against the commission for taking their property without just compensation.


OVERVIEW: The landowners' property was rezoned as a floodway by the commission and the landowners argued that such rezoning constituted a taking because the value of their real property had been diminished from $ 60,000 to $ 1000. The landowners subsequently instituted an inverse condemnation action against the commission and the trial court dismissed the landowners' complaint with prejudice. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court first noted that it would treat the dismissal with prejudice as a summary judgment for the commission. The court held that no cause of inverse condemnation could lie because the action was premature. The question of whether the zoning ordinance had "gone too far" and therefore constituted a taking hinged upon the economic impact of the rezoning. However, the landowners had not attempted to obtain a permit or a special exception and thus could not show that a final determination had been made that deprived them of all reasonable use of their property. That omission was critical because the economic impact could not be evaluated until a final determination regarding the possible uses of the property had been made. There was no error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which entered judgment in favor of the commission in the landowners' inverse condemnation action.

Heitman v. State


No.54A05-9306-CR-2011


1 This case was diverted to our office on December 13, 1993, by direction of the Chief Judge.


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


627 N.E.2d 1307; 1994 Ind. App. LEXIS 4



January 18, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MONTGOMERY CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Thomas K. Milligan, Judge. Cause No. 54C01-9008-CF-111.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Montgomery Circuit Court (Indiana), which, after a jury trial, convicted him of child molesting and incest.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had custody of his two daughters after a divorce. He moved with them out of state. The older daughter returned to Indiana and accused him of molesting her. The Indiana police investigated and defendant cooperated fully with the investigation. More than five years after the last incident was alleged to have occurred, the State charged defendant. Defendant was found guilty and sentenced. On appeal, the court reversed. The court found that Ind. Code § 35-41-4-2(a)(1) provided a five year statute of limitations but that Ind. Code § 35-41-4-2(g)(1) tolled the statute of limitations if the accused lived out of state or concealed himself. The court found that under Ind. Const. art. 1, § 13, the legislature could not enact a statute that fell disproportionately on some citizens. The court found that because defendant had fully cooperated with the investigation, the tolling provision of Ind. Code § 35-41-4-2(g)(1) should not apply because defendant was always available for service of process. The court found that any other interpretation of the statute would not have a fair and substantial relation to the State's ability to bring that person to justice.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, vacated defendant's convictions, and ordered him to be immediately released from custody.

Commissioner of Labor v. Gary Steel Prods. Corp.


No. 49A02-9309-CV-474


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


643 N.E.2d 407; 1994 Ind. App. LEXIS 1695



November, 30, 1994, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Civil Division, Room Two. The Honorable Kenneth H. Johnson, Judge. Cause No. 49D029206-MI-0636.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent Commissioner of Labor and the Board of Safety Review (collectively IOSHA) appealed a decision from the Marion Superior Court Civil Division, Room Two (Indiana), which reversed IOSHA's finding that petitioner employer had committed a series of safety violations.


OVERVIEW: IOSHA had determined that the employer was guilty of eight "knowing" violations and had ordered a $ 10,000 penalty for each. In reversing the decision, the trial court found that IOSHA had violated the employer's due process rights, and the finding was unsupported by the facts. On appeal, the court held that deference had to be given to IOSHA's interpretation of the statute. IOSHA's decision to look to the federal law in construing the statute, and in holding that the "knowing" requirement of the statute did not require a showing of bad motive, was well within its discretion. Thus, reversal on this basis was improper. The court also rejected the trial court's conclusion that the statute, Ind. Code § 22-8-1.1-27.1 was unconstitutionally vague, because it only involved the classification of penalties, and did not prohibit any particular conduct. However, the trial court properly reversed seven of the eight violations, because the IOSHA order cited a federal regulation which did not apply to the employer. The eighth violation was unsupported by any evidence. Thus, the trial court did not err in reversing the order.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court in favor of the employer was affirmed.

 

966 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Moran v. State


No. 49A05-9212-CR-427


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


625 N.E.2d 1231; 1993 Ind. App. LEXIS 1497



December 13, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to Transfer Granted December 12, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Ind. LEXIS 185.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION MUNICIPAL COURT. The Honorable Charles A. Wiles, Judge. Cause No. 92-057811.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of a decision of the Marion Municipal Court (Indiana), which denied their motion to suppress evidence obtained through a police search of a residence shared by them.


OVERVIEW: Defendants contended that the trial court erred in finding that no reasonable expectation of privacy existed under the state constitution for trash put out for disposal. Defendant further argued that the good faith exception to the probable cause requirement did not apply to a search warrant that was used by the police to obtain incriminating evidence. The court found that that the warrantless police search of defendants' trash did not violate the Fourth Amendment because the garbage containers were placed in defendants' driveway approximately one foot from the street, which was readily accessible to the public. The court found that an individual wishing to rummage through the contents of the containers would not have needed to step onto defendants' property to do so, thus the police could not reasonably have been expected to avert their eyes from the incriminating evidence. The court found the motion to suppress was properly denied because an independent magistrate properly found probable cause to issue the search warrant in contention and the police officers reasonably relied on the warrant's validity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court because a warrantless search of defendants' trash was proper under the state constitution.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff developer sought review of the judgment of the Lake Superior Court (Indiana), which affirmed the denial of approval to the developer's preliminary residential subdivision plan by defendant, the Lake County Plan Commission (Indiana).


OVERVIEW: The developer's residential subdivision plan was denied by the commission and the developer petitioned the trial court for a writ of certiorari. OUTCOME: The commission's denial of the developer's subdivision plan was affirmed.

Helton v. State


No. 55A01-9305-CR-178


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


624 N.E.2d 499; 1993 Ind. App. LEXIS 1447



December 1, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MORGAN SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable G. Thomas Gray, Judge. Cause No. 55D01-9204-CF-74



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Morgan Superior Court (Indiana), which convicted him of participating in criminal gang activity in violation of Ind. Code § 35-45-9-3.


OVERVIEW: Defendant belonged to a gang in which he was the second in command. As part of an initiation ritual, defendant participated in the beating of two boys who wanted to become members. Defendant was convicted of violating Indiana's Criminal Gang Activity Statute (gang statute) for committing battery on one of the boys. The issue on appeal was whether the gang statute was constitutional under the United States and Indiana Constitutions. In his appeal, defendant argued that the gang statute was unconstitutional, that the trial court erred in allowing a police officer to testify as to the history of defendant's gang under the pedigree exception to the rule against hearsay, and that the gang statute did not apply to his conduct. In affirming defendant's conviction, the court held that the trial court's erroneous admission of the officer's testimony of the gang's history under the pedigree exception was harmless and that the gang statute passed constitutional muster. Its prohibitions included a battery committed by one gang member on another consenting gang member.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the superior court that convicted defendant of criminal gang activity was affirmed.

 

969 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Farm Credit Servs., ACA v. Estate of Decker


No. 71A05-9209-CV-00313


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


624 N.E.2d 491; 1993 Ind. App. LEXIS 1426



November 30, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ST. JOSEPH PROBATE COURT. The Honorable Peter F. Nemeth, Judge. Cause No. 71JO1-9010-ES-0581.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CAUSE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant judgment holder sought review of a decision from the St. Joseph Probate Court (Indiana), which, on motion by appellee personal representative, disallowed the judgment holder's claim in a probate case because it was filed more than one year after the death of the decedent.


OVERVIEW: The judgment holder had knowledge of a decedent's death because his attorney and the judgment holder communicated about the fact that an estate might be opened. The personal representative failed to give the judgment holder notice under Ind. Code § 29-1-7-7. The judgment holder filed a claim over one year after the decedent's death. On motion by the personal representative, the trial court disallowed the judgment holder's claim on the ground that it was barred by the one-year limitation period in § 29-1-7-7(e). On appeal, the court reversed because the knowledge of the decedent's attorney of the judgment holder's claim was imputed to the personal representative. Thus, his failure to give actual notice of the opening of the estate contravened § 29-1-7-7. However, because there was a fact question as to whether the judgment holder was prevented from filing its claim because of the imputed actions of the attorney the matter was remanded to the trial court to determine if the one-year time limitation should be extended. The court also held that the one-year statute of limitations was not state action within the meaning of the Fourteenth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that disallowed the judgment holder's probate claim and remanded for further proceedings.

Kern v. Wolf


No. 57A03-9210-JV-00342


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a court-appointed advocate (CASA) and a county department of public welfare, filed an action against respondent mother to terminate her parental rights in her child. The mother challenged a judgment of the Noble Circuit Court (Indiana), which terminated her parental rights.


OVERVIEW: The mother's child was found to be in need of services and was placed in foster care. The mother exercised visitation with the child and participated in parenting classes and court-ordered counseling sessions. Her boyfriend was enjoined from any contact with the child. However, the mother married him. The CASA and DPW filed a petition to terminate the mother's parental rights. The trial court granted the petition. The court held that the conditions resulting in the child's removal from the mother's home would not be remedied, and termination of the mother's parental rights was in the child's best interests. The CASA acted within the statutory parameters of Ind. Code Ann. § 31-6-1-12 when she took measures to pursue the termination of the mother's parental rights. There was evidence in the record to support the trial court's finding that the mother's boyfriend presented a threat to the child's emotional well being and that he would present a physical threat to the child. There was also evidence in the record to support the finding that the child's safety in the mother's home could be ensured, if at all, only with long-term counseling.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.
