Black v. State


No. 27A02-9303-CR-109


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


621 N.E.2d 368; 1993 Ind. App. LEXIS 1166



October 4, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE GRANT SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable John P. Porter, Judge. Cause No. 27E01-9206-CM-431.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Grant Superior Court (Indiana) entered judgment upon a jury's verdict convicted defendant of operating a vehicle with .10 percent by weight of alcohol in his blood. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped for speeding. The officer smelled alcohol and saw an opened container of beer in the car. Defendant acknowledged that he had been drinking. The officer administered a portable breath test to defendant. Defendant was then taken to the police station where a breath test was administered using an Intoxilyzer. A test result of .10 percent blood alcohol was recorded. On appeal, defendant contended that the police did not have probable cause to stop him and that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction. The court rejected the probable cause argument, noting that police officers were authorized to stop speeding vehicles. However, the court reversed defendant's conviction because it found that defendant's evidence demonstrated that a reading of .10 percent blood alcohol content could have been rounded up from a lesser blood alcohol content and, thus, the evidence of a .10 percent reading did not establish that defendant's blood-alcohol content was at least .10 percent when he was operating the vehicle.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for operating a vehicle with .10 percent by weight of alcohol in his blood.

Lexington Ins. Co. v. American Healthcare Providers


No. 49A02-9208-CV-354


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


621 N.E.2d 332; 1993 Ind. App. LEXIS 1076



September 13, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Transfer Denied March 3, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MARION CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable John M. Ryan, Judge. Cause No. 49C01-8812-MI-4062-C.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant and plaintiffs sought relief from the decision of the Marion Circuit Court (Indiana) that denied their respective motions for summary judgment in plaintiffs' declaratory judgment action against appellant that claimed appellant owed plaintiffs a duty to defend in lawsuits and indemnify them from any judgment rendered.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs filed a complaint for declaratory relief against appellant that claimed appellant owed them a duty to defend in lawsuits brought by liquidators and to indemnify them and their directors from any judgment rendered. Plaintiffs' directors had filed a separate declaratory judgment action, which was consolidated with plaintiffs' appeal. The lower court certified each denial of cross-motions for summary judgment for interlocutory appeal. The appellate court affirmed the lower court's denial of plaintiffs' summary judgment because plaintiffs did not demonstrate that any legislation prohibited the use of the exclusion or that the companies were required to maintain expansive directors and officers liability insurance policies. The court reversed the denial of appellant's motion for summary judgment because the exclusion in the policies unambiguously applied to exclude coverage for the liquidators' claims in both lawsuits, and the exclusion was not contrary to public policy.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the lower court's denial of summary judgment on behalf of plaintiffs, reversed the denial of summary judgment with respect to appellant, and concluded that the exclusion provision unambiguously applied to exclude coverage for the claims and the exclusion was not contrary to public policy.

Young v. State


No. 34A02-9207-CR-308


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


620 N.E.2d 21; 1993 Ind. App. LEXIS 1013



August 24, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Transfer Denied October 13, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE HOWARD COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Douglas A. Cox, Judge. Cause No. 34C01-8810-CF-149.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Howard County Circuit Court (Indiana) convicted and sentenced defendant for dealing in cocaine in violation of Ind. Code § 35-48-4-1(a)(1). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Two confidential informants were introduced to defendant. Defendant told one of the informants that he knew of two local suppliers and quoted prices and quantities. Defendant obtained cocaine for the informant and offered to help the informants find cocaine sources in the future. Subsequently, defendant convicted by a jury of dealing in cocaine and adjudicated a habitual offender. On appeal, defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction because the State failed to overcome his defense of entrapment. The court determined that the State sufficiently rebutted the defense of entrapment. The evidence that defendant quoted prices and quantities demonstrated his understanding of drug terminology. Defendant also demonstrated his familiarity with suppliers and an understanding of how the drug market worked. The court also determined that defendant failed to show that his counsel was ineffective because he did not establish that he was prejudiced by his counsel's performance. Lastly, the court found that defendant's sentence enhancement was not unconstitutionally disproportionate. The court upheld the trial court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for dealing in cocaine.

South E. Ind. Natural Gas Co. v. Ingram


No. 69A01-9208-CV-263


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


617 N.E.2d 943; 1993 Ind. App. LEXIS 846



July 19, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE RIPLEY CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Eugene A. Stewart, Special Judge. Cause No. C-84-11



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee customers filed a negligence action against appellant gas utility relating to a partial interruption of service that resulted in damage to the contents of the customers' greenhouse. The Ripley Circuit Court (Indiana) denied the utility's motion for judgment on the pleadings. The utility appealed.


OVERVIEW: The utility experienced a reduction in line pressure, which resulted in a partial interruption of gas service and did not advise the customers to switch to an emergency source of heat. Loss of heat occurred in their greenhouse causing a total loss to its contents. The customers alleged the utility's failure to warn them to switch to an emergency source of heat was the proximate cause of their damages; the utility alleged the trial court lacked jurisdiction because the customers did not exhaust administrative remedies as the Indiana Utility Regulatory Commission (IURC) had exclusive jurisdiction. The court held the denial of a judgment on the pleadings was proper because (1) the IURC did not have exclusive jurisdiction over the issues raised as it could determine if the utility used reasonable care in providing services, which was a collateral issue, but its findings were not binding; (2) exhaustion was not required in a common law negligence claim, and hence, a dismissal was unwarranted; and (3) the customers stated a claim for relief as the utility owed a duty of reasonable care under Ind. Code § 8-1-2-4 to furnish reasonably adequate service, and under contract and common law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the utility's motion for judgment on the pleadings.

 

975 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Hendershot v. Carey


No. 27A02-9202-CV-77


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


616 N.E.2d 412; 1993 Ind. App. LEXIS 784



July 7, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE GRANT CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Thomas R. Hunt, Judge. Cause No. 27C01-8903-CP-189



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employees sought review of the decision of the Grant Circuit Court (Indiana), which enter judgment in favor of defendants, mayor, chief executive officer of the sanitary district, and the board of sanitary commissioners, in the employees' action to collect pay that was allegedly wrongfully withheld.


OVERVIEW: The city discovered that it had miscalculated the number of pay periods in its 1988 budget. Instead of the budgeted 26 pay periods, there were actually 27. The city did not have enough funds and decided not to pay the employees for the unbudgeted pay period. The employees filed an action against defendants, alleging that defendants wrongfully withheld wages and sought collection of the wages for the unbudgeted period. The trial court granted judgment in favor of defendants. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment for the employees who were paid hourly and affirmed the decision for the employees who were paid a salary. The court held that salaried employees' wages were the amount agreed upon to be paid for the entire year, and as long as that amount was tendered over the course of the year, the number of pay periods was irrelevant. However, the wages earned by an hourly employee represented the work performed during the pay period, and thus hourly employees were entitled to wages for the unbudgeted pay period. The court also held that the city's decision to not pay for the unbudgeted period did not violate Ind. Const. art. I §§ 21, 24, and 27 or Ind. Code § 22-2-5-1.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment for the employees who were paid hourly and affirmed the decision for the employees who were paid a salary. The court remanded the case to the trial court with instruction to determine which employees were hourly and to make other determinations consistent with the opinion.

In re Jordan


No. 49A02-9212-JV-618


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


616 N.E.2d 388; 1993 Ind. App. LEXIS 707



June 24, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT, JUVENILE DIVISION. The Honorable James W. Payne, Judge. Cause No. 49D09-9111-JC-000596.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of an order from the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which granted summary judgment to appellee Marion County Department of Public Welfare (DPW) in her complaint for declaratory and injunctive relief. She sought the release of her minor son from DPW custody.


OVERVIEW: The son had been hospitalized and DPW received a report that the mother suffered from Munchausen Syndrome by proxy. She was advised that he was being taken into protective custody. She filed her complaint. Because of a holiday weekend, nearly 156 hours passed before a post-detention hearing was held in response to the DPW's petition for temporary custody. The son was returned to the mother under DPW's supervision. She claimed that due process required that a detention hearing be held within 48 hours, including holidays and weekends, of a child's removal from his parent's custody. Upon review, the court affirmed. It found that the constitutionality of the detention statute was not moot even though the DPW's petition had been dismissed. The detention statute, Ind. Code § 31-6-4-6(e) provided that a hearing had to be held with 72 hours, excluding weekends and legal holidays, after a child had been taken into custody. The court found that between § 31-6-4-6(e) and Ind. Code § 31-6-4-4(c), an adequate balance between the need of the child to be protected and the parent's right to have custody was maintained. The detention statute met the requirements of due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment for DPW in the mother's action for declaratory and injunctive relief.

Taylor v. State Election Bd.


No. 74A01-9207-CV-2481


1 This case was transferred to this office on April 20, 1993 by direction of the Chief Judge.


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


616 N.E.2d 380; 1993 Ind. App. LEXIS 700



June 22, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE SPENCER CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Wayne Roell, Judge. Cause No. 74C01-9201-CP-7



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant councilman challenged an order of the Spencer Circuit Court (Indiana), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, election board, its chairman and members, and a county council, in the councilman's action seeking a declaratory judgment that he could remain on the county council even though Ind. Code § 3-8-1-5(3)(B), apparently disqualified him from holding the office.


OVERVIEW: The councilman's seat on the county council was declared vacant by operation of Ind. Code § 3-8-1-5(3)(B), which was passed after his election and which disqualified him on the basis that he was convicted of two counts of felony criminal recklessness while he was a member of the county council. The councilman sought a declaratory judgment that he could remain on the county council, and the trial court concluded that the councilman was properly disqualified. The councilman appealed, alleging that the statute was unconstitutional as applied to him. The court affirmed, holding that § 3-8-1-5(3)(B) was not unconstitutional because it was reasonably necessary to accomplish the legitimate objective of disqualification. The statute was not an ex post facto law because the legislature's aim in enacting the statute was not to punish past activities but to regulate elected officials based upon their general characteristics, including trustworthiness. The councilman's disqualification did not constitute improper disenfranchisement because each of the councilman's convictions was a felony which was punishable by imprisonment for a term of years and therefore was an infamous crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of the election board, its chairman and members, and the county council, in the councilman's action seeking a declaratory judgment that he could remain on the county council.

DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant remonstrators challenged a judgment of the Boone Superior Court (Indiana), which reversed a decision of respondent county board of zoning appeals (BZA) and ordered respondent county zoning director to issue a zoning usage permit to respondent property owners.


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to the superior court's verdict ordering the zoning director to issue a usage permit to the property owners, the court held that the superior court erred in finding that the BZA acted outside the scope of its quasi-judicial authority on the issue. The court then held that the property owners were estopped from contesting the validity of the ordinance sections at issue because they had previously applied for a permit pursuant to the ordinances. Additionally, the court held that the evidence on record was sufficient to support the findings denying the permit. Thus, the court reversed the superior court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the superior court's judgment in favor of the property owners.

In re Wardship of R.B.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of a judgment from the Allen Superior Court, Family Relations Division (Indiana), which terminated her parental rights to five of her children.


OVERVIEW: The county department of public welfare took the children away from the mother because she used crack cocaine. The physical and mental conditions of the children were seriously impaired as a result of her inability to supply the children with food, clothing, shelter, medical care, education, or supervision. The mother contended that Ind. Code § 31-6-5-4(c)(2) was unconstitutional on its face because it required a standard lower than clear and convincing evidence to grant a petition to terminate parental rights. Upon review, the court found that the statute required the department to show that there was a reasonable probability, by clear and convincing evidence, that the conditions resulting in the children's removal would not have been remedied. There was sufficient evidence to support the termination of the mother's parental rights. She failed to regularly attend counseling and narcotics anonymous meetings. She frequently missed her scheduled visitation with the children and was not able to provide them with a stable home. She had no steady employment. The mother showed a total lack of commitment on her part to have the children returned to her care.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the termination of the mother's parental rights.

Fair v. State


No. 49A04-9207-CR-255


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA FOURTH DISTRICT


615 N.E.2d 489; 1993 Ind. App. LEXIS 698



June 21, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION MUNICIPAL COURT. CRIMINAL DIVISION. ROOM 15. The Honorable Richard E. Sallee, Judge. Cause No. 49F15-9110-CF-139133


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Marion Municipal Court, Criminal Division (Indiana), which convicted him of dealing in a sawed-off shotgun, a class D felony in violation of Ind. Code § 35-47-5-4.1, after it denied his motion to suppress evidence obtained in a warrantless search of his car.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with dealing in a sawed-off shotgun, a class D felony in violation of § 35-47-5-4.1. The trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence obtained in a warrantless search of his vehicle. A bench trial was held where defendant renewed his objection to the evidence obtained in the search. The trial court found defendant guilty and he appealed. The court affirmed his conviction, holding that the police officer had probable cause to arrest defendant for public intoxication and took him into custody due to his arrest. By reason of defendant's arrest, the police officer had a right and a duty to impound his car. The court held that the police officer's inventory search of an impounded car pursuant to established police caretaking procedures constituted an exception to the federal and Indiana constitutional requirement that the police search and seize property under a warrant. The court further held that it could not say that the police officer's expectation of what he would find in the inventory searched changed the nature of that search.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction of defendant for dealing in a sawed-off shotgun, a class D felony, after it denied his motion to suppress evidence obtained in a warrantless search of his car.

Hartman v. State


No. 43A03-9202-CR-52


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


615 N.E.2d 455; 1993 Ind. App. LEXIS 657



June 15, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 30, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE KOSCIUSKO COUNTY COURT. The Honorable James C. Jarrette, Judge. Cause No. 43E01-9108-CM-1532.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for operating a vehicle while intoxicated, in violation of Ind. Code § 9-30-5-1, a class C misdemeanor, in the Kosciusko County Court (Indiana), following a jury trial.


OVERVIEW: A police officer pulled over defendant's car after it was observed swerving off the road. Defendant failed field sobriety tests, and a subsequent breath test revealed a blood alcohol level of .14 percent. Defendant was charged with and convicted of operating a vehicle while intoxicated, in violation of Ind. Code § 9-30-5-1. The court affirmed, holding that there was no error in instructing the jury on the results and accuracy of the breathalyzer test, and that the law providing a presumption that blood alcohol levels were .10 percent while driving if they were at lease .10 percent when measured was not unconstitutional. Further, these laws did not violate defendant's right to confrontation, as it would be impractical to have a toxicologist present to testify as to the accuracy of the machine and the competence of the test administrator, and copies of certificates of inspection were admissible. Moreover, the jury could rely on the presumption that his blood alcohol was at least .10 percent while driving because the test was taken within three hours, and he offered no rebuttal evidence. Finally, the officer had sufficient cause to stop defendant based on his observations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for operating a vehicle while intoxicated.

Conner v. State


No. 21A01-9205-CR-126


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


613 N.E.2d 484; 1993 Ind. App. LEXIS 529



May 20, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended May 23, 1993. Transfer Denied December 30, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Ind. LEXIS 213.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Daniel L. Pflum, Judge. Cause No. 21C01-9109-CF-88.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Fayette Circuit Court (Indiana) that rendered judgment against him after a jury's finding of guilt on charges of distributing a substance represented to be a controlled substance. Defendant also challenged his enhanced six-year sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of distributing a substance represented to be a controlled substance and received a six-year enhanced sentence. Defendant challenged his conviction and his sentence. The court affirmed his conviction, but remanded the case for a new sentence hearing. The court held: (1) Ind. Code § 35-48-4-4.6 was constitutional and did not require the distribution of an actual controlled substance; (2) no error resulted from the trial court's deletion of the word "controlled" before "substance"; (3) defendant's equal protection rights were not violated by the state because the prosecutor had the discretion to charge him with either a Class C or D felony because defendant was not a member of a suspect class and was not treated differently then anyone else; (4) the state proved that the plant material sold was not a controlled substance, the statutory scheme was not unreasonable, and the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting evidence or in not declaring a mistrial; and (5) defendant's sentencing statement was inaccurate in that defendant was not an admitted drug dealer, and his unemployment was not an aggravating factor, thus, his sentencing was improper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that rendered judgment against him after a jury found defendant guilty of charges of distributing a substance represented to be a controlled substance. However, the court reversed his enhanced six-year sentence and remanded the case back to the trial court for a new sentencing hearing.

 

983 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Maher v. State


No. 71A03-9211-CR-3701


1 This opinion is the 2000th majority decision by Judge Staton.


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


612 N.E.2d 1063; 1993 Ind. App. LEXIS 405



April 22, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ST. JOSEPH SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Sanford M. Brook, Judge. Cause No. 71D01-9201-CF-00089



DISPOSITION: We affirm.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a determination of the St. Joseph Superior Court (Indiana), which, after accepting his plea of guilty to possession of cocaine, sentenced him to a one year suspended sentence and pursuant to Ind. Code § 35-48-4-15(a) (Supp. 1992), suspended his operator's license and his ability to register motor vehicles for six months.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to one count of possession of cocaine, a Class D Felony. The trial court sentenced him to one year with the Department of Corrections. The trial court then suspended the sentence and placed defendant on probation for one year. Pursuant to § 35-48-4-15(a), the trial court also suspended his operator's license and his ability to register a motor vehicle in the state of Indiana for a period of six months. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that: (1) driving was not a fundamental right in Indiana; (2) in support of § 35-48-4-15(a), the state provided a reasonable basis highway safety and reducing the distribution and use of drugs for the classification, and defendant's equal protection arguments failed; (3) there was clear and convincing evidence that the purpose of highway safety was forwarded by the application of § 35-48-4-15(a) to defendant; (4) defendant could not properly make a privileges and immunities claim; and (5) defendant's request to change the public policy of Indiana was not properly addressed to the court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's suspension of defendant's driving and motor vehicle registration privileges.

 

984 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Keil Chem. Co., Div. of Ferro Corp. v. Common Council of Hammond


No. 45A03-9212-CV-420


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


612 N.E.2d 209; 1993 Ind. App. LEXIS 397



April 20, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied July 20, 1993. Transfer Denied October 1, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT, ROOM NO. TWO. The Honorable Morton B. Kanz, Judge. Cause No. 45D02-9110-MI-01066.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant company sought review of an order of the Lake Superior Court (Indiana), which dismissed its petition for writ of certiorari seeking review of a decision by appellees, the City of Hammond (City) and the common council of the City.


OVERVIEW: The company was an unsuccessful use variance applicant before the common council. The company filed a petition for writ of certiorari in the trial court, naming as respondents the common council and the City. The City filed a motion to dismiss for lack of jurisdiction. The trial court dismissed the petition for lack of presentment on the grounds that the company failed to meet its burden of strict compliance with the statutory requirements for review of the complained of decision. The company appealed. The court held that although the company fulfilled its statutory obligation to "present" its petition, inasmuch as the petition was filed in open court, the company's petition was nevertheless appropriately dismissed for lack of proper verification and notice. The company's petition was not verified by an executive or administrative officer of the company, the actual "person aggrieved," as required by Ind. Code § 36-7-4-1003. The evidence also showed that the company did not comply with Ind. Code § 36-7-4-1005 by failing to notify three property owners, who were adversary parties necessary and indispensable to the proceeding, of the hearing. As such, dismissal was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, which dismissed the company's petition for writ of certiorari seeking review of a zoning decision.

 

985 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Poulson v. Poulson


No. 35A02-9202-CV-84


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


612 N.E.2d 193; 1993 Ind. App. LEXIS 363



April 15, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE HUNTINGTON CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Everett E. Goshorn, Special Judge. Cause No. 35C01-9110-JP-50.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the juvenile court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of a decision of the Huntington Circuit Court (Indiana), which ordered him to pay appellee daughter for support and college expenses pursuant to Ind. Code § 31-6-6.1 et seq. (1992), the Paternity Statute.


OVERVIEW: The father asserted that he could not be ordered to pay support and college expenses under the Paternity Statute when there was no actual controversy regarding paternity. Specifically, he maintained that a trial court did not have jurisdiction over a paternity dispute when there was no real controversy regarding paternity. The court noted that the purpose of the Paternity Statute was to vest the father with the rights and responsibilities of parenthood, not merely to establish the fact of parenthood. The father had no real basis for complaint when he was judged to be what he freely admitted he was, the father of the daughter, and was then called upon to fulfill his non-custodial parental support obligations. The court also concluded that the daughter had standing to bring the paternity action against the father under Ind. Code § 31-6-6.1-2(a)(4), and that she had timely filed her petition that appropriately sought a statutorily authorized remedy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Culver-Union Township Ambulance Serv. v. Steindler


No. 50A04-9109-CV-306


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


611 N.E.2d 698; 1993 Ind. App. LEXIS 329



April 8, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to Transfer Granted March 7, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Ind. LEXIS 17.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARSHALL CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Michael D. Cook, Judge. Cause No. 50C01-9009-CT-74.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, municipal ambulance service, president of a municipal board, and municipal trustee, sought an interlocutory review of the decision of the Marshall Circuit Court (Indiana), which denied appellants' motions to dismiss and for judgment on the pleadings in appellee executrix's wrongful death and 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action.


OVERVIEW: The executrix filed a wrongful death action and a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action against appellants, alleging that the ambulance service caused the wrongful death of the decedent, and various policies adopted by appellants constituted a reckless indifference to decedent's constitutionally guaranteed right to live. The trial court denied appellants' motion to dismiss and for judgment on the pleadings, but granted their motion for interlocutory appeal. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's denial of the motions to dismiss and for judgment on the pleading in the wrongful death action, holding that the issue of whether a special duty arose could not be resolved upon a motion to dismiss or a motion for judgment on the pleadings and that the executrix met her pleading burden by alleging the elements of negligence. However, the court reversed the trial court's denial of the motion to dismiss or for judgment on the pleading on the executrix's § 1983 claim and remanded with instructions to grant either motion in favor of appellants. The court held that the § 1983 action did not survive the decedent's death.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of appellants' motions to dismiss or for judgment on the pleading on the executrix's wrongful death claims, but reversed the trial court's denial of the executrix's § 1983 claims and remanded to the trial court to dismiss those claims.

Blackden v. Kaufman


No. 37A03-9205-CV-141


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


611 N.E.2d 663; 1993 Ind. App. LEXIS 301



April 5, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 13, 1993. Transfer Denied October 14, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE JASPER SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable J. Philip McGraw, Judge. Cause No. CP-86-4-38



DISPOSITION: For the foregoing reasons the judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of a decision of the Jasper Superior Court (Indiana), which dismissed their proposed medical malpractice claim against appellee doctors and clinic before the Indiana Department of Insurance. Appellees' motion to dismiss alleged that appellants prevented the panel from rendering its opinion within 180 days as required by Ind. Code § 16-9.5-9-3.5(a).


OVERVIEW: Appellants alleged that appellees committed medical malpractice by negligently diagnosing, treating, and caring for one of appellant's lower back problem. The alleged negligence occurred on or around February 12, 1984. Appellants requested and received an extension of time and a new submission schedule was set with appellants to submit their materials by May 1, 1991, and appellees to submit their materials by June 10, 1991, to the panel. Four days before the panel was to hear the case, appellant's attorney mailed his submission. Consequently, it did not arrive and the panel dismissed the claim. The court held that neither the failure of an appellee to come forward with evidence, nor the failure of the panel to render an opinion, was an impediment to sanctioning the complainant. The court held that dismissal was an appropriate sanction under Ind. Code § 16.9.5-9.5(b). The court found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in utilizing this remedy for appellants' failure to comply with the evidentiary schedule set up by the panel chair, especially after repeated requests to submit such evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

Saint Mary Medical Ctr. v. Baker


No. 45A03-9211-CV-366


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


611 N.E.2d 135; 1993 Ind. App. LEXIS 240



March 22, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended May 7, 1993. Rehearing Denied May 12, 1993. Transfer Denied November 18, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT, ROOM #3. The Honorable James Danikolas, Judge. Cause No. 45D03-9110-CP-03330



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; remanded for an evidentiary hearing on appellate attorney fees.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant medical center challenged a judgment from the Lake Superior Court (Indiana) that dismissed for lack of subject matter and of personal jurisdiction its collections action against appellee patient alleging that she was obligated to pay for medical treatment received for her injuries arising during employment.


OVERVIEW: The patient suffered injuries at work that were treated by the medical center. The worker's compensation insurance carrier partially paid the medical center bill, and disputed its remainder. The medical center brought this lawsuit to collect the balance due from the patient. The court affirmed the trial court decision granting the patient's motion to dismiss. The court found appellate attorney fees appropriate, but remanded the matter for an evidentiary hearing on their appropriateness. The trial court correctly dismissed the complaint for lack of subject matter and personal jurisdiction because it was the improper forum when the medical center failed to exhaust its administrative remedies pursuant to Ind. Code § 22-3-1-2. The application of Ind. Code § 22-3-3-5, which governed the issue of financial liability for medical treatment, was an issue that should have been directed to the Worker's Compensation Board (board). The trial court award of attorney fees to the patient for trial under Ind. Code § 34-1-32-1(b)(1) was in its discretion because the medical center's complaint was "frivolous" when its attorney failed to discover that the board was the proper forum.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court contested by the medical center, which dismissed for lack of subject matter and personal jurisdiction its collections lawsuit against the patient that asserted her obligation to pay for the treatment of her employment related injuries. The court remanded the case for a hearing on attorney fees.

Estate of Wilson v. Wilson


No. 48A05-9209-CV-329


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


610 N.E.2d 851; 1993 Ind. App. LEXIS 183



March 10, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 17, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MADISON CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Fredrick R. Spencer, Judge. Cause No. 48C01-9012-ES-163.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the trial court is AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, heir at law of her deceased aunt, filed a challenge to the decedent's will that named the appellee executrix as sole beneficiary. The Madison Circuit Court (Indiana) granted the executrix' motion to dismiss the heir's complaint because it was not filed within five months after the will was probated. The heir appealed.


OVERVIEW: The decedent died testate, leaving all of her net estate to her niece by marriage and also naming her executrix of the estate. Nearly a year after the will was probated, the decedent's natural niece challenged the will, alleging fraud, duress, and lack of capacity. The trial court granted the executrix' motion to dismiss the heir's complaint because it was not filed within five months after the will was probated pursuant to Ind. Code § 29-1-7-17. The heir contended that the executrix fraudulently failed to notify her of their aunt's death, and that the time limitation therefore did not apply. The heir also argued that because she would be entitled to an intestate distribution if the will were set aside, her right to contest the will was a property interest protected by the Fourteenth Amendment. The court affirmed the dismissal by the trial court, finding that the statute did not require notice of the testate probate proceeding be given to an heir who would take under intestate succession. The court ruled that the notice statute was not unconstitutional because the heir's mere expectancy interest as an intestate heir was not a property right protected by the Fourteenth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court dismissing the heir's will challenge was affirmed.

Smith v. State


No. 49A05-9111-CR-385


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


610 N.E.2d 265; 1993 Ind. App. LEXIS 171



March 8, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied April 13, 1993. Petition to Transfer Granted September 28, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Ind. LEXIS 138.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION COUNTY MUNICIPAL COURT. The Honorable Ruth D. Reichard, Judge. Cause No. 49F16-9010-CM130381.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED AND CAUSE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction after a jury trial in the Marion County Municipal Court (Indiana) on a Class A misdemeanor charge of battery. Defendant also appealed from his sentence to 1-year incarceration with 255 days suspended and his placement on probation for 1 year following his incarceration, with 6 months of the probation to be served under home detention.


OVERVIEW: After a verbal altercation, defendant physically assaulted his wife. He was tried and convicted on a charge of battery, a Class A misdemeanor under Ind. Code § 35-50-3. The trial court sentenced defendant to 1-year incarceration with 255 days suspended. Defendant was placed on probation for one year following his incarceration, with six months of the probation to be served under home detention. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction, holding that (1) defendant was not denied effective assistance of counsel because he did not establish that but for his counsel's errors, the result of the proceeding would have been different and because the court would not second guess counsel's trial tactics and strategy; and (2) improper comments by the prosecutor did not deprive defendant of a fair trial because the evidence against defendant was not close and he did not show that the persuasive effect on the jury placed him in grave peril. The court held that, while § 35-50-3-1 permitted the trial court to impose a term of probation of up to one year regardless of whether the term exceeded a suspended sentence, the home detention order failed to comply with § 35-38-2.5-6.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction on a charge of battery. The court affirmed defendant's sentence, but remanded the matter to the trial court with instructions to enter a home detention order setting forth the conditions required by Indiana law.

Morrison v. State


No. 49A04-9109-CR-308


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


609 N.E.2d 1155; 1993 Ind. App. LEXIS 152



March 4, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable John R. Barney, Jr., Judge. Cause No. 49G03-8909-CF-106447.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded in part, affirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) on charges of dealing in cocaine under Ind. Code § 35-48-4-1, possession of cocaine under Ind. Code § 35-48-4-6, and resisting law enforcement under Ind. Code § 35-44-3-3. He appealed the convictions and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant set up a cocaine sale with an undercover informant. The informant gave the signal to police cars to follow defendant's car. One officer turned on her emergency lights, and defendant fled. After a high-speed chase defendant was arrested. No drugs were found in the car, but after a search along the route a bag with the cocaine was found. On cross-examination of the State's key witness, the informant, the trial judge sustained the State's objection to the question regarding the witness's address. The trial judge did not conduct an in-camera hearing regarding the relevance of the address. On appeal, the court held that the failure to conduct an in-camera hearing was reversible error. Defendant was precluded from conducting his cross-examination of the key witness. The trial court committed harmless error when it responded to the jury's question during deliberations without defendant being present. Defendant's counsel was present. The error was harmless because the trial court denied the jury's request to replay testimony in an effort to determine the exact location of the officer when she engaged her emergency lights during the chase. Defendant suffered no prejudice.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dealing and possession charges and remanded for a new trial. It affirmed the conviction on the charge of resisting law enforcement.

Wesner v. Metropolitan Dev. Com.


No. 49A02-9011-CV-7021


1 This case was transferred to this office on January 8, 1993 by direction of the Chief Judge.


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


609 N.E.2d 1135; 1993 Ind. App. LEXIS 149



March 3, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected March 10, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION MUNICIPAL COURT. The Honorable Taylor L. Baker, Judge. Cause No. 49F12-8903-CP-0638.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant massage parlor sought review of a decision of the Marion Municipal Court (Indiana), which granted injunctive relief to appellee Metropolitan Development Commission (commission) in its action to enforce certain zoning ordinances, which the massage parlor had violated.


OVERVIEW: The massage parlor was operating on property under which there was a zoning ordinance, which prohibited the establishment of any adult entertainment business within 500 feet of a residential district. The commission filed an action to enforce the ordinance against the massage parlor. The trial court granted the commission permanent injunctive relief, prohibiting the massage parlor from operating on the property pursuant to the ordinance. The massage parlor appealed, claiming that the commission was guilty of laches, that the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague, and that its use of the premises was a lawful pre-existing non-conforming use. On appeal, the court affirmed, ruling that public policy interests prohibited the massage parlor as a private party from asserting the doctrine of laches against a municipality seeking to enforce its zoning ordinances. The court concluded that the evidence did not establish that the use of the premises prior to the passage of the ordinance was lawful. Finally, the ordinance survived a constitutional vagueness challenge because the commission established that the term "massage parlor" had a sufficiently precise meaning to the average person.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's award, which granted injunctive relief to the commission in its action to enforce certain zoning ordinances against the massage parlor.

McCullough v. State


No. 46A03-9205-CR-00133


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


608 N.E.2d 1009; 1993 Ind. App. LEXIS 113



February 22, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAPORTE COUNTY SUPERIOR COURT. CRIMINAL DIVISION, ROOM 2. The Honorable Donald D. Martin, Judge Presiding. Cause No. 46D01-8908-CF-075.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for retrial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Laporte County Superior Court, Criminal Division (Indiana), which convicted defendant of neglect of a dependent, a violation of Ind. Code § 35-46-1-4(a)(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed a jury instruction was misleading and inadequate because it failed to advise the jury to convict only upon finding that he was subjectively aware of a high probability that he exposed his dependent to a danger which was both actual and appreciable. The court reversed and remanded and held that the neglect statute was construed to apply only to situations where the placement of the dependent exposed the dependent to a danger which was "actual and appreciable" inasmuch as the statutory phrase "may endanger" was unduly vague. Repetition of the statutory language of Ind. Code § 35-46-1-4(a)(1), unaccompanied by other instruction, allowed conviction upon a less definite degree of proof than was necessary to avoid unconstitutional vagueness. Additionally, the jury was instructed that the State could meet its burden of proof by showing that the defendant placed the victim in a situation that might have endangered the life and health of the victim. However, the State had the burden of proving that the dependent's life or health was placed in actual, appreciable danger by defendant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the case to the trial court for retrial.

Collins v. Day


No. 93A02-9110-EX-449


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


604 N.E.2d 647; 1992 Ind. App. LEXIS 1806



December 14, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 22, 1993. Petition to Transfer Granted November 28, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Ind. LEXIS 159.



DISPOSITION: APPEAL FROM THE FULL WORKER'S COMPENSATION BOARD OF INDIANA. The Honorable Rogelio Dominguez, Chairman. Appl. No. C-111311. Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee appealed from the order of the Workers' Compensation Board of Indiana upholding the dismissal by the hearing judge of the employee's request for workers' compensation benefits for an injury sustained in the farming operation of defendant employer.


OVERVIEW: The employee was injured while working at the employer's farming operation, which was an agricultural enterprise. The employer had not waived the exemption of agricultural employees from workers' compensation coverage, under Ind. Code § 22-3-2-9. When the employee requested workers' compensation benefits, the hearing judge granted a motion to dismiss. The workers' compensation board upheld the dismissal. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that exemption of agricultural employees was not a violation of the Equal Protection Clause of the state or federal constitution. The classification that excluded agricultural employees was rationally related to furthering legitimate state interests in protecting the farming economy. The agricultural employee failed to meet his burden of showing that the statute was unconstitutional. The court noted that injured agricultural employees were not left without legal recourse, but could bring common law negligence actions for damages against their employers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the workers' compensation board which upheld the dismissal by the hearing judge of the employee's request for workers' compensation benefits for an injury arising during the course of his employment in an agricultural enterprise operated by the employer.

The court agreed with the landowners and reversed the judgment of the trial court.

Steelman v. State


No. 89A01-9109-CR-0287


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


602 N.E.2d 152; 1992 Ind. App. LEXIS 1593



October 28, 1992, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE WAYNE COUNTY SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Robert L. Reinke, Judge. Cause No. 89D02-9102-CF-028



DISPOSITION: The judgment is in all things affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Wayne County Superior Court (Indiana), which had convicted defendant for dealing in marijuana within 1,000 feet of school property, a Class C felony, pursuant to Ind. Code § 35-48-4-10, had adjudicated defendant an habitual offender, and had imposed an enhancement in defendant's sentencing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant offered to sell marijuana joints to a confidential informant, whom police officers fitted with a listening device, a tape recorder, and a microphone. They followed the informant to defendant's apartment, where he paid defendant a certain sum for six marijuana joints. The trial court convicted defendant for dealing in marijuana within 1,000 feet of school property under § 35-48-4-10, adjudicated that he was a habitual offender, and imposed an enhanced sentencing. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment and held that: (1) the state did not have to prove that defendant knew he was within 1,000 feet of school property; (2) section 35-38-4-10(b)(2)(B) was not ambiguous because the definition of school property under § 35-41-1-24.7 was not vague; (3) the surveyor's "line of sight" technique to determine the 1,000-foot perimeter around the school property was sufficient to show that the delivery occurred within 1,000 feet of school property; and (4) the increase in the penalty for delivering marijuana within 1,000 feet of school property did not violate due process because there was no racially discriminatory impact, coupled with an intent or purpose to discriminate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant for dealing in marijuana within 1,000 feet of school property, adjudicating defendant an habitual offender, and imposing an enhancement in defendant's sentencing.

 

999 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Price v. State


No. 49A02-9109-CR-378


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


600 N.E.2d 103; 1992 Ind. App. LEXIS 1434



September 14, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition to Transfer Granted November 1, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Ind. LEXIS 183. Rehearing Denied June 18, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MARION MUNICIPAL COURT. The Honorable William S. Mercuri, Judge. Cause No. 49F04-9101-CM-199. Cause No. 49FA04-9101-CM-199



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of her conviction for disorderly conduct and public intoxication by the Marion Municipal Court (Indiana).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of disorderly conduct in violation of Ind. Code § 35-45-1-3(2) and public intoxication in violation of Ind. Code § 7.1-5-1-3. Defendant challenged the constitutionality of the disorderly conduct statute under the Ind. Const. art I, § 9, and under the U.S. Const. amend. I and amend. XIV. The court affirmed defendant's conviction, holding that the statute was neither overbroad nor void for vagueness, and the "unreasonable noise" provision of § 35-45-1-3(2) was constitutional with respect to fighting words, speech inciting imminent lawless action, and public nuisance speech. The court noted that when the utterance was alleged to be fighting words, the circumstances had to present additional indicia of serious provocation likely to incite even a police officer to an immediate and violent reaction and the "unreasonable noise" language of the statute did not vest the police with unwarranted discretion to suppress protected speech. The court also held that, for purposes of § 7.1-5-1-3, a street was a public place and a non-expert could offer an opinion as to the defendant's intoxication.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the defendant's conviction for disorderly conduct and public intoxication.

 

1000 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Portage v. Harrington


No. 64A03-9109-CV-285


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


598 N.E.2d 634; 1992 Ind. App. LEXIS 1391



September 10, 1992, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE PORTER SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Raymond Kickbush, Judge. Cause No. 64C01-9005-CP-77



DISPOSITION: For the foregoing reasons, the decision of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, city and port authority, appealed a judgment from the Porter Superior Court (Indiana), which declared its ordinance requiring plaintiffs, marine owners and other boaters, to pay an annual license fee of $ 75 per dock slip to be unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Marina owners and other boaters filed an action seeking declaratory and injunctive relief. Their complaint alleged that the $ 75.00 annual license fee imposed by the city's ordinance for use of a dock and waterway was contrary to Ind. Code § 36-1-3-8. The trial court agreed and entered judgment in their favor, declaring the ordinance void, after finding that the ordinance was unrelated to the costs of regulation and therefore, was an impermissible revenue tax. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that while the city had the authority under § 36-1-3-4(b) to authorize a license fee for the use of the waterway, the fee imposed upon the boaters and other users was not reasonably related to the administrative costs of exercising its regulatory power. The court further held that trial court's special findings of fact entered under Ind. R. Trial P. 52(A), specifically, that the monies collected through the enforcement of the ordinance would not be limited to the probable expense of issuing licenses and inspecting and regulating boating activity, had support in the record and were not clearly erroneous.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which had declared the city's ordinance void and held that the license fee that was not reasonably related to the administrative costs of exercising the city's regulatory power.
